Divine Power Attaches to Non-Existent as to Existent
Sanusi's chosen position on divine power and non-existent things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's chosen position that divine power (qudra) attaches to non-existent things (ma'dum) just as it attaches to existent things (mawjud), and how this aligns with al-Baqillani's doctrine against al-Juwayni.

Core Idea
Divine power reaches both existent and non-existent alike.

In this passage, the author reports Sanusi's decisive choice on a key question about the scope of divine power. Understanding this choice helps clarify the Ash'ari position on whether God's power relates to things before they exist. Let's examine the text to see Sanusi's view and his support for it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the key terms: قدرة (power), معدوم (non-existent), موجود (existent).
The passage is short but dense with theological significance.
2
Identify the three scholars mentioned
The passage names al-Baqillani (the authority Sanusi follows), Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni, the opponent), and Sanusi himself. Understand their roles.
Sanusi chooses between two earlier authorities.
3
Understand the disagreement
Al-Baqillani held that divine power attaches to non-existent things as it does to existent. Al-Juwayni disagreed. Sanusi sided with al-Baqillani and supported it with proof.
This disagreement reflects different philosophical assumptions about the nature of possibility and divine attributes.
4
Reflect on the outcome
The author notes that Sanusi's statement became so well-known that later books transmit it specifically from him. This shows the influence of his choice.
Sanusi's ikhtiyār shaped subsequent Ash'ari theology on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اختياره الجاد لكون القدرة تتعلق بالمعدوم كتعلقها بالموجود ، وهو مذهب القاضي الباقلاني، خلافاً لإمام الحرمين ، داعماً قوله بالحجة ، حتى صار قوله هنا ممَّا تتناقله عنه الكتب من بعده ، وتحيل عليه في كتابه هذا دون غيره
His serious choice that power (القدرة) attaches to the non-existent (المعدوم) just as it attaches to the existent (الموجود), and this is the doctrine of Qadi al-Baqillani, contrary to Imam al-Haramayn [al-Juwayni], supporting his statement with proof, until his statement here became among what books transmit from him afterwards, and they refer to it in this book of his and not others.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage presents Sanusi's decisive choice (ikhtiyār) on a key theological question: whether divine power (qudra) attaches to non-existent things (ma‘dūm) just as it attaches to existent things (mawjūd). Sanusi adopted the position of Qadi al-Baqillani, who affirmed that power can be related to non-existent objects, contrary to Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni who held otherwise. Sanusi supported his view with rational proof (ḥujja). The author notes that this particular position became so characteristic of Sanusi that later books transmit it from him and refer to it specifically in this work.

Key Terms
قدرة
معدوم
موجود
قاضي الباقلاني
إمام الحرمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that divine power only attaches to things that exist, not to things that do not yet exist.
Correction: Sanusi, following al-Baqillani, affirms that divine power attaches to both existent and non-existent, meaning God's power encompasses all possible things, whether they currently exist or not.

Checkpoint
Who did Sanusi disagree with on the issue of divine power attaching to non-existent?
A) Al-Baqillani.
B) Al-Juwayni.
C) Al-Ash'ari.
D) Al-Ghazali.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's choice that divine power attaches to non-existent as to existent, following al-Baqillani, became a defining feature of his theology and was widely transmitted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a situation in your life that seems utterly hopeless—something that feels 'non-existent' in terms of possibility. How does the truth that God's power attaches to the non-existent change the way you will pray about it today?
?
Sanusi chose this position and defended it with proof, making it a hallmark of his theology. What core belief about God are you willing to study deeply and defend, even if it sets you apart from others?
?
If you truly believe that God's power is not limited by the present state of things, what comfort does that give you for a difficult relationship or a past mistake that seems impossible to fix?

Divine Power and the Nonexistent
Commentary notes Sanusi's adoption of al-Baqillani's view on power and nonexistent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's specific choice regarding the relation of divine power to the nonexistent and how it aligns with al-Baqillani against al-Juwayni.

Core Idea
Divine power relates equally to the existent and the nonexistent.

In studying divine attributes, one key issue is whether God's power attaches only to existing things or also to nonexistent ones. The commentator notes that Sanusi took a firm stance on this, siding with al-Baqillani over Imam al-Haramayn. This passage highlights a significant doctrinal choice that later scholars relied upon.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the specific terminology for power (qudra), nonexistent (ma'dum), and existent (mawjud).
2
Identify the two scholars
Identify al-Qadi al-Baqillani and Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni). Understand that they held opposing views on this issue.
Al-Baqillani held that power attaches to both existent and nonexistent; al-Juwayni disagreed.
3
Understand Sanusi's choice
Sanusi deliberately selected al-Baqillani's view and supported it with evidence. Note that his statement became widely quoted in later books.
4
Reflect on significance
Consider why this choice matters for theology: it affirms that God's power is not limited to what exists, but encompasses all possibilities.
This relates to God's ability to create and annihilate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- اختياره الجاد لكون القدرة تتعلق بالمعدوم كتعلقها بالموجود، وهو مذهب القاضي الباقلاني، خلافاً لإمام الحرمين، داعماً قوله بالحجة، حتى صار قوله هنا ممَّا تتناقله عنه الكتب من بعده، وتحيل عليه في كتابه هذا دون غيره.
- His serious choice that power attaches to the nonexistent just as it attaches to the existent, and that is the school of al-Qadi al-Baqillani, contrary to Imam al-Haramayn, supporting his statement with evidence, until his statement here became something that later books transmit from him, and they rely upon it in his book specifically.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a commentary note about Sanusi's doctrinal choice regarding divine power (qudra). The commentator states that Sanusi firmly selected the view that divine power relates to the nonexistent (ma'dum) as it relates to the existent (mawjud). This is the position of al-Baqillani, in opposition to Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni). Sanusi supported his view with proofs, and his statement on this matter became widely quoted in later works, which rely specifically on this book of his.

Key Terms

المعدوم
الموجود
القاضي الباقلاني
إمام الحرمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sanusi always agreed with Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) on all issues.
Correction: On this specific issue of divine power relating to the nonexistent, Sanusi sided with al-Baqillani, not al-Juwayni.

Checkpoint
Whose view did Sanusi adopt regarding the attachment of power to the nonexistent?
A) Imam al-Haramayn
B) Al-Qadi al-Baqillani
C) Ibn al-Kallab
D) Al-Qalanisi

Key Takeaway
Sanusi deliberately selected al-Baqillani's view that divine power attaches to both the existent and the nonexistent, a position that was then transmitted by later scholars from his book.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Allah's power encompasses even what does not yet exist, how does that affect your reliance on Him for your future? What is one specific future matter you will trust Him with today?
?
The fact that Allah's power is not limited to what exists means that nothing—past, present, or future—escapes His authority. Is there any area of your life where you act as if Allah's power is limited? What step will you take to acknowledge His absolute power in that area?
?
Al-Baqillani and Sanusi insisted that divine power is equal for existent and nonexistent. If you really believed that, would you worry less about things that have not happened yet? What is one fear about the future that you need to surrender to Allah's power right now?

Sanusi's Preference on Perceptual Attributes
Commentary note on Sanusi's doctrinal preference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi preferred al-Ash'ari's view that the attributes of perception relate to all existent things, not only to their specific objects.

Core Idea
Sanusi chose Ash'ari's broader view on the reach of God's perceptual attributes.

This passage records a key doctrinal choice by Sanusi: he sided with al-Ash'ari over Ibn Kullab and al-Qalanisi on the scope of God's attributes of perception. The disagreement centered on whether these attributes—like hearing and seeing—relate to all existent things or only to their direct objects. This seemingly subtle difference has implications for how we understand God's knowledge of every detail of creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic and its English translation. Notice the names: Ibn Kullab, al-Qalanisi, and al-Ash'ari. The key phrase is 'تعلق صفات الإدراك بعموم الموجودات'—the attachment of perceptual attributes to all existent things.
2
Identify the two positions
Ibn Kullab and al-Qalanisi restricted the attributes to their specific objects (e.g., hearing only to sounds). Al-Ash'ari held that they relate to all existent things in general, not only to what is derived from them.
3
Understand why Sanusi preferred Ash'ari
Reflect on why Sanusi might favor Ash'ari's view. Consider how this aligns with the Ash'ari emphasis on God's comprehensive knowledge and power over all things.
The passage doesn't give reasons, but later lessons may explore the theological implications.
4
Consider the doctrinal significance
This choice shapes how we understand God's omniscience: if the attributes relate to all existent things, then God knows everything directly, not just through derived categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- ترجيحه لمذهب الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري على ما ذهب إليه كل من ابن كلاب والقلانسي رحمهما الله في مسألة تعلق صفات الإدراك بعموم الموجودات، لا بما يشتق منها فقط.
- His preference for the school of Shaykh Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari over what each of Ibn Kullab and al-Qalanisi (may Allah have mercy on them) held regarding the issue of the attachment of the attributes of perception (sifat al-idrak) to all existent things (general 'umum al-mawjudat), not only to that which is derived from them.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a commentary note about Sanusi's doctrinal choice regarding the attributes of perception (sifat al-idrak). The commentator states that Sanusi preferred the view of al-Ash'ari over that of Ibn Kullab and al-Qalanisi. The issue is whether the attributes of perception (like hearing, seeing, knowing) relate to all existent things in general or only to those from which they are derived (e.g., hearing relates only to sounds). Al-Ash'ari held that they relate to all existent things, while the other two restricted them.

Key Terms
صفات الإدراك
ابن كلاب
القلانسي
أبو الحسن الأشعري
عموم الموجودات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which scholar's view did Sanusi prefer on the scope of the attributes of perception?
A) Ibn Kullab
B) Al-Qalanisi
C) Al-Ash'ari
D) Al-Baqillani

Key Takeaway
Sanusi affirmed that God's attributes of perception encompass all existent things, aligning with al-Ash'ari's broad view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that God's sight encompasses every atom of your being and every moment of your day, how would that change the way you live the next hour?
?
When you sin in private, do you act as if only derived perceptions (like sound or sight) matter, or do you internalize that God's perceptual attributes cover even your thoughts?
?
The lesson says Sanusi chose the broader view. But what about you—do you live as if God's knowledge is only about your actions, or do you submit to the fact that He perceives your intentions and hopes as well?

Eternal Power and Will: The Attributes of Meaning
Sanusi defines eternal power and begins defining eternal will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of God's eternal power and will as attributes of meaning, and how power operates in accordance with will.

Core Idea
God's power and will work together to bring existence and specify possibilities.

Sanusi introduces the seventh preface on the eternal attributes of meaning. He defines two essential divine attributes: eternal power, which brings all possibilities into existence or annihilates them in accordance with will, and will, which specifies which state a possible thing takes. These definitions establish the harmony of God's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the definition of will is cut off – this passage continues into the next page.
2
Distinguish the two attributes
Identify the definitions of eternal power and will. Note that power is about bringing into existence and annihilating, while will is about specification.
3
Understand the relationship between power and will
The passage states that power operates 'in accordance with will'. This means God does not act arbitrarily but with intention and choice.
This harmony is crucial in Sunni theology.
4
Reflect on the incomplete definition
The definition of will is cut off at the end of the page. Consider that the full definition likely specifies that will selects among possibilities.
You may need to consult the next lesson for the complete definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ المقدمة السابعة : في صفات المعاني الأزلية ]
وَالْقُدْرَةُ الْأَزَلِيَّةُ : عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ صِفَةٍ يَتَأَنَّى بِهَا إِيجَادُ كُلِّ مُمْكِنٍ وَإِعْدَامُهُ عَلَى وَفْقِ الْإِرَادَةِ .
وَالإِرَادَةُ : صِفَةٌ يَتَأَنَّى بِهَا تَخْصِيصُ الْمُمْكِن بِبَعْضِ مَا يَجُوزُ عَلَيْهِ
[The Seventh Preface: On the Eternal Attributes of Meanings] And eternal power: it is an expression for an attribute by which the bringing into existence of every possible and its annihilating is feasible in accordance with will. And will: an attribute by which the specification of the possible to some of what is possible for it is feasible
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage begins a preface on the eternal 'attributes of meanings' (صفات المعاني), which are real, positive attributes of God distinct from His essence. The author defines two:

1. Eternal power (القدرة الأزلية) is the attribute through which God can bring every possible into existence and annihilate it, but always in accordance with His will. This shows that power is not arbitrary but aligned with divine volition.

2. Will (الإرادة) is the attribute by which God specifies a possible thing with one of the various possibilities open to it. The definition is cut off, but the idea is that will determines which particular state a possible thing takes among alternatives.

The term 'يَتَأَنَّى' is unusual; it likely means 'it is feasible' or 'it is effected'.

Key Terms
القدرة الأزلية
الإرادة
صفات المعاني
إيجاد
إعدام
تخصيص الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think power alone is sufficient for creation, without need for will.
Correction: Sanusi stresses that power operates 'in accordance with will', affirming that God's actions are intentional and not arbitrary.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does the attribute of eternal power (القدرة الأزلية) enable?
A) Specifying a possible with a particular quality.
B) Bringing every possible into existence and annihilating it, in accordance with will.
C) Knowing all things.
D) Speaking to prophets.

Key Takeaway
God's eternal power and will are distinct attributes that cooperate to create and specify possibilities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Since God's power only brings about what His will specifies, what area of your life are you most afraid is outside His control? How does this truth challenge you to surrender that fear?
?
God's will specifies every detail of every possibility. When you face a difficult decision, do you truly believe that His will has already chosen the best? What is one decision you need to entrust to Him today?
?
If God's power can annihilate anything according to His will, what are you clinging to as if it were permanent? Write one worldly attachment you need to hold loosely, remembering it exists only by His will.

The Four Eternal Attributes of Meaning
Sanusi defines four of the eternal attributes: power, will, knowledge, and life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of Allah's eternal attributes of power, will, knowledge, and life as presented by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Allah's eternal attributes define how He acts, wills, knows, and lives.

In this passage, Sanusi introduces the foundational attributes that describe Allah's essence in relation to creation. These are not new terms but precise definitions that form the basis of the Ash'ari understanding of divine attributes. Let's explore each definition carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify each attribute
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Identify the four attributes (power, will, knowledge, life) and note how each is defined.
The footnote provides a variant reading for life, so pay attention.
2
Understand the function of each attribute
For each attribute, note what it accomplishes. Power brings things into existence or annihilates them. Will specifies possibilities. Knowledge discloses the known. Life enables perception.
These functions are specific and distinct.
3
Notice the footnote variant
The footnote clarifies that life is the attribute that makes perception valid, and a variant wording says 'that he is described with perception' instead of just 'perception'.
This emphasizes that life is a prerequisite for perception.
4
Reflect on why these attributes are eternal
All four are described as 'azaliyyah' (eternal). Consider why this is important in Islamic theology — they are not created or acquired.
This guards against the misconception that divine attributes are temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة السابعة : في صفاتِ المعاني الأزليَّة . وَالْقُدْرَةُ الأَزَلِيَّةُ : عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ صِفَةٍ يَتَأَنَّى بِهَا إِيجَادُ كُلِّ مُمْكِنٍ وَإِعْدَامُهُ عَلَى وَفْقِ الْإِرَادَةِ . وَالإِرَادَةُ : صِفَةٌ يَتَأَنَّى بِهَا تَخْصِيصُ الْمُمْكِن بِبَعْضِ مَا يَجُوزُ عَلَيْهِ . وَالْعِلْمُ : صِفَةٌ يَنْكَشِفُ بِهَا الْمَعْلُومُ عَلَىٰ مَا هُوَ بِهِ . وَالْحَيَاةُ : صِفَةٌ يَصِحُّ مِمَّنْ قَامَتْ بِهِ الإِدْرَاكُ . ( أ ) : ( أن يتصف بالإدراك ) بدل ( الإدراك )
The Seventh Preface: On the Eternal Attributes of Meanings. Eternal power: is an expression of an attribute by which the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation are performed in accordance with the will. And will: is an attribute by which the specification of the possible thing to some of what is permissible for it is performed. And knowledge: is an attribute by which the known is disclosed as it is. And life: is an attribute from which perception becomes valid (for the one in whom it subsists). (1): 'That he is described with perception' instead of 'perception'.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a set of definitions for four eternal attributes of Allah. The author begins with eternal power (al-qudrah al-azaliyyah), which is the attribute by which every possible thing is brought into existence or annihilated in accordance with the divine will. Then eternal will (al-iradah) is defined as the attribute by which a possible thing is specified to one of its permissible states. Then eternal knowledge (al-'ilm) is the attribute by which the known is disclosed exactly as it is. Finally, eternal life (al-hayah) is the attribute that makes perception valid for the one in whom it subsists. A footnote provides a variant reading: instead of 'perception' (al-idrak), it has 'that he is described with perception' (an yattasifa bil-idrak), which further clarifies that life is the basis for perception.

Key Terms
قدرة أزلية
إرادة
علم
حياة
إدراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these attributes are created or temporal.
Correction: They are described as 'azaliyyah' (eternal), indicating they are uncreated and everlasting attributes of Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the definition, what does eternal power (al-qudrah al-azaliyyah) accomplish?
A) It specifies possible things
B) It brings possible things into existence and annihilates them in accordance with the will
C) It discloses the known as it is
D) It makes perception valid

Key Takeaway
Allah's four eternal attributes — power, will, knowledge, and life — are defined by their specific functions in relation to possible things.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's knowledge discloses everything exactly as it is, then He knows every secret thought you have ever had. How does that reality make you feel about the words you speak and the intentions you harbor? What would it mean to live today as if every moment is fully known by Him?
?
Allah's will specifies every possible outcome in your life to exactly what occurs. Are there areas in your life where you resist His specification—where you wish things were different? Can you name one thing today that you need to surrender to His will?
?
The attribute of life is the foundation of all perception. You are alive because He gives you life. When you wake up tomorrow, what would it look like to thank Him for the gift of perception—to see, hear, feel—as a direct reflection of His attribute of life?

Eternal Hearing, Sight, Perception, and Speech
Sanusi defines hearing, sight, perception, and the eternal attribute of speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi defines the eternal attributes of hearing, sight, perception, and speech, and why speech is distinct from created expressions.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes of perception and speech are eternal and beyond physical limitations.

Sanusi continues his enumeration of the essential attributes by defining hearing, sight, and perception, then devotes a longer definition to the attribute of speech. These definitions are crucial for distinguishing between human and divine attributes, particularly for speech, which must be understood as an eternal meaning, not composed of letters or sounds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to get a sense of the definitions.
Notice the parallel structure for hearing, sight, and perception.
2
Identify the key attributes
Locate the definitions of eternal hearing, sight, and perception. Observe that perception is mentioned conditionally ('on the view accepting it').
3
Analyze the definition of speech
Carefully read the definition of eternal speech. Note the negations: it is not letters or sounds, not subject to parts, time, or change.
This distinguishes Allah's speech from human speech.
4
Reflect on the relationship to knowledge
Notice that speech pertains to the same objects as knowledge. Consider how this ties speech to divine omniscience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالسَّمْعُ الأَزَلِيُّ : صِفَةٌ يَنْكَشِفُ بِهَا كُلُّ مَوْجُودٍ عَلَى مَا هُوَ بِهِ انْكِشَافاً يُبَايِنُ سِوَاهُ ضَرُورَةٌ ، وَالْبَصَرُ مِثْلُهُ ، وَالْإِدْرَاكُ عَلَى الْقَوْلِ بِهِ مِثْلُهُمَا . وَالْكَلَامُ الأَزَلِيُّ : وَهُوَ الْمَعْنَى الْقَائِمُ بالذَّاتِ ، الْمُعَبَّر عَنْهُ بِالْعِبَارَاتِ الْمُخْتَلِفَاتِ ، الْمُبَايِنُ لِجِنْسِ الْحُرُوفِ وَالْأَصْوَاتِ ، الْمُنَزَّهُ عَن الْبَعْضِ وَالْكُلَّ ، وَالتَّقْدِيمِ وَالتَّأْخِيرِ ، وَالتَّجَدُّدِ وَالسُّكُوتِ، وَاللَّحْنِ وَالإِعْرَابِ ، وَسَائِرِ أَنْوَاعِ التَّغَيُّرَاتِ ، الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ الْعِلْمُ مِنَ الْمُتَعَلَّقَاتِ .
And eternal hearing: is an attribute by which every existent is disclosed as it is, with a disclosure that necessarily distinguishes it from other than it. And sight is like it. And perception, on the view accepting it, is like them both. And eternal speech: and it is the meaning subsisting in the essence, expressed by different expressions, distinct from the genus of letters and sounds, transcendent over part and whole, precedence and postponement, renewal and silence, solecism and inflection, and all other types of changes, pertaining to whatever knowledge pertains to of the objects of knowledge.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage defines three more eternal attributes: hearing (sam'), sight (basar), and perception (idrak) – though the author notes that perception is accepted only on some views. Each is defined as a disclosing attribute. Then the author gives a lengthy definition of eternal speech (al-kalam al-azali). This speech is a meaning (ma'na) subsisting in the essence of Allah. It is expressed through various expressions (such as the revealed scriptures) but is itself distinct from the genus of letters and sounds. It is transcendent over partition into parts, temporal sequence, renewal, silence, linguistic errors, and all changes. It relates to the same objects as knowledge. This definition emphasizes that Allah's speech is not composed of letters and sounds like human speech, but is an eternal attribute.

Key Terms
سمع أزلي
بصر
إدراك
كلام أزلي
معنى قائم بالذات
حروف
أصوات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah's speech is like human speech, composed of letters and sounds.
Correction: Sanusi states that eternal speech is distinct from the genus of letters and sounds and is transcendent over all changes, including linguistic ones.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is distinctive about eternal speech (al-kalam al-azali) in relation to letters and sounds?
A) It is composed of subtle letters
B) It is distinct from the genus of letters and sounds
C) It is expressed only through Arabic
D) It changes with time

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes of hearing, sight, and perception disclose existents, while His speech is an eternal meaning, not composed of letters or sounds, and free from all change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often refer to Allah's hearing as if it functions like your ears. After reading that His hearing is an eternal attribute that discloses every existent as it is, distinct from physical hearing, what in your life would change if you truly believed that Allah hears your every thought and secret? Are you willing to be more mindful of what you think and say?
?
The author says Allah's speech is not letters or sounds, and it is free from all change. When you recite the Quran, do you sometimes forget that it is an expression of an eternal meaning? How would your recitation be different if you meditated on the fact that you are reciting an expression of the uncreated speech of Allah?
?
Reflect on the attribute of sight: Allah sees everything as it is, without limitation. Is there a part of your life you are trying to hide from His sight? What would it mean for you to live with the awareness that Allah's sight discloses you completely?

Knowledge, Life, and Eternal Hearing
Sanusi defines al-`ilm, al-hayat, and al-sam` al-azali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of three divine attributes: knowledge (al-`ilm), life (al-hayat), and eternal hearing (al-sam` al-azali) as taught by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are real, eternal, and distinct from God's essence.

Sanusi begins by defining the attributes that are essential to God's nature. These definitions are foundational for Ash'ari theology, clarifying that each attribute is a real quality of God that is not identical to His essence. In this lesson, we explore the first three: knowledge, life, and eternal hearing.

Guided Path
1
Read the definitions carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that each definition starts with 'صِفَةٌ' (an attribute).
2
Identify the function of each attribute
For each attribute, note what it does: knowledge discloses the known, life makes perception sound, hearing discloses all existents.
3
Reflect on the distinction from essence
Ask yourself: if these attributes are not the same as God's essence, what does that imply? The commentary will help explain.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْعِلْمُ : صِفَةٌ يَنْكَشِفُ بِهَا الْمَعْلُومُ عَلَىٰ مَا هُوَ بِهِ
وَالْحَيَاةُ : صِفَةٌ يَصِحُ مِمَّنْ قَامَتْ بِهِ الْإِدْرَاكُ
وَالسَّمْعُ الْأَزَلِيُّ : صِفَةٌ يَنْكَشِفُ بِهَا كُلُّ مَوْجُودٍ عَلَىٰ مَا هُوَ بِهِ انْكِشَافاً يُبَايِنُ سِوَاهُ ضَرُورَةً
وَالْبَصَرُ مِثْلُهُ
وَالْإِدْرَاكُ عَلَى الْقَوْلِ بِهِ مِثْلُهُمَا
وَالْكَلَامُ الْأَزَلِيُّ : وَهُوَ الْمَعْنَى الْقَائِمُ بِالذَّاتِ ، الْمُعَبَّرُ عَنْهُ بِالْعِبَارَاتِ الْمُخْتَلِفَاتِ ، الْمُبَايِنُ لِجِنْسِ الْحُرُوفِ وَالْأَصْوَاتِ ، الْمُنَزَّهُ عَنِ الْبَعْضِ وَالْكُلِّ ، وَالتَّقْدِيمِ وَالتَّأْخِيرِ ، وَالتَّجَدُّدِ وَالسُّكُوتِ ، وَاللَّحْنِ وَالْإِعْرَابِ ، وَسَائِرِ أَنْوَاعِ التَّغَيُّرَاتِ ، الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ الْعِلْمُ مِنَ الْمُتَعَلَّقَاتِ
Al-`ilm (knowledge): an attribute by which the known is disclosed as it is. Al-hayat (life): an attribute by which perception is sound from the one who possesses it. Al-sam` al-azali (eternal hearing): an attribute by which every existent is disclosed as it is, a disclosure necessarily distinct from others. Al-basar (sight) is similar to it. Al-idrak (perception), on the view that it is additional, is similar to both. Al-kalam al-azali (eternal speech): it is the meaning subsisting in the Essence, expressed by different expressions, distinct from the genus of letters and sounds, transcendent of part and whole, priority and posteriority, renewal and silence, solecism and inflection, and all kinds of changes, and pertains to whatever the knowledge relates from the things related.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage provides definitions of six divine attributes as held by the Ash'ari school. Each definition emphasizes that the attribute is an eternal, real quality of God distinct from His essence. (1) Al-`ilm: an attribute of knowledge that reveals the known as it is. (2) Al-hayat: life, a condition that makes the possessor capable of perception. (3) Al-sam`: eternal hearing, which discloses all existents in a way necessarily distinct from other modes of disclosure. (4) Al-basar: sight, similar to hearing. (5) Al-idrak: perception, mentioned only for those who hold it is an additional attribute beyond hearing and sight. (6) Al-kalam: eternal speech, defined as a meaning residing in God's essence, not composed of letters or sounds, free from temporal changes, and related to all that knowledge relates.

Key Terms
العلم
الحياة
السمع الأزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition, what does the attribute of life (al-hayat) make possible?
A) The disclosure of the known
B) The soundness of perception
C) The disclosure of every existent
D) The expression of speech

Key Takeaway
Knowledge, life, and eternal hearing are real, eternal attributes of God, each with a distinct function in disclosing or enabling perception.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you realize that Allah's knowledge discloses everything about you exactly as it is—including your hidden motives—what thought or action today needs to be brought into alignment with that reality? What concrete step will you take right now to address it?
?
If life is the attribute that enables perception, in what area of your spiritual life have you become 'dead'—no longer perceiving Allah's signs or feeling His presence? What is one small habit you can start today to revive that perception?
?
Eternal hearing means Allah hears every existent being, including your silent cries and whispered doubts. Do you truly live as if you are heard by the One who knows every detail? Or do you act as if you are alone? What will you say to Him in sincere prayer right now, trusting that He hears?

Sight, Perception, and Eternal Speech
Sanusi defines al-basar, al-idrak (on a view), and al-kalam al-azali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of sight (al-basar), perception (al-idrak) on the view that it is additional, and eternal speech (al-kalam al-azali), including the detailed negations that distinguish divine speech from human speech.

Core Idea
Eternal speech is a meaning in God's essence, not composed of letters or sounds.

Having defined knowledge, life, and hearing, Sanusi now turns to sight, perception, and a more extended definition of eternal speech. The definition of speech is particularly detailed because it guards against the common anthropomorphic misconception that God's speech is like human speech. This lesson unpacks that definition and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Examine the first two definitions
Note that sight is defined as 'similar to' hearing, and perception is also similar (for those who hold it is an additional attribute).
This shows a pattern: many attributes are analogous in function.
2
Focus on the definition of eternal speech
Read the long definition carefully. Identify the core claim: speech is a meaning subsisting in the essence. Then list all the things it is distinct from (letters, sounds, part/whole, etc.).
The negations are deliberately exhaustive to remove any temporal or physical aspect.
3
Understand the relationship with knowledge
The definition ends by saying speech pertains to all that knowledge relates. This shows that divine speech covers the same objects as divine knowledge.

Allah's Direct Creation and Absolute Sovereignty
Sanusi affirms Allah's direct creation and absolute sovereignty with no intermediaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah is the direct creator of all actions and accidents, with no intermediaries or partners, and that all benefit and harm are by His pure grace without any entitlement.

Core Idea
Allah alone creates and controls everything; no one shares His authority.

This passage establishes the fundamental Islamic belief in Allah's absolute sovereignty and direct involvement in all that occurs. Sanusi begins by affirming that Allah is the direct creator of everything, including accidents, and that He has no associates or intermediaries. He then emphasizes that no creature can bring benefit or ward off harm except by Allah's pure favor, underscoring that nothing is owed to anyone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong negations: 'لا معين ولا وزير...'
2
Identify key affirmations
Identify the key affirmations: Allah is the direct agent, no intermediaries, nothing hidden, no one can benefit except by Allah's grace.
3
Consider the implications
Reflect on what it means that Allah has no purpose, necessity, or entitlement in bestowing grace. This highlights His absolute freedom and generosity.
This connects to the core idea.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you have grasped the main point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العام اللازمِ إلى المولى العظيمِ جلَّ وعلا ، وهو سبحانه المباشر لجميعها بالخلْقِ والإمداد بالأعراض ، ويخص ما شاءَ منها بما شاءَ مِنْ شرفٍ أو ضدّهِ ، وليسَ لهُ منها معين ولا وزير ولا وكيل ولا واسطة أصلاً ، وليس شيء منها يغيب عن علمه وتدبيره وسمعه وبصره ، ولا يقدر أحد منها أنْ يُقرِّبَ نفسَهُ - فكيفَ بغيرِه ؟! ـ إلى نعمة ، أو يبعدها عن نقمةٍ ؛ إلا أنْ يتفضَّل المولى العظيم بذلكَ على مَنْ يَشَاءُ بمحضِ الفضلِ والكرمِ ، مِنْ غيرِ غرضِ ولا وجوب ولا استحقاق . وعبادته جل وعلا وخدمته ومعصيتُهُ تبارك وتعالى إنَّما هي أفعال مِنْ أفعاله المخترعة له في ذواتِ عبيده ، ليس له حاجةٌ في طاعتِها ولا غرض ، ولا ينالُ مِنْ إيجادها كمالاً كما لا ينالُ مِنْ خلقِهِ لأضدادها نقصاً ، ثم رتَّبَ سبحانَهُ عليها ما شاءَ مِنْ ثواب وعقاب فضلاً وعدلاً ، لا لقضاء حقٌّ في الثوابِ ، ولا لإشفاء غيظ في العقاب .
The necessary universal extends to the Mighty Lord, Glorified and Exalted is He, and He, Exalted is He, is the direct agent of all of them by creation and supply of accidents, and He distinguishes what He wills from them with whatever He wills of honor or its opposite, and there is for Him from them no helper, no vizier, no deputy, and no intermediary at all, and nothing from them is hidden from His knowledge, His planning, His hearing, and His sight, and no one from them is able to bring himself - how then another? - to a blessing, or to distance himself from a punishment, unless the Mighty Lord bestows that upon whom He wills by pure grace and generosity, without any purpose, necessity, or entitlement. And His worship, Glorified and Exalted is He, and His service and disobedience to Him, Blessed and Exalted is He, are only actions from among His actions created by Him in the essences of His servants; He has no need in their obedience and no purpose, nor does He attain from their existence perfection, just as He does not attain from His creation of their opposites deficiency. Then He, Exalted is He, ordained upon them what He wills of reward and punishment as grace and justice, not to fulfill a right in reward, nor to satisfy anger in punishment.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a theological exposition about Allah's absolute sovereignty and direct involvement in all acts. It begins by stating that Allah is the direct creator and supplier of all things, specifically mentioning accidents (al-a'rad). He distinguishes some things with honor or its opposite. He has no partners or intermediaries. Nothing escapes His knowledge, planning, hearing, and sight. No one can benefit themselves or avoid punishment except by Allah's pure grace and generosity, without any ulterior purpose, necessity, or entitlement. Then it discusses worship, service, and disobedience: these are actions created by Allah in the essences of His servants. Allah has no need or purpose in their obedience, nor does He gain perfection from it or suffer deficiency from its opposite. Finally, He ordains reward and punishment upon these actions as grace and justice, not due to any right in reward or to satisfy anger in punishment. This underscores that reward is purely by divine favor and punishment by divine justice, not by any merit or revenge.

Key Terms
مباشر
أعراض
وساطة
فضل
كرم
استحقاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that angels or saints can independently bring benefit or harm, or that humans can earn reward by their own actions.
Correction: This passage clarifies that no one can bring benefit or ward off harm except by Allah's pure grace, and that He does so without any necessity or entitlement. All power belongs to Allah alone.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does it mean that Allah is the 'direct agent' (المباشر) of all things?
A) He creates through intermediaries.
B) He creates directly without any helper, vizier, deputy, or intermediary.
C) He only creates the major things.
D) He creates only good things.

Key Takeaway
Allah alone creates everything directly, and no one can benefit or harm except by His pure grace, which He gives without any need or obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that no one—not even yourself—can bring you a blessing or remove a punishment unless Allah wills it? Then why do you sometimes feel anxious about what others can do to you, as if they have independent power?
?
If Allah has no helpers or intermediaries, why do you sometimes act as if you need to please people to get what you want from Allah? Search your heart: is there a person or thing you rely on as a 'middleman' between you and Allah's provision?
?
This passage says Allah bestows by pure grace without any entitlement whatsoever. Does your heart accept that you deserve nothing from Allah, or do you secretly feel entitled to His blessings because of your good deeds, your lineage, or your sacrifices? What would change in your worship if you truly internalized that every single blessing is a pure gift?

Human Actions and the Basis of Reward and Punishment
Sanusi explains that human actions are created by Allah and that reward/punishment are acts of grace and justice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that human actions (whether obedient or disobedient) are created by Allah, that Allah has no need of them nor does He gain or lose from them, and that reward and punishment are bestowed purely as grace and justice, not as a right or revenge.

Core Idea
Our actions are Allah's creation; He rewards and punishes by grace and justice, not because we deserve it.

Having established Allah's direct control over all creation, Sanusi now addresses the nature of human actions – worship, service, and disobedience. He explains that these are actions created by Allah in His servants, and that Allah has no need or purpose in them. Then he clarifies the basis of reward and punishment: they are given as grace and justice, not to fulfill a right or satisfy anger. This lesson helps us understand the proper relationship between divine sovereignty and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'وعبادته جل وعلا' to the end. Notice the shift from discussing creation in general to specifically human actions.
2
Identify the key points about actions
Identify that actions are created by Allah, that Allah has no need of them, and that He does not gain or lose from them.
This refutes any notion that Allah benefits from our worship.
3
Understand reward and punishment
Note that reward and punishment are described as grace and justice, not as a right or vengeance. This is the core of the lesson.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about how this shapes our understanding of divine justice and mercy. Reward is a gift, punishment is just, not vindictive.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العام اللازمِ إلى المولى العظيمِ جلَّ وعلا ، وهو سبحانه المباشر لجميعها بالخلْقِ والإمداد بالأعراض ، ويخص ما شاءَ منها بما شاءَ مِنْ شرفٍ أو ضدّهِ ، وليسَ لهُ منها معين ولا وزير ولا وكيل ولا واسطة أصلاً ، وليس شيء منها يغيب عن علمه وتدبيره وسمعه وبصره ، ولا يقدر أحد منها أنْ يُقرِّبَ نفسَهُ - فكيفَ بغيرِه ؟! ـ إلى نعمة ، أو يبعدها عن نقمةٍ ؛ إلا أنْ يتفضَّل المولى العظيم بذلكَ على مَنْ يَشَاءُ بمحضِ الفضلِ والكرمِ ، مِنْ غيرِ غرضِ ولا وجوب ولا استحقاق . وعبادته جل وعلا وخدمته ومعصيتُهُ تبارك وتعالى إنَّما هي أفعال مِنْ أفعاله المخترعة له في ذواتِ عبيده ، ليس له حاجةٌ في طاعتِها ولا غرض ، ولا ينالُ مِنْ إيجادها كمالاً كما لا ينالُ مِنْ خلقِهِ لأضدادها نقصاً ، ثم رتَّبَ سبحانَهُ عليها ما شاءَ مِنْ ثواب وعقاب فضلاً وعدلاً ، لا لقضاء حقٌّ في الثوابِ ، ولا لإشفاء غيظ في العقاب .
The necessary universal extends to the Mighty Lord, Glorified and Exalted is He, and He, Exalted is He, is the direct agent of all of them by creation and supply of accidents, and He distinguishes what He wills from them with whatever He wills of honor or its opposite, and there is for Him from them no helper, no vizier, no deputy, and no intermediary at all, and nothing from them is hidden from His knowledge, His planning, His hearing, and His sight, and no one from them is able to bring himself - how then another? - to a blessing, or to distance himself from a punishment, unless the Mighty Lord bestows that upon whom He wills by pure grace and generosity, without any purpose, necessity, or entitlement. And His worship, Glorified and Exalted is He, and His service and disobedience to Him, Blessed and Exalted is He, are only actions from among His actions created by Him in the essences of His servants; He has no need in their obedience and no purpose, nor does He attain from their existence perfection, just as He does not attain from His creation of their opposites deficiency. Then He, Exalted is He, ordained upon them what He wills of reward and punishment as grace and justice, not to fulfill a right in reward, nor to satisfy anger in punishment.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a theological exposition about Allah's absolute sovereignty and direct involvement in all acts. It begins by stating that Allah is the direct creator and supplier of all things, specifically mentioning accidents (al-a'rad). He distinguishes some things with honor or its opposite. He has no partners or intermediaries. Nothing escapes His knowledge, planning, hearing, and sight. No one can benefit themselves or avoid punishment except by Allah's pure grace and generosity, without any ulterior purpose, necessity, or entitlement. Then it discusses worship, service, and disobedience: these are actions created by Allah in the essences of His servants. Allah has no need or purpose in their obedience, nor does He gain perfection from it or suffer deficiency from its opposite. Finally, He ordains reward and punishment upon these actions as grace and justice, not due to any right in reward or to satisfy anger in punishment. This underscores that reward is purely by divine favor and punishment by divine justice, not by any merit or revenge.

Correction: The passage clarifies that Allah has no need of worship and does not gain or lose from actions. Reward and punishment are by grace and justice, not to satisfy anger or fulfill a right.

Key Takeaway
Human actions are created by Allah, and He rewards or punishes purely out of grace and justice, without any need or emotion.

The Invalidity of Essential Causation
Sanusi proves that the doctrine of essential causation necessarily leads to kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the belief in essential causation (al-ījāb al-dhātī) is considered kufr according to Sanusi.

Core Idea
Believing God creates by necessity, not will, leads to denying His power and the Quran.

Sanusi begins his refutation of false doctrines about divine causality. He singles out the view that God's essence necessarily produces the world, like a cause forces its effect. This passage shows that such a belief inevitably leads to the denial of core Islamic tenets, making it a clear case of unbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of essential causation
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice how Sanusi defines al-ījāb al-dhātī as the belief that God's essence creates by necessity, not by choice.
The term 'essential causation' (الإيجاب الذاتي) is contrasted with creation by will.
2
Identify the three necessary consequences
Sanusi lists three things that necessarily follow from this belief. Find them in the text and write them down.
Each consequence starts with 'ومن لازمه'.
3
Reflect on why each consequence is incompatible with Islamic scripture
Consider how each consequence contradicts verses from the Quran, such as those emphasizing God's will and power.
Sanusi quotes Quran 28:68 and 5:64 as examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[بطلان القول بالإيجاب الذاتي]
أمَّا الأمرُ الأَوَّلُ ؛ وهو الإيجاب الذاتي (۱) ؛ أي : اعتقادُ أنَّ الذاتَ العلية سبب في وجودِ الممكناتِ لا بالاختيار ، بل بطريق العلَّةِ والطبيعة : فلا إشكال في كفرِ مَنْ يعتقدُ هذا ؛ لأنَّ مِنْ لازم المذهبِ إنكار القدرةِ والإرادةِ الأزليتينِ ، ومِنْ لازمه قدم العالم ومِنْ لازمِهِ تكذيب القرآنِ في قولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَختار [القصص : ٦٨] ، وقوله عزّ وجلَّ : بَلْ يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ يُنفِقُ كَيْفَ (۱) يَشَاءُ [المائدة : ٦٤] ، ونحو ذلك مما هو كثير في الكتاب والسنَّةِ
(۱) قال المصنف في ( شرح العقيدة الصغرى » ( ص ۲۸۹ ) : ( وهو أصل كفر الفلاسفة ) ، وكذا أصل كفر الطبائعيين
[Invalidity of the doctrine of essential causation]
As for the first matter; it is essential causation (1); i.e., the belief that the exalted essence is a cause for the existence of contingent things not by choice, but by way of cause and nature: there is no doubt about the kufr of whoever believes this; because from the doctrine necessarily follow the denial of eternal power and will, and from it necessarily follows the eternity of the world, and from it necessarily follows the denial of the Qur'an in His saying, exalted: 'And your Lord creates whatever He wills and chooses' [28:68], and His saying, mighty and majestic: 'But His two hands are outstretched, He spends how He wills' [5:64], and similar to that which is abundant in the Book and the Sunnah.
(1) The author said in Sharḥ al-ʿAqīda al-Ṣughrā (p. 289): 'It is the root of the kufr of the philosophers,' and likewise the root of the kufr of the naturalists.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the invalidity of the doctrine of al-ījāb al-dhātī (essential causation). The author begins by identifying it as the first matter in a larger discussion. He defines it as the belief that the divine essence (al-dhāt al-ʿaliyya) is a cause for the existence of contingent things, not by choice but by way of causal necessitation. He then states that there is no doubt about the kufr of whoever holds this belief, because from this doctrine necessarily follow the denial of eternal power and will, the eternity of the world, and the denial of numerous Quranic verses such as 'Your Lord creates whatever He wills and chooses' (28:68) and 'His two hands are spread out, He spends how He wills' (5:64), among many others in the Book and Sunnah. The footnote adds that this is the root of the kufr of the philosophers and the naturalists.

Key Terms
الإيجاب الذاتي
علة
طبيعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that God’s creation is necessitated by His essence without any will or choice, similar to how fire necessarily burns.
Correction: Sanusi proves that this belief leads to kufr because it denies God’s eternal power and will, the temporal creation of the world, and the clear Quranic verses affirming that God creates what He wills and chooses.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, which of the following necessarily follows from the belief in essential causation?
A) Affirmation of God's power and will.
B) Denial of eternal power and will.
C) Creation of the world in time.
D) Affirmation of resurrection.

Key Takeaway
Essential causation is kufr because it contradicts God's will, power, and the Qur'an.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

This lesson says essential causation leads to kufr. Have you ever entertained the idea that God had to create the world? If so, what does that imply about your belief in His will, and how can you repent from that?

Read the verse 'Your Lord creates whatever He wills and chooses.' Does your heart truly submit to the absolute freedom of God's will, or do you unconsciously place restrictions on it? What concrete step can you take today to deepen your trust in His sovereignty?

The Disbelief of the Believer in Nature
Sanusi declares the kufr of the one who believes in nature and lists its necessary implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in nature necessarily entails disbelief and what its necessary implications are.

Core Idea
Belief in nature leads to denial of Allah's eternal power and will, which is kufr.

Sanusi makes a bold declaration that belief in nature is not a harmless philosophical view but a direct contradiction to Islamic creed. He lays out the necessary implications that follow from this belief. Let us examine his arguments and see why all orthodox scholars unanimously reject this doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to grasp Sanusi's harsh ruling.
2
Identify the three necessary implications
Look for the three 'لازم' statements and note them.
3
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
Consider how the quoted verses refute the doctrine of nature.
Verses are from Qasas 68 and Ma'idah 64.
4
Understand the accusation of deception
Sanusi says proponents equivocate; why would they do that?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا والطبيعة : فلا إشكال في كفرِ مَنْ يعتقدُ هذا ؛ لأنَّ مِنْ لازم المذهبِ إنكار القدرةِ والإرادةِ الأزليتينِ ، ومِنْ لازمه قدم العالم ومِنْ لازمِهِ تكذيب القرآنِ في قولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ وَرَبُّكَ يَخْلُقُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيَختار ﴾ [القصص : ٦٨] ، وقوله عزّ وجلَّ : ﴿ بَلْ يَدَاهُ مَبْسُوطَتَانِ يُنفِقُ كَيْفَ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [المائدة : ٦٤] ، ونحو ذلك مما هو كثير في الكتاب والسنَّةِ (١) وهذه اللوازم في اللوازم البينة ، ولذا جعلت مذهباً للقائل بملزومها ، علماً أن هذه اللوازم لا ينكرها القائلون بالتعليل والطبع ، وإنما يجمجمون تلبيساً وتدليساً على من لا خبرة له بكلامهم .
This, and nature: there is no doubt about the disbelief of one who believes this; because from the necessary implications of the doctrine is denial of eternal power and will, and from its necessary implications is the pre-eternity of the world, and from its necessary implications is the denial of the Qur'an in His saying, may He be exalted: 'And your Lord creates what He wills and chooses' [Qasas: 68], and His saying, may He be mighty and majestic: 'Nay, both His hands are outstretched; He spends how He wills' [Ma'idah: 64], and similar to that which is abundant in the Book and the Sunnah. (1) And these necessary implications are among clear necessary implications, and therefore it is considered a doctrine for the one who holds its necessary consequence, knowing that those who hold causation and nature do not deny these necessary implications, but they equivocate and deceive those who have no experience with their speech.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage condemns the doctrine of nature (الطبيعة), stating unequivocally that whoever believes it is a disbeliever. The author lists three necessary implications (لوازم) of this belief: (1) denial of God's eternal power and will, (2) pre-eternity of the world, and (3) contradiction of explicit Quranic verses about God's free choice and action. These implications are obvious (بينة), so the doctrine is clearly opposed to Islam. The author notes that proponents of cause (تعليل) and nature (طبع) do not openly deny these implications but engage in deception and equivocation to hide the consequences of their view.

Correction: Sanusi shows it necessarily entails kufr by leading to denial of Allah's attributes, pre-eternity of the world, and contradiction of the Qur'an.

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
Divine Attributes Must Subsist in God and Are Uncreated
Sanusi proves that divine attributes subsist in God's essence and need no creator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that divine attributes must subsist in God's essence and cannot be created or exist independently.

Core Idea
An attribute cannot exist without a subject; divine attributes are inseparable from God.

Sanusi now turns to a crucial point: the divine attributes are not created entities that could exist on their own. They are real qualities that subsist in God's essence. In this passage, he provides a logical proof and then defends it against an objection that might seem plausible. Understanding this argument is key to grasping the Islamic position on God's attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how Sanusi structures his argument: a claim, a proof, an objection, and a response.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage begins by stating the doctrine: the attributes of the Eternal must subsist in His essence and are free from needing a creator.
3
Follow the proof
Understand why self-subsistence is impossible: it would invert the reality of an attribute, which by definition requires a subject. If it stood alone, it would cease to be an attribute.
This uses the principle of 'inversion of realities' (قلب الحقائق).
4
Understand the objection and answer
The objection suggests an attribute could be 'of' a subject without inhering in it. Sanusi answers that this would lead to 'preference without a preferrer'—no reason for the attribute to belong to that specific subject.
The answer ties subsistence to the very meaning of being an attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيام صفاتِ القديمِ بذاتِهِ العليَّةِ واستغناؤُها عنِ المخصص ] وأما ما ذكرناه في القسم الرابع - وهو صفات مولانا جل وعلا - مِنْ وجوب قيامها بذاتِهِ العليَّةِ ، ووجوبِ غَنائها عنِ المخصص : فلأنَّ كونَها صفاتٍ يُوجِبُ استحالة قيامها بأنفسها ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنْ قلبِ الحقائق ، إذ حقيقة الصفة تستلزم موصوفاً يتصف بها ، فلو قامَتْ بنفسها لم تكن صفةً ، لكن مفارقةُ الصفة لحقيقتها التي هي كونها صفةً لموصوف .. محال ، فقيامُها إذاً بنفسها الذي استلزم مفارقتها لحقيقة نفسها .. محال . فإن قلتَ : قُصارى ما أنتج دليلكم أنَّ الصفةَ لا تُعقَلُ حقيقتها بدون موصوف بها ، ولا يلزمُ مِن استلزامها موصوفاً بها أن تقوم بذلكَ الموصوف ؛ لاحتمال أن تكون صفة لموصوف ولا تقوم به فالجواب : أَنَّهُ لا معنى لكونها صفةً لموصوف إلا قيامها بهِ ؛ إِذْ لو لم تقم به لم يمكن أن تكون صفة له دون غيره ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنَ الترجيح بلا مُرجح ، فلو لم تقم إذاً بموصوفها لم تكن صفةً له ولا لغيره ؛ لعدم مُوجِب الاختصاص، فقد لزم إذاً مِنْ قيامها بنفسها وجود الصفةِ بلا موصوف ، وذلك إبطال لحقيقتِها .
[The subsistence of the attributes of the Eternal in His sublime essence and their independence from a creator.] As for what we mentioned in the fourth section – which is the attributes of our Lord, Mighty and Sublime – regarding the necessity of their subsistence in His sublime essence and the necessity of their independence from a creator: it is because their being attributes necessitates the impossibility of their subsistence by themselves, due to what follows from that of the inversion of realities (قلب الحقائق). For the reality of an attribute entails a subject qualified by it; so if it subsisted by itself, it would not be an attribute. But the separation of an attribute from its reality – which is its being an attribute of a subject – is impossible. So its subsistence by itself, which necessitates its separation from its own reality, is impossible. If you say: The most that your proof yields is that the reality of an attribute is not conceivable without a subject, but it does not necessarily follow from its entailing a subject that it must subsist in that subject; because it is possible that it be an attribute of a subject without subsisting in it. The answer: There is no meaning to its being an attribute of a subject except its subsistence in it; for if it did not subsist in it, it could not be an attribute of it to the exclusion of another, due to what would follow of preference without a preferrer. So if it did not subsist in its subject, it would not be an attribute of it nor of anything else, for lack of a cause of specification. Thus it follows from its subsistence by itself that there exists an attribute without a subject, and that is an invalidation of its reality.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a proof and defense of two doctrines: (1) the divine attributes must subsist in God's essence, and (2) they are uncreated (do not need a creator like contingent things). The author states that because they are attributes, they cannot subsist by themselves; that would invert the nature of an attribute (قلب الحقائق). The objection attempts to separate the conceptual entailment from actual subsistence: an attribute might be predicated of a subject without inhering in it. The answer is that 'attribute of X' means precisely 'subsisting in X'; otherwise, there would be no reason for it to be attached to this subject rather than another (preference without a preferrer). Without subsistence, it would be an attribute of nothing, destroying its very nature. This argument is crucial to uphold the real distinction between God and His attributes while avoiding anthropomorphism.

Key Terms
صفات القديم (attributes of the Eternal)
مخصص (creator/particularizer)
قيام بالذات (subsistence in the essence)
قلب الحقائق (inversion of realities)
موصوف (qualified subject)
ترجيح بلا مرجح (preference without a preferrer)
موجب اختصاص (cause of specification)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's attributes could exist independently as created entities separate from His essence.
Correction: Attributes cannot subsist by themselves because that would invert their reality; they must inhere in a subject, and without subsistence there is no reason for them to belong specifically to God, so they cannot be created.

Checkpoint
What is the key response to the objection that an attribute could be of a subject without subsisting in it?
A) It leads to infinite regress
B) There would be no reason for it to belong to that subject rather than another
C) The objection contradicts the Quran
D) The subject would become the attribute

Key Takeaway
Divine attributes must subsist in God's essence and are uncreated; otherwise they would not be true attributes and would lack a cause of specification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever imagine God's attributes as separate tools He uses, like His mercy being a 'thing' He can give or withhold? How does the truth that His attributes are uncreated and subsist in His essence change the way you call upon Him in du'a?
?
If you truly believed that every attribute of God is as real and eternal as His essence, would you ever fear that His mercy could run out or His justice be suspended? Examine your heart for any lingering doubt that God's attributes are temporary or changeable.
?
When you read in the Quran that God is al-Samī' (the All-Hearing) and al-Baṣīr (the All-Seeing), do you take those as mere metaphors or as real attributes? This lesson forces you to confront that His hearing and seeing are as real as His existence. Are you ready to live knowing that your every word and action is witnessed by attributes that are inseparable from God Himself?

Divine Attributes
intermediate

Proof that Attributes Must Subsist in the Essence
Sanusi proves attributes must subsist in the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi argues that divine attributes cannot subsist by themselves because it would invert their reality.

Core Idea
An attribute that subsists by itself ceases to be an attribute.

Sanusi begins his proof by stating the necessity of attributes subsisting in the essence. He argues that the very definition of an attribute requires a subject that it qualifies. If an attribute existed independently, it would contradict its own nature. Let's examine his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage closely
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the compressed style.
Focus on the logic: from definition to impossibility.
2
Identify the key claim
Sanusi claims that attributes must subsist in the essence and are independent of a specifier.
This is the thesis he will prove.
3
Understand the reasoning
He argues that the reality (حقيقة) of an attribute entails a subject (موصوف). If it subsisted by itself, it would not be an attribute.
The key is 'قلب الحقائق' (inversion of realities).
4
Note the conclusion
Therefore, subsistence by itself is impossible because it separates the attribute from its essential nature.
This is a deductive proof based on definitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما ذكرناه في القسم الرابع - وهو صفات مولانا جل وعلا - من وجوب قيامها بذاتِهِ العليَّةِ، ووجوبِ عَنائِها عنِ المخصص: فلأنَّ كونَها صفاتٍ يُوجِبُ استحالة قيامها بأنفسها؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنْ قلبِ الحقائق، إذ حقيقة الصفة تستلزم موصوفاً يتصف بها، فلو قامَتْ بنفسها لم تكن صفةً، لكن مفارقةُ الصفة لحقيقتها التي هي كونها صفةً لموصوف محال، فقيامُها إذاً بنفسها الذي استلزم مفارقتها لحقيقة نفسها محال.
فإن قلتَ: قُصارى ما أنتج دليلكم أنَّ الصفةَ لا تُعقَلُ حقيقتها بدون موصوف بها، ولا يلزمُ مِن استلزامها موصوفاً بها أن تقوم بذلكَ الموصوف؛ لاحتمال أن تكون صفة لموصوف ولا تقوم به.
فالجواب: أَنَّهُ لا معنى لكونها صفةً لموصوف إلا قيامها بهِ؛ إِذْ لو لم تقم به لم يمكن أن تكون صفة له دون غيره؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنَ الترجيح بلا مُرجح، فلو لم تقم إذاً بموصوفها لم تكن صفةً له ولا لغيره؛ لعدم مُوجِب الاختصاص، فقد لزم إذاً مِنْ قيامها بنفسها وجود الصفةِ بلا موصوف، وذلك إبطال لحقيقتِها.
(1) إذ يصير ما هو في معنى العرض في الحادث ذاتاً قائمة بنفسها، فالصفة معنى، والمعنى لو قام بنفسه انقلبت حقيقته؛ إذ يصير ذاتاً لا معنى.
(2) في (أ) وحدها هنا زيادة: (لغة)
وذلك عين ما ألزمناه في البرهان السابقِ
And as for what we mentioned in the fourth section—which is the attributes of our Lord, exalted and sublime—regarding the obligation of their subsisting in His sublime essence and their necessity of being independent of the specifier: that is because their being attributes necessitates the impossibility of their subsisting by themselves, due to what follows from that of inversion of realities, since the reality of the attribute entails a described entity that is qualified by it. So if it subsisted by itself, it would not be an attribute. But the separation of the attribute from its reality, which is its being an attribute of a described entity, is impossible. Therefore, its subsistence by itself, which entails its separation from its own reality, is impossible.
If you say: The utmost that your proof produces is that the reality of the attribute is not understood without a described entity that has it, but it does not follow from its entailing a described entity that it subsists in that described entity, because it is possible that it be an attribute of a described entity without subsisting in it.
The answer: There is no meaning to its being an attribute of a described entity except its subsistence in it; for if it did not subsist in it, it could not be an attribute for it to the exclusion of others, due to what follows from that of preponderance without a preponderator. So if it does not subsist in its described entity, it is not an attribute for it nor for anything else, due to the absence of a cause of specification. Therefore, from its subsistence by itself follows the existence of an attribute without a described entity, and that is an invalidation of its reality.
(1) Because what is in the meaning of an accident in the contingent becomes an essence subsisting by itself. So the attribute is a meaning, and if a meaning subsists by itself, its reality is inverted, because it becomes an essence, not a meaning.
(2) In (A) alone there is an addition: (language).
And that is exactly what we imposed in the preceding proof.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage is a proof followed by an objection and its answer. Sanusi begins by restating the fourth section of his discussion: the attributes of God must necessarily subsist in His essence and must be independent of any specifier (i.e., they do not require an external cause to be attached to the essence). The reason is that being attributes necessitates that they cannot subsist by themselves, because that would invert realities. The reality of an attribute is that it entails a subject (موصوف) that is qualified by it. If an attribute existed on its own, it would not be an attribute. To separate an attribute from its defining reality is impossible. Therefore, the very idea of an attribute subsisting by itself is impossible—that would separate it from its essential nature.
Then Sanusi presents an objection: the objector says that the proof only shows that the concept of an attribute requires a subject, but it does not prove that the attribute must actually subsist in that subject; it might be an attribute of a subject without inhering in it (like a relation). The answer is that the very meaning of being an attribute of a subject is to subsist in it. If it did not subsist in it, there would be no way to specify it as the attribute of that subject rather than another—that would require a preponderance without a preponderator (ترجيح بلا مرجح), which is impossible. So the only way for the attribute to be specifically related to its subject is to subsist in it. Therefore, if the attribute does not subsist in its subject, it is not an attribute for that subject or any other. Thus, an attribute subsisting by itself would be an attribute without any subject, which invalidates its reality. The footnote explains that if an attribute (which in contingent things is an accident) were to subsist by itself, it would turn into an essence, inverting its nature. Sanusi concludes that this is exactly the point he made in the earlier proof.

Key Terms
صفة
قيام
موصوف
قلب الحقائق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that attributes are independent entities that could exist on their own.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the very definition of an attribute requires a subject; without it, it is not an attribute.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is it impossible for an attribute to subsist by itself?
A) It would then be independent of the essence, contradicting its contingency.
B) The reality of an attribute requires a subject in which it subsists; otherwise it would not be an attribute.
C) God cannot have attributes.
D) Attributes are identical with the essence.

Key Takeaway
An attribute's very definition entails a subject; therefore, it cannot exist independently.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of Allah's mercy, do you ever imagine it as something that could 'exist' on its own, separate from Him? How does realizing that mercy cannot be an attribute without Him force you to see it as part of His very being, not a gift detached from Him?
?
This lesson says that an attribute by definition requires a subject. Have you ever unknowingly treated one of Allah's attributes as if it had an independent existence—like imagining His power as a force out there? What would it mean for your worship to truly internalize that every attribute is nothing but Allah Himself?
?
If an attribute cannot stand alone, then how dependent are you on Allah for even your best qualities? Do you ever try to carry yourself as if your patience or generosity is your own independent possession? Let this truth shatter that illusion: what would it take to live every moment relying on the One who alone is self-subsistent?

Answering the Objection: Attributes Must Subsist in Their Subject
Sanusi answers an objection about attribute subsistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's response to the objection that an attribute could be related to a subject without subsisting in it.

Core Idea
The only way an attribute can be specific to a subject is by subsisting in it.

An objector proposes a subtle challenge: maybe an attribute can be related to a subject without literally inhering in it. Sanusi replies that this would make the attribute unspecific and lead to preponderance without a preponderator. Let's see how he defends the necessity of subsistence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the objection in Arabic and translation. The objector concedes the need for a subject but denies inherence.
Understand the nuance: relation vs. inherence.
2
Analyze Sanusi's answer
Sanusi asserts that being an attribute of a subject means subsisting in it; otherwise, the attribute cannot be specific to that subject.
He uses the principle of preponderance without a preponderator (ترجيح بلا مرجح).
3
Understand the consequence
If the attribute does not subsist, it cannot be an attribute of any subject, which invalidates its reality.
The footnote explains that a self-subsistent attribute would become an essence, inverting its nature.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Consider why Sanusi's response effectively closes the loophole.
The argument ties specificity to inherence via rational necessity.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An attribute can be related to a subject merely by conceptual attribution without real inherence.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what problem arises if an attribute is not said to subsist in its subject?
A) The attribute would be eternal.
B) There would be no reason for it to be specific to that subject.
C) The subject would be imperfect.
D) The attribute would become a substance.

Key Takeaway
Without subsistence, an attribute cannot be uniquely tied to its subject; therefore, subsistence is necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call God 'All-Knowing', do you truly believe that His knowledge is a real attribute that subsists in His essence, or do you sometimes treat it as just a metaphor? How does this lesson challenge you to deepen your conviction about the reality of God's attributes?
?
The argument here uses logic to prove that attributes cannot be arbitrary. Is your faith built on logical necessity or on casual acceptance? Are there any attributes of God that you have not seriously thought about as necessarily belonging to Him? What will you do to rectify that?
?
If you were to face someone who denies the reality of God's attributes, claiming they are mere relations, would you be able to articulate Sanusi's rebuttal? This lesson calls you to be intellectually prepared: will you take the time to master this proof so you can defend your creed?
