Why God's Attributes Cannot Be Called Needy
Sanusi explains why it is incorrect to say God's attributes are in need (muftaqir) of the essence and criticizes Fakhr al-Din al-Razi for doing so.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi prohibits using the term 'dependency' for God's attributes and why he criticizes al-Razi for doing so.

Core Idea
Describing God's attributes as 'needy' implies deficiency, impossible for the Perfect.

Sanusi now turns to a subtle but important point: the language we use about God's attributes. In this passage, he explains why the term 'dependency' (iftiqar) should never be applied to the divine attributes, and he takes the notable theologian Fakhr al-Din al-Razi to task for doing just that. This lesson unpacks his linguistic and theological reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, noticing Sanusi's linguistic examples and his critique of al-Razi.
Focus on the reasoning, not the names.
2
Analyze the linguistic argument
Consider the examples of hunger and nakedness. Why does Sanusi say dependency ends once the need is met? Apply this to God's attributes.
This shows the term implies a change from state of need to satisfaction.
3
Understand the theological impossibility
Sanusi argues that both the attributes and the essence are necessary and eternal; thus there is no 'missing' something. Hence dependency is inconceivable.
The attributes are not acquired; they are eternal.
4
Examine the critique of al-Razi
Notice that Sanusi does not reject al-Razi's premise that attributes subsist in the essence, but the conclusion that this implies dependency. He faults al-Razi for not seeing the negative connotation.
This is an important lesson about precision in theological language.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنَّما عدلنا عن ذكر الافتقار إلى الذات في صفة المولى تبارك وتعالى؛ لأنَّ الافتقار والفقر يقتضيانِ لغةً وعُرْفاً الحاجة إلى أمر مفقود يُطلَبُ حصوله؛ فيُقالُ: الجائع يفتقر إلى الأكْلِ، فإذا أكل وشبعَ لم يُوصَف بالافتقار إلى الأكل، وكما يُقالُ: العُرْيانُ مفتقر إلى كسوة، فإذا اكتسى لم يُطلَق عليهِ الافتقار إلى الكسوة، وقس على هذا ولا شكّ أنَّ صفاتِ مولانا تبارك وتعالى يستحيل عليها الافتقار؛ لأنَّهُ إنْ كانَ لتحصيل وجودها فوجودها حاصل واجبٌ غني عن الفاعل أزلاً وأبداً، وإنْ كانَ لتحصيل وجودِ موصوفها فهو ذاتُ مولانا جل وعزّ، أيضاً حاصل واجب غني لا يتصوَّرُ عدمُهُ أزلاً ولا أبداً، غني عن كل ما سواه، ومفتقر إليه كلُّ ما عداه، فمعنى الفقرِ إذاً لا يتصوَّرُ في الذات ولا في صفاتِها، فيُمنع إطلاق لفظِهِ على الصفاتِ الأزليَّةِ وقد غَفَلَ الفخرُ فأساءَ الأدب، وأطلق عليها الفقر إلى الذاتِ العليَّةِ؛ نظراً منه إلى استحالة قيامها بأنفُسِها، ووجوب قيامها بموصوفها (1) ولم يتنبه إلى ما يوهمه الفقر والافتقارُ مِنْ فقد أمر (2)
(1) وهو قوله قبل: (فلو قامت بنفسها لم تكن صفة...)
(2) انظر (الأربعين) (ص 228)، و (مفاتيح الغيب) (123/1)، وانظر أيضاً أبكار الأفكار) (259/3)، و (شرح العقيدة الكبرى) (ص 326)، وعامة متكلمي الأعاجم على هذا القول؛ كالعلامة العضد وتلميذه العلامة السعد
And we only refrained from mentioning dependency (iftiqar) upon the essence in the attribute of the Lord, blessed and exalted, because dependency and poverty (faqr) linguistically and conventionally imply need for something missing that is sought to be obtained. So it is said: the hungry person is in need of food; when he eats and is satisfied, he is not described as being in need of food. And similarly it is said: the naked person is in need of clothing; when he clothes himself, he is not described as being in need of clothing. And analogize to this. And there is no doubt that the attributes of our Lord, blessed and exalted, are impossible to have dependency because if it were for the attainment of their existence, then their existence is already obtained, necessary, independent of an agent eternally and everlastingly. And if it were for the attainment of the existence of their described entity, then it is the essence of our Lord, majestic and sublime, also obtained, necessary, independent, whose non-existence is inconceivable eternally and everlastingly, independent of everything other than Him, and everything other than Him is dependent upon Him. Therefore, the meaning of poverty (faqr) is not conceivable in the essence nor in Its attributes. So its verbal usage with respect to the eternal attributes is prohibited. And al-Fakhr (al-Razi) was heedless and behaved poorly, and applied to them poverty with respect to the sublime essence, looking from his standpoint at the impossibility of their subsisting by themselves and the necessity of their subsisting in their described entity, and he did not pay attention to what poverty and dependency suggest of the loss of something.
(1) That is his earlier statement: (If it had subsisted by itself, it would not be an attribute...)
(2) See [al-Arba'in (p. 228), Mafatih al-Ghayb (1/123), also Abkar al-Afkar (3/259), Sharh al-Aqida al-Kubra (p. 326)], and the majority of non-Arab theologians hold this view, like al-‘Allama al-‘Aḍud and his student al-‘Allama al-Sa‘d.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a clarification and critique. Sanusi explains why he avoided the term 'dependency' (الافتقار) or 'poverty' (الفقر) when describing God's attributes. He argues that linguistically and conventionally, 'dependency' implies a need for something missing that one seeks to obtain. For example, a hungry person is dependent on food only before eating; after eating, that dependency ceases. Similarly, a naked person is dependent on clothing until clothed. Applying this to God's attributes: if we say they are dependent on the essence for their existence, that would imply that their existence was not already actual—but their existence is necessary, eternal, and independent of any agent. If we say they are dependent for the existence of their subject (the essence), the essence itself is also necessary, eternal, and its non-existence is inconceivable. So the concept of poverty/dependency simply does not apply to either the essence or its attributes. Therefore, using such language for the eternal attributes is forbidden. Sanusi then criticizes Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (الفخر) for being heedless and ill-mannered (أساء الأدب) by calling the attributes 'poor' or 'needy' with respect to the essence. Al-Razi's reasoning was that attributes cannot subsist by themselves and must subsist in the essence, which is true, but he failed to see the negative implications of the term 'poverty'—that it suggests a lack or deficiency. The footnotes provide cross-references to al-Razi's works and note that the majority of non-Arab theologians (متعكلمي الأعاجم) agree with Sanusi's position, including al-‘Allama al-‘Aḍud and his student al-‘Allama al-Sa‘d.

Key Terms
افتقار (dependency)
فقر (poverty)
ذات (essence)
صفة أزلية (eternal attribute)
الفخر (al-Fakhr al-Razi)
واجب غني (necessary, independent)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Describing God's attributes as 'dependent' or 'needy' (muftaqira) upon the essence is an acceptable theological expression.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the term implies a lack or deficiency, which is impossible for the eternal attributes and essence. Hence such language is prohibited.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi criticize al-Razi for describing God's attributes as 'needy' (مفتقرة) of the essence?
A) Because al-Razi denied the attributes altogether.
B) Because al-Razi claimed the attributes are not eternal.
C) Because the term 'need' implies a lack that is impossible for necessary beings.
D) Because al-Razi said the attributes subsist by themselves.

Key Takeaway
Using the term 'dependency' for God's attributes is prohibited because it implies a deficiency that contradicts their eternal and necessary perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about Allah's attributes, do you ever use words or phrases that, even unintentionally, suggest need or imperfection? How will you check your own language after learning from Sanusi's warning about al-Razi's heedlessness?
?
Sanusi says al-Razi 'behaved poorly' by using the term 'poverty' for divine attributes. Is there any term you use for Allah that might carry a similar implication? What step will you take today to remove that from your vocabulary?
?
If a friend told you that describing Allah's attributes as 'dependent' is harmless because they cannot exist without Him, how would you explain from this passage why that language is actually problematic? Do you feel confident enough to correct them?

Why Divine Attributes Cannot Be Called 'In Need'
Sanusi refutes the use of 'neediness' for divine attributes and criticizes al-Razi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the term 'neediness' (iftiqār) cannot be applied to God's attributes despite their dependence on the essence.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are eternally perfect; neediness implies lack, impossible for Allah.

Sanusi here addresses a subtle but crucial point in kalam: the language we use for Allah must be free from any implication of imperfection. While the attributes subsist through the essence, calling them 'in need' of the essence would suggest a prior deficiency. In this passage, he explains the linguistic reasoning and critiques al-Razi's oversight.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the examples of hunger and nakedness.
2
Understand the linguistic argument
Focus on why 'neediness' linguistically implies a lack of something sought. See how the examples illustrate this.
3
Analyze the critique of al-Razi
Identify al-Razi's error: he thought 'neediness' was appropriate because attributes cannot subsist independently, but he missed the connotation of lack.
Consider how the author balances critique with a supplication for forgiveness.

وذلك عين ما ألزمناه في البرهان السابقِ [ خطأُ مَنْ وصف صفاتِ اللهِ تعالى بكونها مفتقرةً إلى الذاتِ ] وإنَّما عدلنا عن ذكر الافتقار إلى الذات في صفة المولى تبارك وتعالى ؛ لأنَّ الافتقار والفقر يقتضيانِ لغةً وعُرْفاً الحاجة إلى أمر مفقود يُطلَبُ حصوله ؛ فيُقالُ : الجائع يفتقر إلى الأكْلِ ، فإذا أكل وشبعَ لم يُوصَف بالافتقار إلى الأكل ، وكما يُقالُ : العُرْيانُ مفتقر إلى كسوة ، فإذا اكتسى لم يُطلَق عليهِ الافتقار إلى الكسوة ، وقس على هذا ولا شكّ أنَّ صفاتِ مولانا تبارك وتعالى يستحيل عليها الافتقار ؛ لأنَّهُ إنْ كانَ لتحصيل وجودها فوجودها حاصل واجبٌ غني عن الفاعل أزلاً وأبداً ، وإنْ كانَ لتحصيل وجودِ موصوفها فهو ذاتُ مولانا جل وعزّ ، أيضاً حاصل واجب غني لا يتصوَّرُ عدمُهُ أزلاً ولا أبداً ، غني عن كل ما سواه ، ومفتقر إليه كلُّ ما عداه ، فمعنى الفقرِ إذاً لا يتصوَّرُ في الذات ولا في صفاتِها ، فيُمنع إطلاق لفظِهِ على الصفاتِ الأزليَّةِ وقد غَفَلَ الفخرُ فأساءَ الأدب ، وأطلق عليها الفقر إلى الذاتِ العليَّةِ ؛ نظراً منه إلى استحالة قيامها بأنفُسِها ، ووجوب قيامها موصوفها ولم يتنبه إلى ما يوهمه الفقر والافتقارُ مِنْ فقد أمرٍ يُحتاج إلى حصولِهِ ، والله سبحانَهُ المسؤولُ أنْ يسمح لنا ولهُ ولسائرِ المؤمنين والمؤمناتِ ، وأن يعامل جميعنا دنيا وأخرى بما هو أهلُ لهُ مِنْ كثرة العفوِ والغفرانِ لعظيم الزلاتِ ، ولا يعاملنا بما نحنُ لهُ أهلُ مِنَ النقم وأنواع العقوباتِ ، والطردِ دنيا وأخرى عن جميع الخيراتِ ؛ بجاه نبيه ومصطفاه سيّدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وعلى آلِهِ وصحبه فهو وسيلتنا العظمى وذخيرتنا الكبرى وملجونا الأعز والأرفع في الحياة وبعد الوفاة
And that is exactly what we forced upon him in the previous proof: [The error of the one who describes God's attributes as being in need of the essence]. And indeed we refrained from mentioning the neediness to the essence regarding the attribute of the Lord, blessed and exalted, because neediness and poverty linguistically and customarily imply the need for a missing thing whose attainment is sought; thus it is said: the hungry person needs food, but when he eats and is satiated he is not described as needing food; and likewise it is said: the naked person is in need of clothing, but when he is clothed the need for clothing is not applied to him. And analogize to this. And there is no doubt that the attributes of our Lord, blessed and exalted, are impossible of neediness, because if [the neediness] was for the attainment of their existence, then their existence is actual, necessary, independent of an agent eternally and forever; and if [the neediness] was for the attainment of the existence of their possessor, that is the essence of our Lord, mighty and sublime, also actual, necessary, independent, whose non-existence is inconceivable eternally and forever, independent of all other than Him, and everything other than Him is in need of Him. So the meaning of poverty is therefore inconceivable in the essence nor in its attributes, and thus the application of its word to the eternal attributes is prevented. And al-Fakhr [al-Razi] was heedless and spoke disrespectfully, and applied to them poverty to the sublime essence, considering from his perspective the impossibility of their subsisting by themselves and the necessity of their subsisting through their possessor, and he did not realize what poverty and neediness imply of the lack of something whose attainment is needed. And Allah, glorified is He, is the one asked to grant leniency to us and to him and to the rest of the believing men and believing women, and to treat all of us in this world and the next with what is befitting of Him of abundant pardon and forgiveness for great slips, and not to treat us with what is befitting of us of punishments and types of penalties, and expulsion in this world and the next from all good things; by the status of His Prophet and chosen one, our master and patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and upon his family and his companions, for he is our greatest means, our greatest treasure, and our most honored refuge in life and after death.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and clarification concerning the term 'neediness' (iftiqār) as applied to God's attributes. The author begins by linking this discussion to a previous proof ('the previous proof') which established the error of describing God's attributes as being in need of the essence. He then explains why the author and his school avoid using the term 'iftiqār ilā al-dhāt' for divine attributes. The reason is linguistic and customary: 'iftiqār' and 'faqr' imply a need for something that is missing and sought after. He illustrates this with examples: a hungry person is in need of food, but after eating is no longer described as such; a naked person is in need of clothing, but after being clothed the term no longer applies. By analogy, neediness implies a prior state of lack. Since God's attributes are eternal and necessarily existent, they cannot be described as needing their essence for their existence because both the attributes and the essence are necessary, independent, and without any lack. The author argues: if the supposed neediness is for the existence of the attributes themselves, then their existence is already actual and necessary, requiring no agent. If it is for the existence of the possessor (the essence), then the essence is also necessary and independent. Hence, the concept of poverty (faqr) is inconceivable for the essence and its attributes. Therefore, the term 'poverty' cannot be applied to the eternal attributes. The author then criticizes Fakhr al-Din al-Razi (al-Fakhr) for heedlessness and poor etiquette in applying 'faqr' to the attributes. Al-Razi's reasoning, based on the impossibility of attributes subsisting by themselves and their need to subsist through the essence, is acknowledged, but he failed to see that 'faqr' and 'iftiqār' imply a lack of something needed. Since the attributes and essence have no lack, the term is inappropriate. The passage concludes with a supplication for forgiveness and mercy for all believers, including al-Razi, and a plea for treatment by God's pardon rather than justice.

Key Terms
الافتقار
الذات
الصفات الأزلية
الفخر (الرازي)
الغنى
الفقر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'neediness' is an acceptable term for the relationship between attributes and essence because the attributes depend on the essence for their subsistence.
Correction: The author shows that 'neediness' implies a prior lack that is incompatible with divine perfection. The attributes are eternally necessary and have no lack.

Checkpoint
Why does the author avoid using the term 'iftiqār' (neediness) for God's attributes?
A) Because the attributes are created and temporal.
B) Because 'iftiqār' linguistically implies a need for something missing, which does not apply to necessary attributes.
C) Because the Quran forbids using this term.
D) Because the attributes are identical to the essence.

Key Takeaway
The term 'neediness' cannot apply to Allah's attributes because they are eternal and perfect, and the word implies a deficiency that is impossible for the Divine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever, even unknowingly, thought of Allah's attributes as being 'in need' of something else, like His mercy needing a recipient or His power needing an object? What does this lesson reveal about the hidden assumption behind such thoughts?
?
The author prays for forgiveness for al-Razi and himself. Is there a scholar or person you have harbored resentment towards for theological errors? How does this lesson's call for leniency (السماحة) challenge you to pardon them as well?
?
When you recite Allah's attributes in His names (e.g., al-Ghaniyy, al-Ṣamad), does your heart affirm their absolute independence, or do you still find traces of neediness in your conception? What step will you take today to purify your understanding?

Definition of Eternal Power (al-qudra al-azaliyya)
Sanusi defines eternal power as the attribute of creating and annihilating possibles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of Allah's eternal power and its relationship to His will.

Core Idea
Eternal power creates and annihilates possibles, always in accordance with the will.

The divine attribute of power (qudra) is a cornerstone of Islamic theology. In this lesson, Imam Sanusi defines eternal power with precision, highlighting its scope and its inseparable connection to the divine will. Understanding this definition clarifies how Allah's omnipotence operates within His wise plan.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition
Read the Arabic passage once carefully. Note the key terms: القدرة الأزلية, إيجاد, إعدام, الممكن, الإرادة.
The word 'يَتَأَنَّى' is a variant of 'يَتَأَتَّى' meaning 'is effected'.
2
Identify the three components
The definition has three parts: (1) it is an attribute (صفة), (2) its effect is bringing into existence and annihilating every possible, (3) this occurs in accordance with the will. Identify each part in the Arabic.
3
Reflect on the role of the will
Ask yourself why Sanusi specifies that power acts 'according to the will'. What misconception does this prevent?
This guards against thinking power is arbitrary or independent of divine wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْقُدْرَةُ الأَزَلِيَّةُ : عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ صِفَةٍ يَتَأَنَّى بِهَا إِيجَادُ كُلِّ مُمْكِن وَإِعْدَامُهُ عَلَى وَفْقِ الْإِرَادَةِ .
And the eternal power: it is an expression of an attribute by which is effected the bringing-into-existence of every possible and its annihilation in accordance with the will.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the divine attribute of eternal power (al-qudra al-azaliyya). The author defines it as an attribute (ṣifa) by which Allah brings into existence (ījād) and annihilates (i‘dām) every possible thing (kull mumkin) in accordance with His will (al-irāda). The definition is precise: power is not independent but operates consistently with the will, meaning that Allah's power does not act arbitrarily but executes what His will specifies. The phrase 'according to the will' guards against the misconception that power alone directly produces effects without the mediation of will.

Key Terms

إعدام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Power acts independently of will and can produce effects arbitrarily.
Correction: The definition explicitly states power operates 'in accordance with the will' (عَلَى وَفْقِ الْإِرَادَةِ), so it is not arbitrary or independent.

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between eternal power and will according to the definition?
A) Power acts independently of will.
B) Power brings about existence and annihilation in accordance with the will.
C) Power only creates, but annihilation is by will.
D) Power and will are the same attribute.

Key Takeaway
Eternal power is the attribute through which Allah creates and destroys all possible things, exactly as His will decrees.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You plan your life as if you control outcomes. How does the truth that all existence and annihilation are in Allah's power—and only according to His will—change your sense of security? Will you surrender control today?
?
Think of a prayer you made that was not answered as you wished. Does the fact that Allah's power is always exercised with His perfect will give you peace? Will you accept His choice even when it hurts?
?
You often rely on your own strength to overcome challenges. How does knowing that even your ability to act is a possible thing created by Allah's power affect your humility? Will you acknowledge your dependence on Him in your next difficulty?

Defining Divine Will (al-Irada)
Sanusi defines will as the attribute that specifies possible things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise meaning of the divine attribute of will (al-irāda) as the attribute of specification (takhṣīṣ) that determines which permissible state a possible thing takes.

Core Idea
Will is not power or knowledge; it is the selector of reality among possibilities.

Before we can talk about how Allah acts, we need to clearly understand the attributes through which He acts. The divine will (al-irāda) is one such attribute, and it is often misunderstood as simply wanting something. In this short but foundational passage, Sanusi gives a precise technical definition that distinguishes will from other attributes like power and knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the one-sentence definition in Arabic carefully. Notice the key terms: الإرادة (will), صفة (attribute), تخصيص (specification), الممكن (the possible), يجوز (permissible).
The word يَتَأَنَّى means 'is effected' or 'occurs through'.
2
Translate and parse the definition
Match each Arabic term with its English meaning. The definition says will is an attribute by which the specification of the possible to some of what is permissible for it is effected.
3
Understand the role of specification
Realize that without will, a possible thing could be either existent or non-existent, or have various qualities. The will selects which specific possibility becomes actual.
This distinguishes will from power: power brings about existence, but will decides which existence.
4
Contrast with power and knowledge
Consider how this definition differs from other attributes. Power enables creation, knowledge encompasses all possibilities, but will singles out one possibility to actualize.
This answers the common misunderstanding that will is just wanting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالإِرَادَةُ : صِفَةٌ يَتَأَنَّى بِهَا تَخْصِيصُ الْمُمْكِن بِبَعْضِ مَا يَجُوزُ عَلَيْهِ .
And the will: an attribute by which is effected the specification of the possible to some of what is permissible for it.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage defines the divine attribute of will (al-irāda). The will is described as an attribute (ṣifa) through which Allah's specification (takhṣīṣ) of a possible thing (al-mumkin) occurs. The specification is 'to some of what is permissible for it' meaning that before the will, a possible thing could be either existent or non-existent, or could have various qualities; the will determines which specific state it actually takes. This distinguishes will from power: power brings about existence or non-existence, but will decides which among the many permissible possibilities is actualized.

Key Terms

تخصيص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It creates all possible things.
B) It specifies which permissible state a possible thing takes.
C) It destroys possible things.
D) It knows all possible things.

Key Takeaway
Divine will (al-irāda) is the attribute that specifies which permissible state a possible thing takes, distinguishing it from power and knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a decision between multiple permissible options, do you truly believe that Allah's will has already specified the best for you, or do you rely on your own estimation? What one decision can you surrender to His will today?
?
Reflect on a time when you wished a different possibility had become real. How does knowing that Allah's will is the selector of reality change your perspective on that event? Can you genuinely thank Him for His specification?
?
If will is distinct from knowledge and power, that means God not only knows what could happen and can make it happen, but He specifically chooses it. How does that personal choice of God affect your relationship with Him? How can you respond to His choice with gratitude and trust right now?

First Division of Attributes and the Objection on Defining Them
Sanusi introduces the first division of divine attributes and addresses an objection on defining them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first division of divine attributes (existence as essential attribute) and why definitions of attributes are only descriptive sketches (rasm), not real definitions (ḥadd).

Core Idea
We can describe attributes without claiming to comprehend Allah's essence.

Sanusi starts unpacking the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī). The first division he identifies is existence itself — not as an added quality, but as what expresses the essence. He then anticipates a crucial objection: if the reality of attributes is as hidden as the essence, how can we define them? His answer distinguishes between a true definition and a mere distinguishing description, laying the groundwork for all future discussions of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and footnotes
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the footnote numbers — they are not mere references but integral responses. The first footnote answers an objection; the second clarifies the author's theological stance.
Footnotes in parentheses are part of the original matn.
2
Identify the first division
Find the sentence that describes the first division of attributes. It is 'that by which is expressed the essence itself, the supreme; and it is existence'. Ask yourself: Why is existence listed first?
Existence is not an attribute added to the essence; it is the essence itself according to al-Ash'ari.
3
Understand the objection and answer
The passage anticipates a question: how can we define attributes if their reality is concealed like the essence? The answer: these are not real definitions (ḥadd ḥaqīqī) but merely descriptive sketches (rasm) to distinguish one attribute from another.
This distinction protects against the misconception that we can fully comprehend Allah's essence through definitions.
4
Reflect on the author's theological choice
The author follows Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari in holding that existence is identical to the existent (al-wujūd ‘ayn al-mawjūd). Consider why this matters for tawḥīd and how it affects the categorization of attributes.
This position avoids making existence an added attribute, preserving divine simplicity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ أقسام صفاتِ الحقِّ تبارك وتعالى ] شرع هنا في بيان صفاتِ المعاني (۱) ؛ وهي الصفاتُ الوجودية التي يتصف بها مولانا تبارك وتعالى ؛ فإنَّ صفاتِهِ تبارك وتعالى تنقسم إلى أقسام : الأول : ما يُعبَّرُ بهِ عن نفسِ الذاتِ العليَّة؛ وهي الوجود (۲) . (۱) إن قيل : صفاتُه تعالى كذاته ، كُنْهُها محجوب عن العقل ، فكيف يحدها ؟ فالجواب : هذا ليس بحد حقيقي ، وإنما هو رسم ؛ لتمييز بعضها عن بعض . (۲) اختار المصنف هنا طريقة إمام أهل السنة أبي الحسن الأشعري من كون الوجود عين الموجود ، وليس بزائد عليه ، فعده صفةٌ فيه تسمح .
[Divisions of the attributes of Allah, blessed and exalted] He began here to explain the attributes of meanings (1); and they are the existential attributes with which our Master, blessed and exalted, is described. For His attributes, blessed and exalted, are divided into divisions: The first: that by which is expressed the essence itself, the supreme; and it is existence (2). (1) If it is said: His attributes, exalted is He, are like His essence, their reality is concealed from the intellect, so how can they be defined? The answer: This is not a real definition, but rather a sketch (rasm) to distinguish some from others. (2) The author here chose the method of the Imam of the People of Sunnah, Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari, that existence is identical to the existent, not additional to it, so he counted it as an attribute with some leniency.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is an introductory explanation of the divisions of Allah's attributes, focusing on the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī) which are the existential attributes (al-ṣifāt al-wujūdiyya). The author states that these attributes are divided into sections. The first section is what expresses the essence itself (al-dhāt al-‘aliyya), namely existence (al-wujūd). The footnote (1) addresses an objection: how can we define attributes if their reality is as hidden as the essence? The answer is that these are not real definitions (ḥadd ḥaqīqī) but only conceptual descriptions (rasm) to distinguish one attribute from another. Footnote (2) notes that the author follows Abu al-Hasan al-Ash‘ari's view that existence is identical to the existent (al-wujūd ‘ayn al-mawjūd), not an additional attribute, but he still lists it as an attribute for practical purposes.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
الصفات الوجودية
الذات
الوجود
حد
رسم
عين الموجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Defining divine attributes means we can comprehend Allah's essence.
Correction: Definitions of attributes are only descriptive sketches (rasm) to distinguish between them; the true essence remains beyond human intellect.

Checkpoint
Why does the author describe the definition of attributes as a 'rasm' rather than a 'ḥadd ḥaqīqī'?
A) Because the attributes are unknowable.
B) Because the attributes are not real.
C) Because a real definition would require knowing the essence, which is hidden, so it is only a distinguishing description.
D) Because the author disagrees with al-Ash‘ari.

Key Takeaway
The first division of attributes is existence, which is not an added quality but the essence itself; definitions of attributes are merely descriptive sketches to distinguish them, not exhaustive explanations of their reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's attributes, do you ever feel frustrated by the limits of your intellect? How does Sanusi's distinction between a real definition and a descriptive sketch change your approach to learning about Him—will you now accept conceptual distinctions without needing to fully comprehend?
?
The lesson says existence is not a quality added to Allah but His very being. How does this affect your awareness of His presence? Do you live as if His existence is merely a 'fact' about Him, or as the reality that sustains you every moment?
?
Sanusi counted existence as an attribute as a concession for distinction. Are there areas in your faith where you treat conceptual categories as ultimate realities? What would it mean for you to humbly admit that your understanding of Allah is only a 'sketch'?

Defining Eternal Power and Will
Sanusi defines eternal power and will as distinct attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of the eternal attributes of power and will and how they differ.

Core Idea
Power creates possibilities; will chooses which ones happen.

In this passage, Sanusi introduces two of the most fundamental divine attributes: eternal power and will. These attributes work together: power makes possible things exist or cease, while will determines which possibilities actually occur. Understanding this distinction is essential for Ash'ari theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the structure: first a heading, then two definitions.
2
Identify the definition of eternal power
Look for the phrase 'وَالْقُدْرَةُ الأَزَلِيَّةُ' and note what it says about creation and annihilation. Observe the relationship to will stated at the end.
Power is always 'in accordance with will'.
3
Identify the definition of will
Find the definition of 'الإرَادَةُ' and understand that it is about specification. Ask yourself: specification of what?
Will specifies among permissible possibilities.
4
Compare the two definitions
Notice how the two attributes are distinct: power brings about existence/non-existence, will determines which possibility. Consider why both are needed.
5
Address the common misunderstanding
Some might think power and will are the same. Based on the passage, explain why they are separate attributes with different functions.
Use the definitions as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة السابعة في صفات المعاني الأزلية. وَالْقُدْرَةُ الأَزَلِيَّةُ : عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ صِفَةٍ يَتَأَنَّى بِهَا إِيجَادُ كُلِّ مُمْكِن وَإِعْدَامُهُ عَلَىٰ وَفْقِ الْإِرَادَةِ . وَالإِرَادَةُ : صِفَةٌ يَتَأَنَّى بِهَا تَخْصِيصُ الْمُمْكِن بِبَعْضِ مَا يَجُوزُ عَلَيْهِ .
The Seventh Introduction: On the Eternal Attributes of Meanings. Eternal power is an expression of an attribute through which the creation of every possible thing and its annihilation are brought about in accordance with will. And will is an attribute through which the specification of the possible to some of what is permissible for it is brought about.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage defines two of the eternal attributes of meanings: power and will. The author states that eternal power is an attribute by which Allah creates and annihilates every possible thing in accordance with His will. Then he defines will as the attribute that specifies which possibilities occur among the permissible options. This is a standard Ash'ari definition: power is the ability to act or not act in accordance with will, and will is the determination of one possibility over others.

Key Terms
القدرة الأزلية
الإرادة
الممكن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Power and will are the same attribute.
Correction: They are distinct: power brings about existence/non-existence in accordance with will, while will specifies which possibilities occur.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does eternal power bring about?
A) Creation and annihilation of possible things in accordance with will.
B) Specification of possibilities.
C) Existence of necessary things.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Eternal power and will are complementary but distinct attributes in Ash'ari theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Think of a time when you desperately wanted a different outcome. This lesson teaches that Allah's will selected that specific possibility among all others. How does that truth challenge you to surrender your preferences to His choice?
?
Do you sometimes act as if Allah's power is arbitrary, as if He could do anything without reason? How does the distinction between power and will here confront that assumption and call you to deeper trust in His wisdom?

Division of Divine Attributes into Self-Attribute and Negative Attributes
Sanusi classifies attributes into self-attribute and five negative attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's classification of Allah's attributes into one self-attribute (existence) and five negative attributes that negate imperfections, including pre-eternity, everlastingness, necessity of existence, and dissimilarity to created things.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes: one self-attribute (existence) and negative attributes that remove all defects.

Sanusi begins by explaining the attributes of meaning (existential attributes) through which Allah is described. He divides them into two major categories: the self-attribute, which is existence itself, and the negative attributes, which negate any imperfection from Allah. This lesson introduces this foundational classification, essential for understanding Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: first the self-attribute, then the negative attributes.
2
Identify the self-attribute
Find where Sanusi defines the self-attribute. It is existence, expressed by the essence itself. Understand that this attribute is not separate from Allah's essence.
3
List the negative attributes
Look for the five negative attributes mentioned. The passage lists four explicitly: pre-eternity, everlastingness, necessity of existence, and dissimilarity to originated things. Note what each negates.
The passage states there are five; the fifth is implied in the footnote as essential existence.
4
Reflect on necessary existence
Understand why necessary existence is considered a negative attribute: it negates the possibility of non-existence at all times, past and future.
This is a common point of confusion.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرع هنا في بيان صفاتِ المعاني (۱)؛ وهي الصفاتُ الوجودية التي يتصف بها مولانا تبارك وتعالى؛ فإنَّ صفاتِهِ تبارك وتعالى تنقسم إلى أقسام:
[ الصفة النفسية ]
الأول: ما يُعبَّرُ بهِ عن نفسِ الذاتِ العليَّة؛ وهي الوجود (۲).
[ الصفات السلبية ( العدمية ) ]
الثاني: ما يرجعُ معناه إلى سلبِ نقص مستحيل على مولانا تبارك وتعالى؛ وهي خمس صفاتٍ:
القِدَمُ: وهو عبارة عن سلب العدمِ في الأزلِ.
والبقاء: وهو عبارة عن سلبِ العدم فيما لا يزالُ.
ويجمعهما معاً: وجوب الوجودِ (۱)؛ لأنَّه عبارة عن عدم قبولِ العدم أزلاً وأبداً.
(۱) فوجوب الوجود معنى عدمي زائد على مطلق الوجود، ويجمعهما معاً أيضاً: الوجود الذاتي؛ وهو الحقيقة التي لا تقبل العدم بوجه من الوجوه، ثم اعلم: أن الأزل والأبد في حقه سبحانه سيَّانِ، ولذا عبّر الإمام المصنف بالمعنى الجامع بينهما؛ لأنه هو الحقيقة المرادة.
والمخالفة للحوادثِ: وهو عبارة عن عن سلبِ الجِرْمِيَّةِ والعرضيَّةِ وخواصهما (٢).
(٢) وسلب الزمانية والإمكانية ـ من الإمكان ـ؛ حتى تخرج المجردات (الحوادث التي لا مكان لها ولا زمان على القول بها، والزمان من خواص الممكنات قال العلامة العطار في ( حاشيته على شرح جمع الجوامع » ( ٤٥١/٢ ) : ( قال بعض المحققين : رفعُ الزمان والمكان يقرب الأمر إلى الأذهان فرفعهما أصل كل خير، ومن دام في عُشَّهما اختبط في الجهل، وتلاطمت عليه أمواج الشُّبه، فظنّ المدد بينه وبين الله بالنهاية أو بعدم النهاية، والتأخر والتقدم، وذلك كله يفضي إلى جهالات وقع فيها الفلاسفة ).
He begins here to explain the attributes of meanings (1); and they are the existential attributes with which our Master, blessed and exalted, is described. Indeed, His attributes, blessed and exalted, are divided into divisions:
[ The Self-Attribute ]
The first: what is expressed by the essence of the supreme Self; and it is existence (2).
[ The Negative Attributes (of non-existence) ]
The second: whose meaning returns to the negation of an impossibility from our Master, blessed and exalted; and they are five attributes:
Pre-eternity: it is an expression of the negation of non-existence in pre-eternity.
And everlastingness: it is an expression of the negation of non-existence in that which does not cease.
And both together: necessity of existence (1); because it is an expression of the non-acceptance of non-existence pre-eternally and post-eternally.
(1) For necessity of existence is an additional negative meaning beyond absolute existence, and both together also: essential existence; and it is the reality that does not accept non-existence in any way. Then know: that pre-eternity and post-eternity are equal with respect to Him, exalted. Therefore the Imam author expressed the comprehensive meaning between them, because it is the intended reality.
And dissimilarity to originated things: it is an expression of the negation of corporeality and accidentalness and their properties (2).
(2) And the negation of temporality and possibility — from possibility — until the abstract entities (the originated things that have no place and no time, according to the view that holds them, and time is among the properties of possible things) are excluded. Al-Allamah al-Attar said in his gloss on Sharh Jam' al-Jawami' (2/451): Some investigators said: The removal of time and space brings the matter closer to minds, so their removal is the origin of every good; whoever dwells in their nest flounders in ignorance, and the waves of doubts surge over him, and he thinks the distance between him and Allah is either finite or infinite, and of posteriority and priority, and all of that leads to ignorances into which the philosophers fell.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage provides a classification of Allah's attributes. The author states that the attributes of meanings are existential attributes, and they are divided into two categories: a self-attribute and negative attributes. The self-attribute is existence, which is expressed by the essence itself. The negative attributes are five, which negate any imperfection from Allah: (1) Pre-eternity (qidam) negates non-existence in the past; (2) Everlastingness (baqa') negates non-existence in the future; together they constitute necessary existence (wujub al-wujud), which is a negative attribute meaning non-acceptance of non-existence at all times. The footnote explains that necessary existence is an additional negative meaning and that pre-eternity and post-eternity are identical with respect to Allah. (3) Dissimilarity to originated things (mukhalafat al-hawadith) negates corporeality, accidentalness, and their properties, as well as temporality and possibility, excluding abstract entities. The second footnote expands on the negation of temporality and possibility and includes a quote from al-Attar emphasizing the importance of removing time and space from considerations of Allah.

الصفات السلبية
الوجود
القدم

وجوب الوجود
المخالفة للحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Necessary existence is a positive attribute like existence.
Correction: It is a negative attribute that negates non-acceptance of non-existence.

A) Four
B) Five

D) Three

Key Takeaway
Sanusi divides attributes into one self-attribute (existence) and five negative attributes that negate all imperfections from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that Allah's attribute of dissimilarity to originated things negates corporeality and accidentalness. Have you ever, even for a moment, imagined Allah in a form or location? What does this attribute demand of you when you think of Him?
?
The footnote states that removing time and space brings the matter closer to the mind and is the origin of every good. When you make du'a, do you feel that Allah is 'far' or 'close' in a spatial sense? How can you train your heart to transcend such limitations?
?
Sanusi defines necessary existence as non-acceptance of non-existence. This means Allah's existence is utterly dependent on nothing and cannot cease. Does this truth make you feel secure or unsettled? Today, what is one worry that you can surrender to the One who truly and eternally exists?

Divine Attributes

The Five Negative Attributes: Definitions and Their Role in Divine Transcendence
Sanusi enumerates the five negative attributes and defines each.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of the five negative attributes (al-ṣifāt al-salbiyya) and how each negates a specific imperfection from God.

Core Idea
Negative attributes protect God's transcendence by removing all imperfections.

Sanusi introduces a key category of divine attributes: those that negate imperfections from God. Unlike positive attributes that describe what God is, negative attributes clarify what God is not. This passage defines each of the five negative attributes, showing how they safeguard tanzīh (transcendence). Understanding them is essential for avoiding anthropomorphism and other errors.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the five attributes
Read the Arabic passage once through. Then read the translation. Notice that the author lists five attributes, each defined as a negation.
Each definition begins with 'expression for the negation of' (عبارة عن سلب).
2
Understand the first three attributes together
Pre-eternity (al-qidam) and perpetuity (al-baqā') are combined in Necessary Existence (wujūb al-wujūd). Reflect on how all three negate non-existence.
The footnote explains that pre-eternity and post-eternity are equal in God's case.
3
Analyze the attribute of unlikeness to incidents
Al-mukhālafah lil-ḥawādith negates corporeality, accidentality, and their properties. See the footnote for further negations of temporality and possibility.
This attribute ensures God is not like any created thing.
4
Examine self-subsistence and oneness
Al-qiyām bil-nafs negates need for a substratum or specificator. Al-waḥdāniyya negates any equal in essence, attributes, and actions.
These complete the set by asserting God's independence and uniqueness.
5
Summarize the key idea
All five attributes are negations. They collectively remove any possible imperfection from God, affirming His transcendence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : ما يرجعُ معناه إلى سلبِ نقص مستحيل على مولانا تبارك وتعالى ؛ وهي خمس صفاتٍ : القِدَمُ : وهو عبارة عن سلب العدمِ في الأزلِ . والبقاء : وهو عبارة عن سلبِ العدم فيما لا يزالُ ويجمعهما معاً : وجوب الوجود (۱) ؛ لأنَّه عبارة عن عدم قبولِ العدم أزلاً وأبداً والمخالفة للحوادثِ : وهو عبارة عن سلبِ الجِرْمِيَّةِ والعرضيَّةِ وخواصهما (٢) .

(۱) فوجوب الوجود معنى عدمي زائد على مطلق الوجود ، ويجمعهما معاً أيضاً : الوجود الذاتي ؛ وهو الحقيقة التي لا تقبل العدم بوجه من الوجوه ، ثم اعلم : أن الأزل والأبد في حقه سبحانه سيَّانِ ، ولذا عبّر الإمام المصنف بالمعنى الجامع بينهما ؛ لأنه هو الحقيقة المرادة

(۲) وسلب الزمانية والإمكانية ـ من الإمكان ـ ؛ حتى تخرج المجردات (الحوادث التي لا مكان لها ولا زمان على القول بها ، والزمان من خواص الممكنات قال العلامة العطار في ( حاشيته على شرح جمع الجوامع » ( ٤٥١/٢ ) : ( قال بعض المحققين : رفعُ الزمان والمكان يقرب الأمر إلى الأذهان فرفعهما أصل كل خير ، ومن دام في عُشَّهما اختبط في الجهل ، وتلاطمت عليه أمواج الشُّبه ، فظنّ المدد بينه وبين الله بالنهاية أو بعدم النهاية ، والتأخر والتقدم ، وذلك كله يفضي إلى جهالات وقع فيها الفلاسفة )

والقيام بالنفس : وهو عبارةٌ عن سلب الافتقار إلى المحل والمخصص . والوحدانية : وهو عبارة عن سلب النظير في الذَّاتِ والصفاتِ والأفعال .
The second: what its meaning refers to the negation of an impossible imperfection regarding our Master, Blessed and Exalted; and they are five attributes: Pre-eternity (al-qidam): it is an expression for the negation of non-existence in eternity-without-beginning. And Perpetuity (al-baqā'): it is an expression for the negation of non-existence in eternity-without-end. And what brings them together: Necessary Existence (wujūb al-wujūd) (1); because it is an expression for the non-acceptance of non-existence eternally without beginning and without end. And Being Unlike the Incidents (al-mukhālafah lil-ḥawādith): it is an expression for the negation of corporeality, accidentality, and their properties (2).

(1) For Necessary Existence is a negative meaning additional to absolute existence, and what also brings them together is Essential Existence (al-wujūd al-dhātī); it is the reality that does not accept non-existence in any way. Then know: that eternity-without-beginning and eternity-without-end are the same with respect to Him, Exalted is He. Therefore, the Imam-author expressed them with the comprehensive meaning because it is the intended reality.

(2) And the negation of temporality and possiblity — from possibility — so that abstract entities (the incidents that have no place and no time according to the view that asserts them) may be excluded. Time is among the properties of contingent things. The scholar al-‘Aṭṭār said in his footnote on Sharḥ Jam‘ al-Jawāmi‘: 'Some verifiers said: The removal of time and place brings the matter closer to minds. So their removal is the basis of all good. Whoever remains in their nest becomes confused in ignorance, and the waves of doubts surge upon him, so he imagines a distance between him and God by finitude or infinitude, and by posteriority and priority, and all that leads to ignorances in which the philosophers have fallen.'

And Self-Subsistence (al-qiyām bil-nafs): it is an expression for the negation of need for a substratum and a specificator. And Oneness (al-waḥdāniyya): it is an expression for the negation of an equal in essence, attributes, and actions.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage defines the five negative attributes (الصفات السلبية) of God. The author begins by stating that these attributes refer to negating any impossible imperfection from God. He then lists the five: Pre-eternity (al-qidam) negates non-existence at the beginning; Perpetuity (al-baqā') negates non-existence at the end; both are combined in Necessary Existence (wujūb al-wujūd), which negates the possibility of non-existence forever. The footnote expands that Necessary Existence is a negative meaning additional to mere existence, and that pre-eternity and post-eternity are equal for God. The third attribute, Being Unlike the Incidents (al-mukhālafah lil-ḥawādith), negates corporeality, accidentality, and their properties. The second footnote clarifies that it also negates temporality and possibility, and quotes al-‘Aṭṭār on the danger of associating time and place with God. The fourth attribute, Self-Subsistence (al-qiyām bil-nafs), negates need for a substratum or a specificator. The fifth, Oneness (al-waḥdāniyya), negates any equal in essence, attributes, and actions.

Misconception: One might think negative attributes are positive qualities.
Correction: They are negations of imperfections, not affirmations of positive traits.

The Seven Essential Attributes and the Dispute over Sensory Perceptions
Sanusi defines the seven positive attributes and presents three views on additional sensory attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven essential positive attributes of Allah (صفات المعاني) and the three scholarly positions regarding additional sensory attributes.

Core Idea
The seven attributes are fundamental; additional perceptions are debated.

Sanusi now turns to the attributes of meanings—the seven existential attributes that subsist in Allah's essence. After listing them, he presents a scholarly disagreement about whether additional sensory perceptions (smell, taste, touch, pleasure/pain) are distinct attributes. Understanding this dispute clarifies how theologians approach the nature of divine perception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven attributes
Read the Arabic list and note each attribute: Power, Will, Knowledge, Life, Hearing, Sight, Speech.
These are the core attributes of meanings.
2
Understand the dispute
The passage presents three views on additional perceptions: they are separate attributes, they reduce to Knowledge, or we withhold judgment.
The author prefers withholding judgment.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why theologians debate this—it affects how we conceive of Allah's perception without anthropomorphism.
The key is avoiding corporeal associations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : صفات المعاني : وهي عبارة عن الصفاتِ الوجودية القائمة بالذاتِ العليَّةِ ؛ وهي سبع صفاتٍ : القدرة ، والإرادة ، والعلم ، والحياة ، والسمعُ ، والبصرُ ، والكلام .

واختُلِفَ في زيادة صفاتٍ ؛ وهي : إدراك المشموماتِ ، وإدراك المذوقاتِ ، وإدراك الملموساتِ ، وإدراك اللذائذ والآلام(۱) فقيل بثبوتِ زيادتها على الصفاتِ السبع (٢) ، وتكونُ مُتعلقة بكل موجود مِنْ غيرِ اتصال بالأجسام ، ولا تكييف باللذَّاتِ والآلام وقيل : ترجعُ في حقِّهِ تعالى إلى العلم(۳) ، وقيل بالوقف ، وهو أحسنها (٤)

(۱) وكلُّها مشتملة بصفة ( الإدراك )

(۲) وهذا مذهب القاضي الباقلاني وإمام الحرمين الجويني

(۳) وعلى هذا القول : فإثبات صفة العلم لا يغني عن إثبات صفة الإدراك للمذكورات

(٤) وهو اختيار المحقق ابن التلمساني وشيخه العلامة المقترح ، واختاره الإمام المصنف
The third: The attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-ma‘ānī): they are the existential attributes subsisting in the Supreme Essence; and they are seven attributes: Power, Will, Knowledge, Life, Hearing, Sight, and Speech.

And there is disagreement concerning the addition of attributes: perception of smells, perception of tastes, perception of tangible things, perception of pleasures and pains (1). For it is said that they are established as additional to the seven attributes (2), and they are related to every existent without contact with bodies and without qualification by pleasures and pains. And it is said that with respect to Him, Exalted, they reduce to Knowledge (3). And it is said to withhold judgment (al-waqf), and it is the best of them (4).

(1) And all of them are included under the attribute of perception (al-idrāk).

(2) This is the position of al-Qāḍī al-Bāqillānī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn al-Juwaynī.

(3) And according to this position, affirming the attribute of Knowledge does not suffice for affirming the attribute of perception for the aforementioned things.

(4) And it is the choice of the verifier Ibn al-Tilimsānī and his teacher the scholar al-Muqtaḥ, and the Imam-author chose it.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage defines the seven positive attributes of God, called attributes of meanings (صفات المعاني). They are existential attributes that subsist in God's essence: Power, Will, Knowledge, Life, Hearing, Sight, and Speech. The author then discusses a disagreement about additional sensory attributes: perception of smells, tastes, tangible things, and pleasures/pains. Three positions are presented: first, that these perceptions are additional attributes beyond the seven (the view of al-Bāqillānī and al-Juwaynī); second, that they reduce to Knowledge (by implication, not separate); third, withholding judgment (al-waqf), which the author considers the best view and chooses. The footnotes clarify that all these perceptions fall under 'perception', name the proponents of the first view, explain that the second view does not negate the need for a separate attribute of perception, and state the author's preference for withholding judgment.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Assuming that the additional sensory attributes (smell, taste, touch, pleasure/pain) are universally accepted as distinct attributes of Allah.
Correction: In reality, there is a significant scholarly disagreement. Some theologians affirm them as separate, others reduce them to Knowledge, and many (including Sanusi) prefer to withhold judgment (al-waqf).

Checkpoint
What is the author's preferred position regarding additional sensory attributes?
A) They are additional attributes beyond the seven.
B) They reduce to Knowledge.
C) Withholding judgment (al-waqf).
D) They are all included under Life.

Key Takeaway
The seven essential attributes are universally accepted, but the status of additional sensory perceptions remains a matter of scholarly debate, with the cautious position being to withhold judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that scholars withheld judgment on certain divine attributes out of caution, even though they could have taken a side. Where in your own faith do you rush to an opinion on a matter that you have not fully investigated? Will you commit to pausing and saying 'I do not know' more often?
?
The seven attributes—Life, Knowledge, Power, Will, Hearing, Sight, Speech—are affirmed as subsisting in God's essence. When you pray, do you truly call upon God by these names with the conviction that they are real in His essence? Which attribute do you most neglect in your worship, and how will you rectify that starting today?
?
The passage shows that the author chose the position of waqf (withholding judgment) as the best, even though other great scholars held strong opinions. Is your heart attached to being right, or to seeking the truth? Are you willing to abandon a comfortable belief if the evidence is not decisive, and remain in a state of humility before God?

The Seven Attributes of Meanings
Sanusi defines ṣifāt al-maʿānī and lists their seven types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what ṣifāt al-maʿānī are and know the seven attributes enumerated by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Ṣifāt al-maʿānī are seven existential attributes subsisting in Allah's essence.

Sanusi continues his classification of divine attributes by defining the third category: attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī). These are real, existential qualities that subsist in the divine Essence. He then lists the seven universally accepted attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of ṣifāt al-maʿānī
The passage begins with a clear definition. Note the key terms: existential attributes (ṣifāt wujūdiyya) and subsisting in the Exalted Essence.
2
Memorize the seven attributes
Sanusi lists seven: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, speech. Commit them to memory as the foundational attributes of meanings.
These are distinct from essential attributes (ṣifāt dhātiyya).
3
Reflect on the ontological status
Consider what it means for an attribute to be 'existential' and 'subsisting in the essence.' This is key to Ashʿarī theology.

Source Text

الثالث : صفات المعاني : وهي عبارة عن الصفاتِ الوجودية القائمة بالذاتِ العليَّةِ ؛ وهي سبع صفاتٍ : القدرة ، والإرادة ، والعلم ، والحياة ، والسمعُ ، والبصرُ ، والكلام . واختُلِفَ في زيادة صفاتٍ ؛ وهي : إدراك المشموماتِ ، وإدراك المذوقاتِ ، وإدراك الملموساتِ ، وإدراك اللذائذ والآلام(۱) فقيل بثبوتِ زيادتها على الصفاتِ السبع (٢) ، وتكونُ مُتعلقة بكل موجود مِنْ غيرِ اتصال بالأجسام ، ولا تكييف باللذَّاتِ والآلام وقيل : ترجعُ في حقِّهِ تعالى إلى العلم(۳) ، وقيل بالوقف ، وهو أحسنها (٤) (۱) وكلُّها مشتملة بصفة ( الإدراك ) . (۲) وهذا مذهب القاضي الباقلاني وإمام الحرمين الجويني (۳) وعلى هذا القول : فإثبات صفة العلم لا يغني عن إثبات صفة الإدراك للمذكورات . (٤) وهو اختيار المحقق ابن التلمساني وشيخه العلامة المقترح ، واختاره الإمام المصنف
The third: Attributes of meanings: they are the existential attributes subsisting in the exalted Essence; and they are seven attributes: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, and speech. And there is disagreement about additional attributes: they are perceiving smells, perceiving tastes, perceiving tactile objects, and perceiving pleasures and pains (1). Some said they are proven as additional to the seven attributes (2), and they are related to every existent without connection to bodies and without qualification by pleasures and pains. And it was said: in His case, exalted, they reduce to knowledge (3). And it was said to suspend judgment (waqf), and that is the best of them (4). (1) All of them are included under the attribute of perception (al-idrāk). (2) This is the doctrine of al-Qāḍī al-Bāqillānī and Imām al-Ḥaramayn al-Juwaynī. (3) On this view, affirming the attribute of knowledge does not suffice for affirming the attribute of perception for the mentioned things. (4) This is the choice of the verifier Ibn al-Tilimsānī and his teacher the distinguished al-Muqtaḥ, and the author (al-muṣannif) chose it.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of divine attributes, namely ṣifāt al-maʿānī (attributes of meanings), and then discusses a disagreement about whether there are additional attributes beyond the seven. The passage begins by stating that ṣifāt al-maʿānī are existential attributes (ṣifāt wujūdiyya) that inhere in the divine Essence. They are seven: power (qudra), will (irāda), knowledge (ʿilm), life (ḥayāt), hearing (samʿ), sight (baṣar), and speech (kalām). Then the author notes that there is disagreement (ukhtulifa) about increasing (ziyāda) other attributes: specifically, the perception of smells, tastes, tactile objects, and pleasures and pains. Three views are mentioned: (1) Some affirm them as additional to the seven, saying they relate to every existent without physical connection or qualification by pleasures and pains. This is the view of al-Bāqillānī and al-Juwaynī. (2) Others say that in God's case, these perceptions reduce to knowledge (ʿilm), but the author notes that even on this view, affirming knowledge does not suffice for affirming perception of those specific things. (3) Others suspend judgment (waqf), and the author indicates that this is the best view, citing Ibn al-Tilimsānī and al-Muqtaḥ, and it is chosen by the author himself. The passage is a classification of the types of attributes and a survey of scholarly positions.

Ṣifāt al-maʿānī are seven existential attributes subsisting in Allah's essence: power, will, knowledge, life, hearing, sight, and speech.

?
Which of these seven attributes do you most neglect in your daily awareness? Commit to reflecting on that attribute before each prayer today, asking Allah to deepen your conviction.

The Dispute Over Additional Perceptual Attributes
Sanusi presents three views on additional perceptual attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three scholarly positions on whether Allah has additional attributes beyond the seven for perceiving smells, tastes, tactile objects, and pleasures/pains.

Core Idea
Theologians disagree whether Allah has additional perceptual attributes beyond the seven.

After listing the seven attributes of meanings, Sanusi turns to a point of disagreement: are there additional attributes for perceiving specific sensory objects like smells and tastes? Three views are presented, and the author prefers suspending judgment (waqf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of dispute
The passage lists four types of perception: smells, tastes, tactile objects, and pleasures/pains. Note that all fall under the general attribute of perception (idrāk).
2
Examine the first view: additional attributes
Some theologians, including al-Bāqillānī and al-Juwaynī, affirm these as extra attributes beyond the seven.
3
Examine the second view: reduction to knowledge
Others say these perceptions reduce to knowledge in God's case, but the author notes that this view does not deny the need for a distinct attribute of perception.
4
Understand the preferred view: suspension of judgment
The author states that waqf (suspending judgment) is the best position, chosen by Ibn al-Tilimsānī and al-Muqtaḥ.

The Fourth Category: Moral Attributes (الصفات المعنوية)
Sanusi defines the fourth category: moral attributes as necessary concomitants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the moral attributes (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya) and how they are necessary concomitants of the seven attributes of meanings.

Core Idea
Moral attributes are not extra attributes but necessary consequences of the essential attributes of meanings.

In this lesson, we explore the fourth category of divine attributes in Sanusi's classification: the moral attributes. These attributes are not separate existential qualities but are the necessary implications of the seven attributes of meanings. Understanding this distinction is key to grasping the Ashʿarī theory of divine attributes, including the concept of states (aḥwāl).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note how Sanusi introduces the fourth category and the list of moral attributes.
2
Understand the relationship between moral attributes and attributes of meanings
The passage states that moral attributes are necessary concomitants (lāzima) of the attributes of meanings. For each attribute of meaning (e.g., power), there is a corresponding moral attribute (e.g., being powerful).
This is a crucial point: the moral attributes do not add extra realities; they are the descriptions that necessarily follow.
3
Identify the seven moral attributes listed
Find each of the seven moral attributes: being powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, speaking. Notice they correspond exactly to the seven attributes of meanings.
The footnote adds alternative abstract names like al-qādiriyya.
4
Reflect on the concept of states (aḥwāl)
Consider that these moral attributes are often identified with the Ashʿarī theory of states (aḥwāl). They are real but not existent in the usual sense. This connects to deeper theological discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : الصفاتُ المعنويَّةُ : وهي صفات الذات اللازمة لصفاتِ المعاني ؛ وهي : كونه تعالى قادراً ، ومريداً ، وعالماً ، وحيّاً ، وسميعاً ، وبصيراً ، ومُتكلّماً (١) . (۱) ويقال فيها أيضاً : القادرية ، والمريدية ، والعالمية . . . إلى آخره
The fourth: The moral attributes (al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya): they are the attributes of the Essence that are necessary concomitants of the attributes of meanings; and they are: His being, exalted, powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking (1). (1) They are also called: being powerful (al-qādiriyya), being willing (al-murīdiyya), being knowing (al-ʿālimiyya) ... etc.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth category of divine attributes: al-ṣifāt al-maʿnawiyya (moral attributes). These are not additional existential attributes but are the necessary concomitants (lāzima) of the seven ṣifāt al-maʿānī. In other words, because God has the attribute of power (qudra), He is necessarily described as 'powerful' (qādir); because He has will (irāda), He is 'willing' (murīd); because He has knowledge (ʿilm), He is 'knowing' (ʿālim); and so on for life (ḥayāt) giving 'living' (ḥayy), hearing (samʿ) giving 'hearing' (samīʿ), sight (baṣar) giving 'seeing' (baṣīr), and speech (kalām) giving 'speaking' (mutakallim). The footnote adds that these moral attributes are also expressed using abstract nouns like al-qādiriyya (the state of being powerful), al-murīdiyya (being willing), al-ʿālimiyya (being knowing), etc. This category corresponds to the theory of aḥwāl (states) in Ashʿarī theology, where these are considered as states (aḥwāl) that are neither existent nor non-existent but are real attributes distinct from the attributes of meanings.

Key Terms
الصفات المعنوية
القادرية
المريدية
العالمية
الأحوال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Moral attributes are additional existential attributes separate from the attributes of meanings.
Correction: Moral attributes are not separate existential attributes; they are necessary concomitants that logically follow from the attributes of meanings. They describe the state of the Essence without adding a distinct reality.

Checkpoint

A) They are the same
B) They are additional existential attributes
C) They are necessary concomitants of ṣifāt al-maʿānī
D) They are negations

Key Takeaway
Moral attributes are the necessary consequences of the seven attributes of meanings, expressing how God is described as powerful, willing, knowing, living, hearing, seeing, and speaking.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if God is 'al-Baṣīr' (the All-Seeing) in your private moments? If you were to fully internalize that His seeing is necessary and not just a concept, what would you change today?
?
When you call God 'al-Ḥayy' (the Living), do you realize that your own life is a gift from Him, and that He alone is the source of all life? How does that realization affect your gratitude and reliance on Him?
?
If God's moral attributes are necessary concomitants of His essential attributes, then His power, will, and knowledge are inseparable from His essence. How does this truth challenge any tendency you might have to compartmentalize God's attributes or to think of them as optional?

Attributes of Actions: Definition and Division
Sanusi presents the fifth category of attributes and divides them into existential and negative subtypes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the fifth category of divine attributes (attributes of actions) and how they are divided into existential and negative subtypes.

Core Idea
Attributes of actions are temporal relations between God and creation, including both acts and their omissions.

Sanusi introduces a fifth category of divine attributes that some theologians add beyond the four already discussed. These are attributes of actions, which describe God's actual relation to creation. In this passage, he defines them and divides them into existential and negative types, clarifying a key theological nuance about whether omitting punishment counts as an act.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the content. Notice the structure: definition, examples, division.
The passage includes a footnote about Maturidi and Ash'ari views that is part of the text.
2
Understand the definition
Attributes of actions are defined as the actualized relation (taʿalluq tanjīzī) of power and will to contingent things, or as the emanation of contingent things from power and will.
This emphasizes that these attributes are not eternal but occur when God creates or acts.
3
Identify the two divisions
The passage divides these attributes into two types: existential (examples given are creating, providing, causing death, moving, stilling) and negative (pardoning, which is leaving punishment).
Negative attributes involve the omission of an act, like not punishing.
4
Consider the theological nuance
The passage discusses whether leaving (tark) punishment is considered an act. If leaving is an act, then pardoning counts as an active attribute; if not, it is a negation of the act of punishment.
This nuance affects the classification of negative attributes.
5
Relate to broader schools
The footnote mentions that the Maturidis affirm an attribute of 'coming-to-be' (takwīn), while the Ash'aris view these as mere relations. al-Taftāzānī preferred the Ash'ari view.
This is a point of theological disagreement beyond the basic definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزادَ بعضُهم قسماً خامساً : وهو صفات الأفعال(۲) : وهي عبارة عن التعلَّقِ التنجيزي للقدرة والإرادة بالممكناتِ ؛ كخلقِهِ تعالى ورَزْقِهِ وإماتته وتحريكه وتسكينه ، وإن شئت قلت : هي عبارة عن صدورِ الممكناتِ عن القدرةِ والإرادة ؛ وهي تنقسم إلى قسمين : صفةٌ فعليَّةٌ وجودية : كالأمثلة المذكورة . وصفة فعلية سلبية : كعفوه تعالى عمَّنْ شاءَ مِنْ أهل المعاصي ؛ فإنَّهُ عبارةٌ عن تركِ العقوبة لمَنْ يستحقُها ، ولا شك أنَّ هذا الترك مُتأخّرُ عن المعصية الحادثة ، وهو فعل بناءً على أنَّ الترك فعل ، أو سلبُ فعلِ العقوبة لمستحقها بناءً على أنَّهُ ليس بفعل . (۲) وهي المعبّر عنها بصفة ( التكوين ) ، والتي قال بها السادة الماتريدية ، وقد رجح العلامة التفتازاني في ( شرح العقائد النسفية ) ( ص ۱۹۳ ) قول السادة الأشاعرة ، وأنها من الإضافات والاعتبارات العقلية
And some added a fifth division: and it is the attributes of actions (2): they are the actualized relation (al-taʿalluq al-tanjīzī) of power and will to contingent things; like His creating, exalted, and His providing, and His causing death, and His moving, and His stilling. And if you wish, you may say: they are the emanation of contingent things from power and will. And they are divided into two parts: an existential active attribute (ṣifa fiʿliyya wujūdiyya): like the mentioned examples; and a negative active attribute (ṣifa fiʿliyya salbiyya): like His pardoning, exalted, whomever He wills from among the people of sins; for it is the leaving (tark) of punishment for one who deserves it, and there is no doubt that this leaving is subsequent to the occurring sin, and it is an act (fiʿl) based on the view that leaving (tark) is an act, or it is the negation (salab) of the act of punishment for its deserving one based on the view that it is not an act. (2) It is that which is expressed by the attribute of coming-to-be (al-takwīn), which the Māturīdī masters affirm, and the distinguished al-Taftāzānī in his Sharḥ al-ʿAqāʾid al-Nasafiyya (p. 193) gave preponderance to the Ashʿarī masters’ statement that it is among the relational (iḍāfāt) and mental considerations (iʿtibārāt ʿaqliyya).
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth category of divine attributes: ṣifāt al-afʿāl (attributes of actions). Some theologians add this category beyond the previous four. The author explains that these are the actualized relation (al-taʿalluq al-tanjīzī) of God's power (qudra) and will (irāda) to contingent things (mumkināt). Examples include creating (khalq), providing (rizq), causing death (imāta), moving (taḥrīk), and stilling (taskīn). Alternatively, they are described as the emanation (ṣudūr) of contingent things from divine power and will. The passage then divides these attributes into two types: (1) existential active attributes (ṣifa fiʿliyya wujūdiyya), which are examples like creating and providing; and (2) negative active attributes (ṣifa fiʿliyya salbiyya), such as God's pardoning (ʿafw) those sinners He wills, which is interpreted as the leaving (tark) of punishment for someone who deserves it. This leaving is temporally subsequent (mutaʾakhkhar) to the sin. There is a theological nuance: whether this leaving is considered an act (fiʿl) or a non-act. If one considers leaving to be an act, then it is an active attribute; if not, it is a negation of the act of punishment. The footnote mentions that this category corresponds to the attribute of takwīn (bringing into existence) affirmed by the Māturīdīs, while al-Taftāzānī preferred the Ashʿarī view that these are merely relational (iḍāfāt) and rational considerations (iʿtibārāt ʿaqliyya).

Key Terms
صفات الأفعال
التكوين
التعلق التنجيزي
صفة فعلية وجودية
صفة فعلية سلبية
الترك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that attributes of actions are eternal or that negative attributes like pardoning are not real actions.
Correction: The passage clarifies that attributes of actions are temporal relations (actualized at the time of action) and that negative attributes like pardoning involve a real leaving of punishment, which is considered an act or a negation depending on one's definition of 'act'.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for dividing attributes of actions into existential and negative types?
A) Whether they are eternal or temporal
B) Whether they involve creation or forgiveness
C) Whether they are actual emanation or leaving of punishment
D) Whether they are related to power or will

Key Takeaway
Attributes of actions are temporal relations between God and creation, divided into existential acts (e.g., creating) and negative omissions (e.g., pardoning).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that God's pardoning is a temporal act subsequent to sin. When you sin, do you truly believe that God's forgiveness is a real, timely act, or do you assume it is automatic? How does this understanding move you to repent immediately rather than delay?
?
If God's providing (rizq) is an attribute of action that occurs in time, does your daily trust in His provision reflect that you rely on His ongoing, moment-by-moment action? What one change can you make today to live with more reliance on His active provision?
?
The theologians debated whether leaving (tark) is an act. Do you treat God's forgiveness as an active choice or as a mere absence of punishment? How does viewing it as an active divine attribute change the way you seek His pardon?
