Refutation of the Polytheism Objection: Pre-Eternity Is Not Self-Subsistent
Sanusi refutes the claim that sharing pre-eternity implies multiple gods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why sharing the attribute of pre-eternity does not imply multiple gods, because pre-eternity is not a self-subsistent attribute intrinsic to the essence.

Core Idea
Pre-eternity is not intrinsic; it can be conceived apart from the essence.

Sanusi addresses a common objection: if multiple beings share pre-eternity, does that make them gods? He argues that the objection fails because pre-eternity is not a self-subsistent attribute – it is not essential to the essence itself. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and clarifies the nature of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection claims that if multiple beings share the most specific attribute of God, pre-eternity, then they would be gods. Recognize why this seems plausible.
The objection relies on the assumption that pre-eternity is an intrinsic, defining attribute.
2
Learn the concept of self-subsistent attribute
Sanusi defines a self-subsistent attribute as one without which the essence cannot be conceived. Note that pre-eternity does not meet this criterion.
Example: animality for a human – you cannot conceive a human without animality.
3
Examine Sanusi's evidence
He proves pre-eternity is not self-subsistent by pointing out that we can conceive the essence's existence before conceiving its pre-eternity.
This shows pre-eternity is not intrinsic to the essence.
4
Apply to the objection
Since pre-eternity is not a self-subsistent attribute, sharing it does not imply multiple essences. Therefore, the objection is invalid.
Sanusi's refutation preserves the unity of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما ألزموهُ مِنْ تعدُّدِ الألوهِيَّةِ بسبب اشتراكها في أخص صفاتِ الإله ؛ وهو القدمُ : ففاسدٌ ؛ لأنَّ القدمَ ليس صفة نفسيَّة ؛ بدليل تعقل وجود الذاتِ قبلَ تعقل قدمها ، والأخص لا يكون إلا صفةً نفسيَّة لا يمكن تعقُلُ الذاتِ بدونها ؛ كالحيوانيَّة للإنسان ، بل هو أخص الصفاتِ النفسيَّةِ ؛ كالناطقيَّة للإنسان
And as for what they forced upon them of the multiplicity of divinity due to their sharing the most specific attribute of God, which is pre-eternity: it is corrupt; because pre-eternity is not a self-subsistent attribute (sifa nafsiyya), as evidenced by the conception of the existence of the essence before the conception of its pre-eternity. And the most specific attribute cannot be except a self-subsistent attribute which the essence cannot be conceived without; like animality for man. Rather, it is the most specific of the self-subsistent attributes; like rationality for man.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage refutes an objection: if multiple beings share the attribute of pre-eternity (qidam), which is the most specific attribute of God, then there would be multiple gods. Sanusi argues this is invalid because pre-eternity is not a self-subsistent attribute (sifa nafsiyya). A self-subsistent attribute is one without which the essence cannot be conceived, like animality for a human (you cannot conceive a human without animality). Pre-eternity, however, is not like that; you can conceive of the existence of the essence without first conceiving its pre-eternity. This shows that pre-eternity is not intrinsic to the essence in the way that rational attributes are. So sharing pre-eternity does not imply multiple essences; it is merely a relational description.

Key Terms
القدم
صفة نفسية
أخص الصفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Pre-eternity is an intrinsic positive attribute of the essence.
Correction: Pre-eternity is not intrinsic; you can conceive the essence without it. It is a relational or negative attribute.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi say that pre-eternity is not a self-subsistent attribute (sifa nafsiyya)?
A) Because it is accidental
B) Because the essence can be conceived without it
C) Because it is an attribute of action
D) Because it is shared with animals

Key Takeaway
Sharing pre-eternity does not entail multiple gods because pre-eternity is not an intrinsic essential attribute; it is merely a description of non-beginning existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that pre-eternity is not an intrinsic attribute of God—it merely describes that He has no beginning. When you think of God, do you sometimes reduce Him to a set of descriptions (like 'the Eternal') rather than recognizing that His essence is beyond what you can conceive? How can you shift your worship to focus on His unknowable essence, not just His attributes? Commit to one specific change in your daily remembrance that reflects this.
?
The polytheists' objection assumed that sharing a description makes things identical. Where in your life do you mistakenly define yourself or others by temporary or shared traits (e.g., status, achievements) rather than by your unique, God-given essence? How can you start seeing yourself and others as God sees—beyond labels? What is one judgment you need to let go of this week?
?
Sanusi's refutation protects tawhid from a subtle intellectual shirk. Search your heart: Are there any 'gods' you have elevated by giving them attributes that belong only to God—like ultimate control, eternal significance, or absolute trust? What is one thing you are holding onto as if it were self-subsistent and necessary? Surrender it to God alone in your next prayer.

The Four Methods of Logical Connection Between Attributes
Sanusi enumerates four methods for proving attribute connection and gives examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four methods (causation, conditionality, essence, rational evidence) used in kalam to prove the necessary connection between divine attributes and the underlying attributes of meaning.

Core Idea
Rational necessity in the witnessed world must apply to the unseen as well.

Sanusi now moves from establishing the general framework of attributes to providing the logical tools that connect them. He introduces four methods—causation, conditionality, essence, and rational evidence—that demonstrate how an attribute like 'being knowing' necessarily implies the attribute of 'knowledge'. These methods are essential for extending arguments from the observable world (shahid) to God (gha'ib). The passage below defines these methods and gives concrete examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the English translation. Note that Sanusi first states the general rule about extending rational necessity, then lists the four methods with examples.
Pay attention to the structured flow: rule → list → examples.
2
Identify the four methods
Look for the names of each method in the Arabic: التعليل, الشرطية, الحقيقة, الدلالة العقلية. Understand how each method proves the connection between a mnemic attribute and an attribute of meaning.
The examples illustrate each method clearly.
3
Understand the logical necessity
Notice that Sanusi emphasizes that once the connection is established in the witnessed world, it must also hold for God, because rational necessity (اللزوم العقلي) cannot be broken. Reflect on why this is important for kalam arguments.
4
Apply the method to a new attribute
Try to use one of the four methods to connect another attribute pair, like 'powerful' and 'power', just as the passage does for 'knowing' and 'knowledge'.
This reinforces the conceptual tool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولمَّا تقرَّرَتِ الملازمة عقلاً بينَ الصفاتِ المعنوية وبين صفاتِ المعاني في الشاهدِ بطريقِ التعليلِ ، أو الشرطيَّة ، أو الحقيقة ، أو الدَّلالة العقليَّةِ .. وجبَ طرد تلك الملازمة شاهداً وغائباً ؛ إذ اللزوم العقلي لا يمكن تخلفه بوجْهِ مِنَ الوجوه .
وتسمى بالجوامع الأربعة ، وإليك أمثلتها :
طريق الجمع بالتعليل : كقولهم: العلم والعالمية متلازمان ، والعالمية مرتبة على العلم ، فلو صح وجود عالمية ولا علم .. لصح وجود علم ولا عالمية ، وهم لا يقولون به .
طريق الجمع بالشرط : كقولهم : الله تعالى مريد ، وكل مريد قاصد لفعله ، والقصد مشروط بالعلم ، فالله تعالى له علم ، وإلا لثبت المشروط بدون الشرط .
طريق الجمع بالحقيقة : كقولهم : العالِمُ في الشاهد : من له علم ، أو ذو العلم ، والله تعالى عالِمٌ ؛ فله علمٌ ، وهذا عمدة من ينفي الأحوال .
طريق الجمع بالدليل العقلي : كقولهم : الإحكام في الشاهد دليل على أن لفاعله علماً به ، والله تعالى مُحْكِم متقن لأفعاله ، فدل على أن له علماً
And when the mutual necessity is established rationally between the mnemic attributes and the attributes of meaning in the witnessed, by way of causation (ta'lil), or conditionality (shartiyya), or essence (haqiqa), or rational evidence (dalala 'aqliyya), it is necessary to extend that mutual necessity to the witnessed and the unseen; for rational necessity cannot be left behind in any way. And they are called the four comprehensive methods, and here are their examples: The method of combination by causation: like their saying: knowledge and being-knowing are mutually necessary, and being-knowing is dependent on knowledge, so if it were valid for being-knowing to exist without knowledge, then it would be valid for knowledge to exist without being-knowing, but they do not say that. The method of combination by condition: like their saying: God, exalted, is willing, and every willing agent intends his act, and intention is conditioned upon knowledge, so God, exalted, has knowledge; otherwise the conditioned would be established without its condition. The method of combination by essence: like their saying: The knower in the witnessed is one who has knowledge, or possesses knowledge, and God, exalted, is knowing; so He has knowledge, and this is the foundation of those who deny the states (ahwal). The method of combination by rational evidence: like their saying: Precision in the witnessed is evidence that its agent has knowledge of it, and God, exalted, is precise and perfects His acts, so that indicates that He has knowledge.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the necessary connection between mnemic attributes (like being knowing) and attributes of meaning (like knowledge). Sanusi states that once this connection is established rationally in the witnessed world via one of four methods — causation (ta'lil), conditionality (shartiyya), essence (haqiqa), or rational evidence (dalala 'aqliyya) — it must be extended to the unseen world as well, because rational necessity (luzum 'aqli) cannot lapse. He then provides examples of each method. The causal method shows that 'knowledge' and 'being-knowing' are mutually necessary; if one could exist without the other, the relationship would be incoherent. The conditional method: God is willing, and will requires intention, which requires knowledge, so God must have knowledge, otherwise a condition would be absent while its conditioned exists. The essential method: a knower is defined as one who has knowledge; God is called 'knowing' in the Qur'an, so He must have knowledge. The rational evidence method: the precision evident in creation proves that the Creator has knowledge of His creation. These four methods (al-jawami' al-arba'a) are standard kalam arguments for establishing divine attributes.

Key Terms
ملازمة
لزوم عقلي
الجوامع الأربعة
التعليل
الشرطية
الحقيقة
الدلالة العقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that rational arguments from the witnessed world do not apply to God because He is transcendent and unlike creation.
Correction: Sanusi asserts that rational necessity (اللزوم العقلي) is universal and cannot be broken; therefore, what is necessarily true in the witnessed world must also be true for God, unless there is a clear difference (which there isn't in these categorical relations).

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the consequence of establishing the rational necessity between attributes in the witnessed?
A) It only applies to the witnessed
B) It must be extended to the unseen
C) It is hypothetical
D) It is based on tradition

Key Takeaway
The four comprehensive methods (al-jawami' al-arba'a) provide rational proofs that divine attributes must be real and connected necessarily to God, based on universal logical principles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you call yourself 'knowing' (as in 'I know something'), do you ever pause to consider what that implies about the reality of knowledge within you? If you take that connection for granted, what does your indifference toward God's perfect knowledge say about your reverence for Him? Commit today to reflecting on one attribute of God every morning.
?
The method of rational evidence says that every precise act points to a knowing agent. Look at your own life—your health, your family, your circumstances. Do you truly see these as proofs of God's knowledge, or do you treat them as random? What would change in your gratitude and trust if you saw each detail as a deliberate sign of His perfect knowledge? Write down one thing today for which you can honestly say 'This is evidence of God's knowledge.'
?
Sanusi warns that rational necessity cannot be broken. If you believe that God is 'Most Merciful', do you also believe that His mercy has a real meaning and is connected to His essence necessarily, or do you reduce it to a feeling? This lesson challenges you to not just name God's attributes but to affirm their reality and necessity. Which attribute of God do you most struggle to believe is truly real and necessary? Ask yourself: does that struggle reveal a lack of trust in His perfection?

The Eternal Attribute of Divine Power
Sanusi defines eternal power as God's power alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'eternal power' in Islamic creed refers specifically to God's power, not to any created power.

Core Idea
Eternal power belongs exclusively to God, not to animals.

Sanusi has just finished a foundational discussion and now turns to the attribute of divine power. He gives a precise definition that prevents confusion between the Creator's power and that of His creatures. This short passage sets the stage for deeper discussions about God's omnipotence.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Sanusi first says 'when you have known this' to connect to previous material, then directly defines the term.
The phrase 'al-qudra al-azaliyya' is the key term.
2
Identify the two kinds of power
The passage contrasts two powers: eternal (azaliyya) and originated (haditha). Note which one belongs to God and which to animals.
This distinction is crucial for tawhid.
3
Reflect on the theological importance
Ask yourself: why does Sanusi need to specify that 'eternal power' is only God's? What confusion would arise if this distinction were not made?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a definition. Sanusi concludes the previous discussion and transitions to the attribute of power (qudra). He clarifies that when the creed mentions 'al-qudra al-azaliyya' (the eternal power), it means the pre-eternal (qadima) power of God, not the temporal originated (haditha) power that belongs to animals. This distinction prevents confusion between divine omnipotence and created power.

Correction: Sanusi explicitly states that 'eternal power' means the pre-eternal power of God alone, distinguishing it from the temporally originated power of animals.

The Most Specific Self-Attribute
Sanusi defines the most specific self-attribue with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of the 'most specific self-attribute' and how it differs from other attributes, using the examples of animality and rationality for humans.

Core Idea
The most specific self-attribute is what makes a thing what it uniquely is.

Sanusi introduces a precise theological distinction: some attributes are so essential to an essence that without them the essence cannot even be conceived. Among these, the 'most specific' is the one that defines the unique identity of a being. In this passage, he illustrates this with the examples of animality and rationality for human beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully and its literal translation. Notice the logical flow: first a statement about existence and pre-eternity, then a definition of self-attribute, then the definition of the most specific self-attribute with examples.
The passage is concise but packed with meaning.
2
Identify the key distinction
Sanusi distinguishes between attributes that can be conceived separately from the essence (like existence) and those that cannot (self-attributes). The self-attribute is necessary for the very conception of the essence.
Existence is not a self-attribute because it is shared by all existents.
3
Grasp the 'most specific' level
The most specific self-attribute is even narrower: it defines the unique kind of the essence. For humans, animality is a self-attribute (shared with animals), but rationality is the most specific self-attribute (unique to humans).
Rationality distinguishes humans from all other animals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعقل وجود الذاتِ قبلَ تعقل قدمها ، والأخص لا يكون إلا صفةً نفسيَّة لا يمكن تعقُلُ الذاتِ بدونها ؛ كالحيوانيَّة للإنسان ، بل هو أخص الصفاتِ النفسيَّةِ ؛ كالناطقيَّة للإنسان
The conception of the existence of the essence precedes the conception of its pre-eternity. And the more specific [attribute] is nothing but a self-attribute without which the essence cannot be conceived, like animality for man; rather it is the most specific of the self-attributes, like rationality for man.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage defines the most specific self-attribute (أخص الصفات النفسية). It first distinguishes between attributes that can be conceived separately from the essence (like existence, which is conceived before pre-eternity) and those that cannot be separated (self-attributes). The self-attribute is necessary for the concept of the essence, e.g., animality is necessary to conceive 'man'. Then it states that the most specific self-attribute is an even narrower necessary attribute, exemplified by rationality (الناطقيَّة) for humans, which distinguishes them from other animals.

Key Terms
self-attribute (صفة نفسية)
most specific self-attribute (أخص الصفات النفسية)
animality (الحيوانية)
rationality (الناطقية)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that existence is the most specific attribute of a thing.
Correction: Existence is not a self-attribute at all; it is conceived separately and shared by all existents. The most specific self-attribute is something like rationality, which uniquely defines the essence.

Checkpoint

A) Existence
B) Animality
C) Rationality
D) Power

Key Takeaway
The most specific self-attribute is the attribute that uniquely defines an essence, such as rationality for humans.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What is the most specific self-attribute that defines you as a unique soul before Allah? Are you cultivating that attribute, or are you letting it be buried under shared, lower attributes like animality? Commit to one practice today that sharpens your rationality towards knowing your Creator.
?
If rationality (الناطقية) is what sets humans apart, then every moment you waste your intellect on trivialities is a betrayal of your very essence. What specific distraction will you eliminate this week to use your reason for what matters most—understanding Allah's signs and commands?
?
The passage teaches that the existence of your essence is conceived before its pre-eternity. Do you live as if your existence is a given, or do you constantly remind yourself that your very being is a gift from the Eternal? What will you do today to make your existence a continuous act of gratitude?

The Four Methods of Establishing Attribute Correlation
Sanusi explains the principle of necessary correlation and lists four methods with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle of necessary correlation between divine attributes and the four complementary methods used to prove it.

Core Idea
Four rational methods prove that divine attributes necessarily correlate with their states.

Sanusi introduces a foundational principle in Islamic theology: the necessary correlation (ملازمة) between a divine attribute (like knowledge) and its corresponding state (like being knowledgeable). Since this correlation is observed rationally in the created world, it must also hold for God. To demonstrate this, theologians developed four distinct but complementary methods, each approaching the correlation from a different logical angle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a general principle followed by four methods with examples.
The footnote marker (١) indicates that the methods are listed separately.
2
Understand the principle of correlation
The first sentence states that correlation is rationally established in the witnessed realm. This is key: we observe that knowledge and being knowledgeable always go together, so they must also go together for God.
3
Examine each of the four methods
Study each method and its example. Note how each method uses a different logical relationship: causal explanation, conditionality, essential definition, and rational indication.
The methods are complementary, not competing.
4
Apply the methods to other attributes
Try to apply the same reasoning to other attributes like will and power. Think about how each method would demonstrate that God has will because He is willing.
5
Check your understanding
Complete the checkpoint quiz and the activity to reinforce your grasp of the four methods.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولمَّا تقرَّرَتِ الملازمة عقلاً بينَ الصفاتِ المعنوية وبين صفاتِ المعاني في الشاهدِ بطريقِ التعليلِ ، أو الشرطيَّة ، أو الحقيقة ، أو الدَّلالة العقليَّة (١).. وجبَ طرد تلك الملازمة شاهداً وغائباً ؛ إذ اللزوم العقلي لا يمكن تخلفه بوجْهِ مِنَ الوجوه .
(١) وتسمى بالجوامع الأربعة ، وإليك أمثلتها :
طريق الجمع بالتعليل : كقولهم: العلم والعالمية متلازمان ، والعالمية مرتبة على العلم ، فلو صح وجود عالمية ولا علم .. لصح وجود علم ولا عالمية ، وهم لا يقولون به
طريق الجمع بالشرط : كقولهم : الله تعالى مريد ، وكل مريد قاصد لفعله ،
والقصد مشروط بالعلم ، فالله تعالى له علم ، وإلا لثبت المشروط بدون الشرط
طريق الجمع بالحقيقة : كقولهم : العالِمُ في الشاهد : من له علم ، أو ذو العلم ، والله تعالى عالِمٌ ؛ فله علمٌ ، وهذا عمدة من ينفي الأحوال
طريق الجمع بالدليل العقلي : كقولهم : الإحكام في الشاهد دليل على أن لفاعله علماً به ، والله تعالى مُحْكِم متقن لأفعاله ، فدل على أن له علماً
And when the correlation was rationally established between the attributes of meaning and the attributes of states in the witnessed realm, by way of causal explanation, or conditionality, or essential definition, or rational indication (1)… it became necessary to extend that correlation to both the witnessed and the unseen; for rational entailment cannot be violated in any way.
(1) They are called the four comprehensive methods, and here are their examples:
The method of collection by causal explanation: such as their saying: knowledge and being knowledgeable are necessarily concomitant, and being knowledgeable is dependent on knowledge; so if it were valid for there to be being knowledgeable without knowledge, then it would be valid for there to be knowledge without being knowledgeable, and they do not say that.
The method of collection by condition: such as their saying: God Almighty is willing, and every willing being intends his action, and intention is conditioned by knowledge; so God Almighty has knowledge, otherwise the conditioned would exist without the condition.
The method of collection by essential definition: such as their saying: the knower in the witnessed realm is one who has knowledge, or the possessor of knowledge; and God Almighty is a knower, so He has knowledge. This is the reliance of those who deny states.
The method of collection by rational indication: such as their saying: precision in the witnessed realm is evidence that its agent has knowledge of it; and God Almighty is the precise, perfect maker of His actions, so that indicates that He has knowledge.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage establishes the principle of necessary correlation (ملازمة) between divine attributes of meaning (صفات معنوية, like knowledge) and attributes of states (صفات معاني, like being knowledgeable). It states that this correlation is rational and observed in the created world, so it must also apply to God. The footnote then provides four methods (called الجوامع الأربعة) used to argue for this correlation, each with an example:
1. By causal explanation (تعليل): showing mutual necessity.
2. By condition (شرط): showing that one is a condition for the other.
3. By essential definition (حقيقة): showing that the state is defined by the attribute.
4. By rational indication (دليل عقلي): using evidence from effect to cause.
The passage underscores that rational entailment cannot fail.

Key Terms
ملازمة
صفات معنوية
صفات معاني
الجوامع الأربعة
تعليل
شرط
حقيقة
دلالة عقلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The four methods are competing and only one is valid.
Correction: The methods are complementary; each approaches the same correlation from a different logical perspective, and together they reinforce the argument.

Checkpoint
Which method uses the principle that if the conditioned exists, the condition must exist?
A) الجمع بالتعليل
B) الجمع بالشرط
C) الجمع بالحقيقة
D) الجمع بالدليل العقلي

Key Takeaway
The four comprehensive methods (الجوامع الأربعة) provide complementary rational proofs that a divine attribute must exist if its corresponding state is affirmed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that God's knowledge is rationally necessary from His actions. In what area of your life are you still acting as if God does not see or know, and when will you stop that today?
?
The four methods prove that every divine attribute must match its state. If you claim to believe in God's knowledge but live carelessly, are you not contradicting your own claim? What will you change right now?
?
These arguments are rational proofs, not blind faith. Do you rely on them as the foundation of your belief, or do you depend on emotions? Are you willing to doubt your doubts and submit to this logical necessity?

Definition of Eternal Power
Sanusi defines 'eternal power' as God's eternal attribute, distinguishing it from created power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'eternal power' in Sanusi's text refers exclusively to God's pre-eternal attribute, not to any created power.

Core Idea
Eternal power is uniquely divine, not shared by creatures.

Sanusi begins his discussion by defining a key term: 'eternal power.' This is not merely a philosophical concept but a precise theological distinction. In this short passage, he clarifies that this power belongs only to God, setting it apart from the temporal power found in animals and other creatures. Understanding this distinction is foundational for avoiding anthropomorphism and preserving divine uniqueness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the rhythm, then read the English translation. Notice how the term 'eternal' is immediately clarified by 'pre-eternal'.
The passage is very short; read it slowly.
2
Identify the two types of power
The passage distinguishes between two powers. Find them: one is eternal (pre-eternal) and belongs to God; the other is created (temporal) and belongs to animals.
Contrast: قديمة vs حادثة.
3
Understand the significance of 'pre-eternal'
The word 'قديمة' means 'pre-eternal' or 'without beginning.' This emphasizes that God's power is not something that came into existence; it is an essential attribute.
This distinguishes God from all creatures, whose powers begin.
4
Reflect on why this matters
Consider why Sanusi begins with this definition. If we attribute power to God in the same sense as created power, we risk comparing God to His creation. This definition guards against that error.
This connects to the broader topic of divine attributes.

The definition is straightforward: eternal power is uniquely divine, not shared by creatures.

Divine Power Brings About Both Existence and Non-Existence
Sanusi argues that eternal power brings about non-existence as well as existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine power is not limited to bringing about existence; it also brings about non-existence, and the key condition for an effect of power is that it be temporal (new), not necessarily existent.

Core Idea
Non-existence can be an effect of divine power as long as it is newly occurring.

Sanusi continues his discussion on divine power by addressing a subtle but crucial point: can God’s eternal power bring about non-existence? Some theologians thought only existing things could be effects of power. This passage refutes that, showing that the real criterion is temporality, not existence. Let’s examine his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation to get a general sense of the argument.
Notice the key terms: إيجاد, إعدام, العدم الطاري.
2
Identify the key claim about divine power
Sanusi states that divine power can bring about both existence and non-existence. What is the significance of this claim?
3
Understand the four possible conditions
The passage lists four possibilities for what validates the effect of eternal power on accidental non-existence. List them and see why they all apply.
These are: possibility with temporality, possibility conditioned by temporality, temporality alone, possibility alone.
4
Contrast Sanusi’s view with Imam al-Haramayn
Sanusi rejects the view that the effect must be an existent. The key condition is that it be temporal and renewed. Understand the difference.
Imam al-Haramayn held that the effect must be existent; Sanusi says it can be non-existent as long as it is new.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( يتأتى بها إيجادُ كلِّ ممكن وإعدامه ) يعني : يتيسر بها إخراج كل ممكن مِنَ العدم إلى الوجودِ ، وإخراجُهُ مِنَ الوجودِ إلى العدم . وقد مرَّ القولُ في جعل العدمِ الطاري أثراً للقدرةِ الأزلية مباشرةً على مذهب القاضي ، وهو الأصح في النظرِ (۲) ؛ لأنَّ المصحِّحَ لتأثير القدرةِ الأزليَّة إن قلنا : هو الإمكانُ معَ الحدوثِ ، أو الإمكانُ بشرط الحدوث ، أو الحدوث فقط ، أو الإمكان فقط (۳) .. فذلك كلُّه محقق ثابت للعدم الطارئ ، ولا يلزمُ في أثر القدرة أن يكون وجودياً كما صارَ إليهِ إمام الحرمينِ بل إنَّما يلزمُ فِيهِ أنْ يكونَ مُتجدِّداً حادثاً ، كانَ ذلك المتجدِّدُ وجوديّاً أو عدميّاً ، وهذا هو الحق الذي لا شكّ فيه ، والله تعالى أعلم .
His statement: 'by which is possible the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation' means: by which is facilitated the bringing out of every possible thing from non-existence into existence, and bringing it out from existence into non-existence. And the discussion has passed regarding making the accidental non-existence an effect of the eternal power directly, according to the madhhab of al-Qadi, and it is the soundest in consideration; because the corrector for the effect of eternal power, if we say: it is possibility together with temporality, or possibility conditioned by temporality, or temporality alone, or possibility alone (3) … then all of that is realized and established for the accidental non-existence. And it is not necessary in the effect of power that it be existent, as Imam al-Haramayn came to hold; rather it is necessary in it that it be renewed and temporal, whether that renewed thing is existent or non-existent. And this is the truth about which there is no doubt, and God Almighty knows best.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument about the scope of divine power. It begins by explicating the phrase 'by which is possible the bringing into existence of every possible thing and its annihilation' (يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن وإعدامه). Sanusi explains that this means power can bring anything from non-being to being and from being to non-being. He then references a previous discussion (possibly from earlier in the work) regarding accidental non-existence (العدم الطاري) being directly an effect of eternal power, following the view of al-Qadi al-Baqillani, which he considers the most correct. The argument proceeds: the factor that validates the effect of eternal power—whether we say it is possibility together with temporality, or possibility conditioned by temporality, or temporality alone, or possibility alone—all these are realized for accidental non-existence. Therefore, it is not necessary that the effect of power be an existent, as Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) claimed. Rather, the necessary condition is that the effect be temporal/renewed (متجدداً حادثاً), regardless of whether that renewed thing is an existent or a non-existent. Sanusi declares this the undeniable truth.

Key Terms
إيجاد
إعدام
العدم الطاري
أثر القدرة
حادث
متجدد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That only existing things can be effects of divine power.
Correction: The effect of power can be non-existence, as long as it is newly occurring (temporal).

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the necessary characteristic for an effect of divine power?
A) It must be an existent entity
B) It must be a possible entity
C) It must be temporal and renewed
D) It must be a substance

Key Takeaway
Divine power can bring about non-existence, as long as that non-existence is a new, temporal event.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's power brings about both existence and non-existence as direct acts, then every loss you experience is not a random absence but a deliberate creation of non-existence by Him. How does that reframe the way you grieve or hold onto things? What might He be teaching you through a loss you are currently facing?
?
The passage insists that what matters is not whether something exists, but whether it is temporally renewed by Allah's power. In your own spiritual life, are you more focused on preserving a static state of belief or on constantly renewing your iman? What practical step can you take today to seek a fresh renewal of your faith?
?
You believe that nothing in the universe escapes Allah's power—every atom's existence and non-existence is directly from Him. Then why do you still fear losing something as if its continuation depends on you? Are you willing to truly hand over control of every coming and going in your life?

Divine Power and Non-Existence as Its Effect
Sanusi defines divine power and argues for non-existence as a direct effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine power can directly bring about non-existence, and why this view is considered more correct in theological reasoning.

Core Idea
Divine power's effect is any new thing, existent or non-existent.

Sanusi begins this passage by defining divine power in terms of its effect: bringing every possible thing into and out of existence. He then addresses a key theological question: can non-existence be a direct effect of God's power? The passage defends the view of al-Qadi al-Baqillani against Imam al-Haramayn, grounding it in the conditions that make an effect valid.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Notice that Sanusi defines divine power by its capacity to both bring into existence and take out of existence.
2
Identify the theological disagreement
Sanusi mentions two positions: al-Qadi al-Baqillani (non-existence can be an effect) and Imam al-Haramayn (only existents). Understand the stakes.
Imam al-Haramayn required the effect to be an existing thing.
3
Examine the 'corrector' theories
Sanusi lists four formulations of what makes an effect valid: possibility with temporality, possibility conditioned by temporality, temporality alone, or possibility alone. Notice how he argues that all apply to accidental non-existence.
This is a key move in the argument.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Sanusi concludes that the effect must be temporally new (ḥādith), not necessarily existent. This is the truth without doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( يتأتى بها إيجادُ كلِّ ممكن وإعدامه ) يعني : يتيسر بها إخراج كل ممكن مِنَ العدم إلى الوجودِ ، وإخراجُهُ مِنَ الوجودِ إلى العدم . وقد مرَّ القولُ في جعل العدمِ الطاري أثراً للقدرةِ الأزلية مباشرةً (1) على مذهب القاضي ، وهو الأصح في النظر (۲) ; لأنَّ المصحِّحَ لتأثير القدرةِ الأزليَّة إن قلنا : هو الإمكانُ معَ الحدوثِ ، أو الإمكانُ بشرط الحدوث ، أو الحدوث فقط ، أو الإمكان فقط (۳) .. فذلك كلُّه محقق ثابت للعدم الطارئ ، ولا يلزمُ في أثر القدرة أن يكون وجودياً كما صارَ إليهِ إمام الحرمينِ بل إنَّما يلزمُ فِيهِ أنْ يكونَ مُتجدِّداً حادثاً ، كانَ ذلك المتجدِّدُ وجوديّاً أو عدميّاً ، وهذا هو الحق الذي (٤) لا شكّ فيه ، والله تعالى أعلم .
His statement: (by which [power] every possible thing's bringing into existence and bringing into non-existence is accomplished) means: by it easily occurs the extraction of every possible thing from non-existence into existence, and its extraction from existence into non-existence. And the statement has already passed concerning making the accidental non-existence an effect of the eternal power directly (1) according to the school of al-Qadi, and it is the more correct in consideration (2); because the corrector for the effect of the eternal power, if we say: it is possibility with temporality, or possibility conditioned by temporality, or temporality alone, or possibility alone (3) ... then all of that is realized and established for the accidental non-existence, and it is not necessary in the effect of power that it be existential, as Imam al-Haramayn inclined to; rather, what is necessary in it is that it be renewed and temporal, whether that renewed thing is existential or non-existential. And this is the truth about which (4) there is no doubt, and God Most High knows best.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage defines divine power as that by which the bringing into existence and non-existence of every possible thing is accomplished. It then argues that the effect of power need not be an existing entity, but must be something new (ḥādith). The author supports the view of al-Qadi al-Baqillani against Imam al-Haramayn who required the effect to be existent. He considers various theories about what corrects the effect (the corrector: possibility with temporality, etc.) and concludes that all these conditions are met for accidental non-existence, so it can be an effect. The key point: the effect of power is any temporally new thing, whether existent or non-existent.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think divine power only produces existents.
Correction: This passage clarifies that non-existence can be a direct effect, as the effect must be temporally new, not necessarily existent.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the necessary condition for something to be an effect of divine power?
A) That it be an existent thing.
B) That it be possible and temporally new.
C) That it be eternal.
D) That it be accidental.

Key Takeaway
The effect of divine power is any temporally new thing, regardless of whether it is existent or non-existent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God’s power directly brings about both your existence and the moments when things cease to exist in your life, how does that change the way you respond to loss or disappointment? Can you name a specific loss you have been resenting, and are you willing to see it as a deliberate act of divine power rather than mere accident?
?
The author insists that the effect of divine power must be temporally new. Your life is filled with countless 'temporal news'—each breath, each thought, each action. Do you live as though each moment is sustained directly by God’s power? What would change in your daily routine if you truly believed that?
?
Imam al-Haramayn thought only existents could be God's effect. You might similarly assume God is only involved when things appear good or exist. When have you acted as though God is absent from the 'non-existences' in your life—the silences, the removals, the endings? Are you willing to worship a God who is sovereign over both giving and taking?

The Prior Non-Existence Is Within God's Power
Sanusi defends that prior possible non-existence is directly within God's power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi considers the prior possible non-existence to be within God's power and why the objection against it is invalid.

Core Idea
God's power truly encompasses even the non-existence that precedes creation.

Sanusi continues his discussion on divine power by addressing a specific case: the state of non-existence that exists before something is created. Some might think that because non-existence is not a 'thing', it cannot be an object of power. Sanusi rejects this, showing that God's power is real and covers preservation and removal of non-existence itself.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Recognize that 'prior possible non-existence' refers to the state of a thing before it is created. Sanusi argues this state is directly within God's power.
This non-existence is not absolute nothingness, but a specific state that precedes creation.
2
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two main parts: the claim that non-existence is within God's power, and the refutation of the objection.
3
Analyze the linguistic argument
Sanusi uses the example of a king having power over people metaphorically. How does this support the claim that God's power over non-existence is real, not metaphorical?
He argues that if metaphorical power is used for lesser things, then real power should apply here.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Sanusi labels the objection as 'bad manners' because it implies a deficiency in God's power. Why is this a serious charge?
In kalam, denying an attribute of perfection is a grave error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ذهبَ بعضُ الأئمَّةِ المحققينَ إلى أنَّ العدم الممكن السابق عن وجودِ الحوادثِ فيما لا يزال (۱) .. مقدور للباري تبارك وتعالى ; كالعدم والوجودِ الطارئينِ ; بمعنى : أنَّهُ في قبضة قدرتِهِ تعالى يتأتّى منه جل وعلا إبقاؤُهُ ، وإزالته بجعل الوجودِ الحادثِ في مكانه . وإطلاق المقدوريَّةِ بأقلَّ مِنْ هذا مستعمل في اللغةِ والعُرْفِ (۲) ; يُقالُ : الملك يقدر على الناس ولا يقدرون عليه ; بمعنى : أَنَّهُ يملكُ على سبيل المجاز تغيير بعض أحوالهم ; كإعزاز أو إذلال ونحوهما . فكيف لا يُطلَقُ على ذلك العدمِ الممكن أنَّه مقدور الله تعالى ؟! فإنه جل وعلا يملكُ إبقاءَهُ وتغييره بما شاءَ وكيف شاء على الحقيقة لا على المجاز (۳) ، فمَلْءُ الفم بأنَّه ليس مقدوراً للمولى تبارك وتعالى ; نظراً إلى أنَّ حقيقته ليسَتْ بوجوديَّةٍ ولا طارئة . . سوء أدب ; بإطلاقِ ما يُوهم عجزاً في قدرته جل وعلا(٤)
And some of the verifying imams went to the view that the possible non-existence which precedes the coming-into-being of events in what is yet to come (1) ... is within the power of the Creator, Blessed and Exalted; like the accidental non-existence and existence; meaning: that it is in the grasp of His power, Exalted; from Him, may He be Glorified, its preservation and its removal by placing temporal existence in its place are facilitated. And the use of the term 'being in power' (al-maqdūriyya) with less than this is customary in language and common usage (2); it is said: the king has power over the people and they do not have power over him; meaning: that he possesses, metaphorically, the ability to change some of their states, like giving honor or humiliation and the like. So how is it not applied to that possible non-existence that it is within the power of God Most High?! For He, Glorified and Exalted, possesses its preservation and its change however He wills and in whatever manner He wills, in reality, not metaphorically (3). So, filling the mouth by saying that it is not within the power of the Lord Blessed and Exalted, considering that its reality is neither existential nor accidental ... is bad manners, by uttering what implies inability in His power, Glorified and Exalted (4).
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage extends the argument about non-existence as an effect of power to the specific case of the possible non-existence that precedes the coming into existence of events (such as the non-existence of a thing before it is created). The author asserts that this prior non-existence is within God's power just like accidental non-existence and existence. He clarifies that 'being in power' (al-maqdūriyya) in its full sense applies here, even though worldly language uses it metaphorically in lesser cases. The objection that non-existence cannot be an object of power because it is not existent is refuted: God truly has power to preserve it or replace it with existence. Denying this implies deficiency in God's power, which is improper.

Misconception: Non-existence cannot be an object of power because it is not a thing.
Correction: God's power truly encompasses non-existence; He can preserve or remove it. Denying this implies a deficiency in His power.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it not a proper objection to say that prior non-existence is not within God's power?
A) Because it is impossible for non-existence to be an object of power.
B) Because God's power is only metaphorical in relation to non-existence.
C) Because non-existence is in the grasp of God's power and He can preserve or change it.
D) Because the prior non-existence is not possible.

Key Takeaway
Prior non-existence is truly within God's power; denying this is bad manners because it implies a limitation in God's power.

?
God's power over even the non-existence of your own being before you were born is real. How does this truth affect your sense of dependence on Him every moment? What would it mean for you to live today as if your very non-existence is in His hands?

Possible Non-Existence is Within Divine Power
Sanusi defends that possible non-existence is maqdur against objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why possible non-existence is considered within divine power according to Sanusi, and how he responds to objections that non-existence cannot be an object of power.

Core Idea
Divine power attaches to possibles, not just existents, so possible non-existence is maqdur.

Sanusi addresses a subtle but important point: can non-existence be an object of divine power? Some might think only existing things can be subject to God's power. However, Sanusi argues that the relevant criterion is possibility (imkan), not existence. He uses linguistic examples and refutes an implied objection, showing that denying maqduriyya for possible non-existence leads to implying impotence in God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the flow from the main claim to the footnote clarifications.
The passage is dense; take it slowly.
2
Identify the three kinds of non-existence
Footnote (1) explains three types: possible (ʿadam mumkin), necessary (wājib), and impossible (mustaḥīl). Possible non-existence is the one at issue.
This classification is key to understanding the scope of the argument.
3
Understand the meaning of maqdur
Sanusi explains that being an object of power means being in the grasp of God's power, such that He can preserve it or replace it with existence. He uses the analogy of a king's metaphorical power to show that applying maqdur to possible non-existence is even more fitting.
The king analogy shows the term is used for less, so for God it is literal.
4
Reflect on the implied objection and response
The passage implicitly responds to the objection: non-existence cannot be maqdur because it is not an existing thing. Sanusi argues that this reasoning is flawed and constitutes bad manners, as it implies impotence.
The phrase 'bad manners' is a strong criticism.
5
Grasp the final clarification from al-Razi and al-Ghazali
The passage ends with a quote from al-Razi clarifying that denying maqduriyya to non-existents means denying attachment of power, not that power was attached and failed. Al-Ghazali notes that when properly understood, there is no disagreement.
This shows the issue is about definition, not substance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجودِ الحوادثِ فيما لا يزال (۱) .. مقدور للباري تبارك وتعالى ؛ كالعدم والوجودِ الطارئينِ ؛ بمعنى : أنَّهُ في قبضة قدرتِهِ تعالى يتأتّى منه جل وعلا إبقاؤُهُ ، وإزالته بجعل الوجودِ الحادثِ في مكانه · وإطلاق المقدوريَّةِ بأقلَّ مِنْ هذا مستعمل في اللغةِ والعُرْفِ (۲) ؛ يُقالُ : الملك يقدرُ على الناس ولا يقدرون عليه ؛ بمعنى : أَنَّهُ يملكُ على سبيل المجاز تغيير بعض أحوالهم ؛ كإعزاز أو إذلال ونحوهما فكيف لا يُطلَقُ على ذلك العدمِ الممكن أنَّه مقدور الله تعالى ؟! فإنه جل وعلا يملكُ إبقاءَهُ وتغييره بما شاءَ وكيف شاء على الحقيقة لا على المجاز (۳) ، فمَلْءُ الفم بأنَّه ليس مقدوراً للمولى تبارك وتعالى ؛ نظراً إلى أنَّ حقيقته ليسَتْ بوجوديَّةٍ ولا طارئة . . سوء أدب ؛ بإطلاقِ ما يُوهم عجزاً في قدرته جل وعلا(٤) (۱) عدم زيدٍ عدم ممكن ، وعدم الشريك عدمٌ واجب ، وعدم القادرية لصانع العالم عدم مستحيل (۲) أراد بـ ( المقدورية ) : الصفة المعنوية للممكن المقدور ؛ وهي الكون مقدوراً ، وهذا لا خلاف فيه ، وسياقه هنا جواب عن سؤال مقدر ؛ تقديره : لا نُسلّم أن العدمَ السابق عن وجود الحوادث مقدور لله تعالى مع أن حقيقته ليست بوجودية ولا طارئة (۳) أن المقدور في قبضة القدرة ، فهذا المعنى حقيقة كما ترى لا مجاز (٤) بمعنى قال الإمام الرازي في ) معالم أصول الدين ) ( ص ۱۰۷ ) : ( والأصوب أن يقال : العلم بكون القادر قادراً على الفعل والترك . . علم ضروري ) ومع هذا : الذين يطلقون عدم المقدورية على أمر عدمي إنما يعنون به ـ ولا يخفى عن الإمام المصنف - عدم تعلق القدرة به ، لا أنها تعلقت به ولم يوجد ، وهذه المسألة يعبر عنها حجة الإسلام بأنها إذا حُرِّرت لا يتصوَّر فيها خلاف
... the existence of events in what is yet to come (1) is within the power of the Creator, blessed and exalted, like non-existence and existence that occur; meaning: it is in the grasp of His power, exalted, that He may preserve it, and remove it by placing occurring existence in its place. And the application of 'being an object of power' to less than this is used in language and custom (2); it is said: the king has power over people and they do not have power over him; meaning: he possesses, metaphorically, the ability to change some of their states, like honor or humiliation and the like. So how can that possible non-existence not be called an object of God's power? For He, exalted, truly possesses the ability to preserve it and change it as He wills and how He wills, not metaphorically (3). So to claim boldly that it is not within the power of the Master, blessed and exalted, considering that its reality is not existential nor occurring ... is bad manners, by uttering what implies impotence in His power, exalted (4). (1) The non-existence of Zayd is possible non-existence, the non-existence of a partner is necessary non-existence, and the non-existence of the ability for the Maker of the world is impossible non-existence. (2) By 'being an object of power' he means the moral attribute of the possible object of power, which is its being an object of power, and there is no disagreement about this. And his context here is a response to an implied question: 'We do not concede that the non-existence preceding the existence of events is within God's power while its reality is not existential nor occurring.' (3) [Meaning] that the object of power is in the grasp of power, so this meaning is real, as you see, not metaphorical. (4) Meaning: Imam al-Razi said in his 'Ma'alim Usul al-Din' (p. 107): 'The more correct view is that knowledge of the powerful being's ability to act and to refrain is necessary knowledge.' And despite this, those who deny being an object of power to a non-existent thing mean by that—and it is not hidden from the author—the non-attachment of power to it, not that power attached to it and it did not exist. And this issue, the Proof of Islam (al-Ghazali) expresses as: when it is properly examined, no disagreement is conceivable concerning it.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the claim that possible non-existence (al-‘adam al-mumkin) is within divine power (maqdur). It begins by asserting that the existence of future events is maqdur, as are contingent existence and non-existence. It explains that to be maqdur means to be in the grasp of power, such that the powerful being can preserve or remove it. The author then notes that the term maqdur is used in language and custom for less than this, citing the example of a king's power over his subjects—which is metaphorical. He then poses a rhetorical question: why not apply maqdur to possible non-existence, since God truly has power to preserve or change it? He strongly criticizes those who deny this, saying it implies impotence (ʿajz) and is bad manners. The embedded footnotes clarify classifications of non-existence (possible, necessary, impossible), note that the passage replies to an objection (implicit: non-existence cannot be maqdur because it is not an existing thing), and quote Imam al-Razi that the knowledge of a powerful being's ability to act or refrain is necessary. The passage concludes by clarifying that those who deny maqduriyya for non-existents mean that power does not attach to them at all, not that power attached without effect, and that this issue has no genuine disagreement when properly understood.

Key Terms
مقدور (maqdūr)
عدم ممكن (ʿadam mumkin)
قدرة (qudra)
إطلاق المقدوريَّة (iṭlāq al-maqdūriyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only existing things can be objects of divine power.
Correction: This passage shows that possible non-existence is also maqdur because power attaches to possibles (mumkin), not just existents.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on what basis is something considered an object of divine power (maqdur)?
A) The thing must exist
B) The thing must be a substance or accident
C) The thing must be possible (mumkin)
D) The thing must have previously existed

Key Takeaway
Possible non-existence is within divine power because power attaches to the possible, not the existent; denying this implies impotence and is bad manners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that your very existence is in God's grasp every moment—He can preserve you or remove you—does that make you turn to Him with gratitude and fear? What would change in your daily life if you truly felt that your next breath is not guaranteed?
?
The passage warns that denying God's power over non-existence is 'bad manners' and implies impotence. In your own heart, do you ever act as if something—your health, your plans, your loved ones—is outside God's control? How can you replace that with true reliance on His power?
?
Sanusi says that when properly understood, there is no disagreement about God's power over possible non-existence. Is there an area in your faith where you cling to a misunderstanding out of pride, unwilling to accept a deeper truth? Will you ask God to humble you and grant you clarity?

The Sole Basis for Divine Power's Attachment
Sanusi states the correct view that imkan alone suffices for eternal power's attachment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the sole basis for the attachment of God's eternal power to possibles is their intrinsic possibility (imkān), regardless of existence, non-existence, or temporal sequence.

Core Idea
Possibility alone suffices for God's power to attach to anything.

This passage presents a decisive theological point: what makes a possible thing an object of God's eternal power is simply that it is possible, not whether it exists or not. The imam (Sanusi) argues that this view is both linguistically sound and safer from implying any deficiency in God. Let's examine his concise reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author's own words set the stage.
2
Identify the key term 'muṣaḥḥiḥ'
Notice that the passage begins by stating that the 'corrector' (muṣaḥḥiḥ) of the attachment of eternal power is imkan only. Ask yourself: what does 'corrector' mean in this context?
It means the factor that validates or makes the attachment correct.
3
Understand the scope of 'every possible'
The passage explicitly includes both existent and non-existent possibles, and both prior and subsequent possibles. Make sure you see how this expands the common understanding.
This is key to the argument that possibility alone is sufficient.
4
Reflect on the evaluation
Sanusi concludes that this view is closer to language and custom, and safer from bad manners and implying deficiency. Consider why this matters in a theological context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الذي اختارَهُ هذا الإمامُ هو الآتي على أنَّ مُصحِّحَ تعلَّقِ القدرة الأزليَّة بالممكن .. الإمكانُ فقط . فكلُّ ممكن على هذا . وجوديّاً كان أو عدميّاً . سابقاً كانَ أو لاحقاً . فهو مقدور لمولانا تبارك وتعالى . ومقدوريَّةٌ كلَّ حقيقةٍ مِنْ هذه الحقائق بما يليقُ بها وهذا القولُ أقرب للُّغَةِ والعُرْفِ . وأسلمُ مِنْ سوء الأدب وإيهام النقص . والله سبحانه أعلمُ
And this which this Imam has chosen is the following: that the corrector of the attachment of eternal power to the possible is possibility (imkan) only. So every possible on this account, whether existent or non-existent, whether prior or subsequent, is an object of power (maqdur) for our Master, blessed and exalted. And the being-an-object-of-power for each of these realities is in accordance with what befits it. And this statement is closer to language and custom, and safer from bad manners and implying deficiency. And God, the Exalted, knows best.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents the chosen position of the Imam (likely Sanusi himself or another authority) regarding the condition for the attachment of divine eternal power (al-qudra al-azaliyya) to possibles. It states that the sole factor that validates (muṣaḥḥiḥ) this attachment is possibility (imkān) alone. Consequently, every possible thing—whether it is an existent or non-existent, whether it is a past, present, or future possible—is an object of power (maqdūr) for God. The phrase 'in accordance with what befits it' means that a non-existent possible is maqdūr in a way appropriate to non-existence (i.e., power to bring it into existence or leave it in non-existence), while an existent possible is maqdūr in a way appropriate to existence (power to preserve or annihilate it). The author then evaluates this view as closer to linguistic usage and custom (which includes calling non-existents maqdūr), and safer from the aforementioned bad manners and implying deficiency in God's power. The passage ends with 'Wa-Allāhu aʿlam' (God knows best), a conventional pious disclaimer.

Key Terms
قدرة أزليَّة (qudra azaliyya)
إمكان (imkān)
ممكن (mumkin)
مقدور (maqdūr)
مُصحِّح (muṣaḥḥiḥ)
مقدوريَّة (maqdūriyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only existent things can be objects of God's power.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that non-existent possibles are also maqdūr, because possibility alone is sufficient for the attachment of power.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the sole factor that validates the attachment of eternal power to a possible?
A) Its existence
B) Its non-existence
C) Its possibility (imkan)
D) Its being prior or subsequent

Key Takeaway
The attachment of God's eternal power to a possible depends solely on its possibility, not on its existence or temporal status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation that seems hopeless or impossible, do you truly believe that God's power attaches to it solely because it is possible? Or do you unconsciously limit Him by thinking 'This is too much'? What would change in your dua if you internalized that every possible is maqdur?
?
The lesson warns against 'bad manners' toward God by implying deficiency in His power. In your speech, do you ever say 'God can't do that' or 'It's impossible' without thinking? How can you train your tongue to reflect the vastness of His power as described here?
?
If you truly believed that non-existent things (like future good deeds or yet-uncreated rewards) are already objects of God's power, how would that affect your hope and effort in seeking them? What is one thing you will start asking Allah for that you previously thought was beyond reach?

Definition of Eternal Power
Sanusi defines eternal power and refutes two sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Allah's eternal power and how it refutes the Qadariyya and naturalists.

Core Idea
Allah's power creates every possible, refuting those who limit it.

Sanusi begins by defining eternal power as the attribute by which Allah brings every possible into existence. He then uses this definition to critique two deviant sects who deny the full scope of divine power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation once.
The passage includes a definition and refutations.
2
Identify the definition
Note that power is defined by what it accomplishes – bringing all possibles into existence.
3
Understand the refutations
See how the definition undermines Qadariyya (who limit God's power over animals) and naturalists (who attribute effects to nature).
These sects are refuted by the universal scope of power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله في تعريف القدرةِ الأزليَّةِ : ( يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن ) يعني : سواء كانَ جِرْماً أو عرضاً . مُكتسباً للحيوان أو غيرَ مُكتسَبٍ . ففيه تنبيه على فسادِ مذهبِ القدريَّةِ الذينَ أخرجوا أفعال الحيواناتِ الاختيارية عن تعلق قدرة الله تعالى . وعلى فسادِ مذهب الطبائعيينَ الذين أسندوا بعض الممكناتِ لقوى الطبائع العلوية والسفلية . وقوله : ( على وَفْقِ الإرادةِ ( إشارة إلى أنَّ فعلَهُ للكائناتِ إِنَّما هو بطريق الاختيار . لا بطريق اللزوم . كفعل العلة والطبيعة عند الفلاسفة والطبائعيين [ صفة الإرادة ] وقوله : ( والإرادة : صفةٌ يتأتى بها تخصيص الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليهِ ) . ا يعني : أنَّ الممكناتِ لمَّا كانَتْ نسبتها إلى قدرتِهِ تعالى على حد السواء . فلو اختصَّتْ بوجودِ بعضها دونَ بعض.. لزمَ العجز . فإذاً لا بدَّ لتخصيص بعض الممكنات بالوقوع دون مقابله .. مِنْ صفةٍ أُخرى . وليسَتْ إلا صفة الإرادة . إذْ لا يلزم نقص في قولنا :
And His statement in the definition of eternal power: 'By it the bringing into existence of every possible is accomplished' means: whether it is a substance (jirm) or an accident, acquired by the animal or not acquired. In it there is a warning against the corruption of the doctrine of the Qadariyya, who excluded the voluntary acts of animals from the attachment of God's power, and against the corruption of the doctrine of the naturalists (ṭabāʾiʿiyyūn), who attributed some possibles to the forces of the upper and lower natures. And His statement: 'In accordance with will (irāda)' is an indication that His action of bringing about beings is only by way of choice (ikhtiyār), not by way of necessity (luzūm), like the action of the cause and nature according to the philosophers and naturalists. [Attribute of Will] And His statement: 'And will is an attribute by which the specification (takhṣīṣ) of the possible to some of what is permissible for it is accomplished.' That is: since possibles are, in relation to His power, on an equal footing, if some possibles were specified for existence without others, powerlessness (ʿajz) would follow. Therefore, for the specification of some possibles to occur rather than their opposite, there must be another attribute, and it is none other than the attribute of will, since no deficiency follows from our saying: ...
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two definitions: first, the definition of eternal power (al-qudra al-azaliyya) as 'that by which the bringing into existence of every possible is accomplished.' The author explains that this includes all possible substances and accidents, whether acquired by animals or not. He then points out that this definition refutes two deviant sects: the Qadariyya (who denied God's power over animals' voluntary acts) and the naturalists (al-ṭabāʾiʿiyyūn, who attributed some events to natural forces). Next, he comments on the phrase 'in accordance with will' (ʿalā wafq al-irāda) from the definition, explaining that God's act is volitional, not necessary like the emanation of a cause. This counters philosophers and naturalists who posit a necessary emanation. The passage then introduces a separate section on the attribute of will (ṣifat al-irāda), quoting the definition: 'Will is an attribute by which the specification (takhṣīṣ) of a possible to some of its permissible states is accomplished.' The explanation follows: since all possibles are equally related to divine power, if some existed and others not without a specifying factor, it would entail impotence (ʿajz). Therefore, another attribute (will) is needed to specify which possible occurs. The passage ends mid-sentence, cut off by the page break, but the argument is clear: will is the necessary attribute that resolves the equal relation of power to possibles.

Key Terms
قدرة أزليَّة (qudra azaliyya)
قدريَّة (Qadariyya)
طبائعيّون (ṭabāʾiʿiyyūn)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which group is refuted by the statement that power brings every possible into existence?
A) The philosophers
B) The Qadariyya
C) The Ash'aris
D) The Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
Eternal power encompasses all possibles, refuting any sect that limits divine control.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every single event in your life—even your own choices—is under Allah's power? Or do you, like the Qadariyya, reserve some control for yourself? In what areas of your life do you act as if Allah's power does not reach? Will you today consciously acknowledge His power in every moment?
?
When you see natural occurrences—a sunrise, a rainstorm, your own heartbeat—do you think they happen by themselves? This lesson reminds you that even what seems natural is created by Allah. Are you attributing any aspect of your life to 'nature' or 'luck'? Will you repent and attribute all to Him?
?
The passage says Allah's action is by choice, not necessity. Do you live as though Allah's actions are arbitrary or that He is compelled by your actions? How does knowing that He acts by perfect will affect your trust in Him? Will you submit to His will, even when you don't understand?

The Attribute of Will: Necessity of Specification
Sanusi defines will and argues for its necessity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of divine will and why it is necessary to specify which possibles occur.

Core Idea
Will resolves the equal relation of power to all possibles.

After defining power, Sanusi turns to the attribute of will. He explains that because power relates equally to all possibles, another attribute is needed to specify which ones come into existence. This is the role of will.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition
Read the Arabic definition of will and its translation.
2
Understand the problem
Note that all possibles are equally within God's power, so without a specifying factor, no particular possible would be selected.
This is called the 'equal relation' problem.
3
See the solution
The attribute of will is introduced as the specifying factor.
Will is not merely knowledge or power; it is a distinct attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله في تعريف القدرةِ الأزليَّةِ : ( يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن ) يعني : سواء كانَ جِرْماً أو عرضاً . مُكتسباً للحيوان أو غيرَ مُكتسَبٍ . ففيه تنبيه على فسادِ مذهبِ القدريَّةِ الذينَ أخرجوا أفعال الحيواناتِ الاختيارية عن تعلق قدرة الله تعالى . وعلى فسادِ مذهب الطبائعيينَ الذين أسندوا بعض الممكناتِ لقوى الطبائع العلوية والسفلية . وقوله : ( على وَفْقِ الإرادةِ ( إشارة إلى أنَّ فعلَهُ للكائناتِ إِنَّما هو بطريق الاختيار . لا بطريق اللزوم . كفعل العلة والطبيعة عند الفلاسفة والطبائعيين [ صفة الإرادة ] وقوله : ( والإرادة : صفةٌ يتأتى بها تخصيص الممكن ببعض ما يجوز عليهِ ) . ا يعني : أنَّ الممكناتِ لمَّا كانَتْ نسبتها إلى قدرتِهِ تعالى على حد السواء . فلو اختصَّتْ بوجودِ بعضها دونَ بعض.. لزمَ العجز . فإذاً لا بدَّ لتخصيص بعض الممكنات بالوقوع دون مقابله .. مِنْ صفةٍ أُخرى . وليسَتْ إلا صفة الإرادة . إذْ لا يلزم نقص في قولنا :

[Attribute of Will] And His statement: 'And will is an attribute by which the specification (takhṣīṣ) of the possible to some of what is permissible for it is accomplished.' That is: since possibles are, in relation to His power, on an equal footing, if some possibles were specified for existence without others, powerlessness (ʿajz) would follow. Therefore, for the specification of some possibles to occur rather than their opposite, there must be another attribute, and it is none other than the attribute of will, since no deficiency follows from our saying: ...
Source pages p. 245

The author explains that this includes all possible substances and accidents, whether acquired by animals or not. He then points out that this definition refutes two deviant sects: the Qadariyya (who denied God's power over animals' voluntary acts) and the naturalists (al-ṭabāʾiʿiyyūn, who attributed some events to natural forces). Next, he comments on the phrase 'in accordance with will' (ʿalā wafq al-irāda) from the definition, explaining that God's act is volitional, not necessary like the emanation of a cause. Definition and Scope of Eternal Power
Sanusi defines eternal power and refutes Qadariyya and naturalists.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's definition of eternal divine power and its scope, including that it attaches to every possible being solely based on possibility.

Core Idea
God's power attaches to all possibles by virtue of possibility alone.

This lesson introduces a foundational attribute of Allah: eternal power. Imam Sanusi carefully defines it and clarifies its scope, refuting two key mistaken groups. The passage explains why God's power encompasses everything that is possible, regardless of time or existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once quietly, then the English translation. Let the author's words settle before you analyze them.
Notice the technical term 'muṣaḥḥiḥ' (corrector).
2
Understand 'the corrector of attachment'
Sanusi states that the only condition for God's power to attach to a thing is that the thing be possible (mumkin). Nothing else is needed.
This refutes those who add extra conditions.
3
Grasp the scope of power
Every possible, whether existent or non-existent, past or future, substance or accident, is within God's power. This is the universal scope of divine power.
It even includes voluntary actions of animals.
4
Identify the two refuted groups
The passage names the Qadariyya (who deny God's power over voluntary acts) and the naturalists (who attribute effects to nature). See how the definition itself refutes them.
The phrase 'in accordance with will' also refutes those who say God acts by necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا الذي اختارَهُ هذا الإمامُ هو الآتي على أنَّ مُصحِّحَ تعلَّقِ القدرة الأزليَّة بالممكن .. الإمكانُ فقط ، فكلُّ ممكن على هذا ؛ وجوديّاً كان أو عدميّاً ، سابقاً كانَ أو لاحقاً.. فهو مقدور لمولانا تبارك وتعالى ، ومقدوريَّةٌ كلَّ حقيقةٍ مِنْ هذه الحقائق بما يليقُ بها وهذا القولُ أقرب للُّغَةِ والعُرْفِ ، وأسلمُ مِنْ سوء الأدب وإيهام النقص ، والله سبحانه أعلمُ وقوله في تعريف القدرةِ الأزليَّةِ : ( يتأتى بها إيجاد كل ممكن ) يعني : سواء كانَ جِرْماً أو عرضاً ، مُكتسباً للحيوان أو غيرَ مُكتسَبٍ ، ففيه تنبيه على فسادِ مذهبِ القدريَّةِ الذينَ أخرجوا أفعال الحيواناتِ الاختيارية عن تعلق قدرة الله تعالى ، وعلى فسادِ مذهب الطبائعيينَ الذين أسندوا بعض الممكناتِ لقوى الطبائع العلوية والسفلية . وقوله : ( على وَفْقِ الإرادةِ ( إشارة إلى أنَّ فعلَهُ للكائناتِ إِنَّما هو بطريق الاختيار ، لا بطريق اللزوم ، كفعل العلة والطبيعة عند الفلاسفة والطبائعيين
And this which this Imam has chosen is that the corrector of the attachment of eternal power to the possible is possibility alone. So every possible according to this—whether existent or non-existent, prior or subsequent—is empowered by our Lord, Blessed and Exalted, and the measure of power for each reality is in accordance with what befits it. This statement is closer to language and custom, and safer from bad manners and suggesting deficiency. And God Almighty knows best. And His statement in the definition of eternal power: 'By it the bringing into existence of every possible is achievable' means: whether it is a substance or an accident, acquired by an animal or not acquired. In this is a warning of the corruption of the doctrine of the Qadariyya who excluded the voluntary acts of animals from the attachment of God's power, and of the corruption of the doctrine of the naturalists who attributed some possibles to the forces of upper and lower natures. And His statement: 'in accordance with will' is an indication that His act of bringing things into existence is by way of choice, not by way of necessity, like the act of the cause and nature according to the philosophers and naturalists.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the divine attribute of eternal power (al-qudra al-azaliyya). The author begins by stating the chosen view: that the corrector (muṣaḥḥiḥ) for the attachment of eternal power to possibles is simply possibility (al-imkān) itself—nothing else. Therefore, every possible, whether existent or non-existent, past or future, is within the power of God Almighty. However, the power's attachment is appropriate to each reality. This view is favored because it aligns with language and custom and avoids implying deficiency in God. Next, the author explains the definition: 'by it the bringing into existence of every possible is achievable.' This includes both substances (jirm) and accidents (ʿaraḍ), and actions of animals whether acquired or not. This refutes the Qadariyya (who deny God's power over voluntary acts of animals) and the naturalists (who attribute effects to natural forces). Finally, the phrase 'in accordance with will' indicates that God acts by choice, not by natural necessity, refuting the philosophers and naturalists.

Key Terms
القدرة الأزليَّة
الممكن
الإمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think God's power only attaches to some possibles, e.g., only to existing things or only to substances.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly states that power attaches to every possible, whether existent or non-existent, substance or accident, past or future.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, to what does the eternal power of God attach?
A) Only to what exists
B) To every possible being
C) Only to good things
D) Only to substances

Key Takeaway
God's eternal power attaches to every possible being solely based on its possibility, not any other condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every act you do, even your most secret sins, is within God's absolute power? If so, why do you still live as if you have autonomy apart from His will? Will you today acknowledge His power over every choice you make?
?
The text says God's power attaches to all possibles by possibility alone—nothing else qualifies. Does your heart accept that nothing—not your goodness, not your deeds—makes you deserving of His power? How does this truth change the way you rely on Him moment by moment?
?
The Qadariyya denied God's power over their choices, effectively limiting His sovereignty. Where in your life do you subtly think you are outside God's control? Will you repent and confess that His power encompasses even your most private decisions?
