That in the right of [Him]? And what is established that sight (mushāhada) is stronger than knowledge is only valid for the contingent (1); due to its deficiency and lack of encompassment (2) — for there may become disclosed to it upon sight matters that knowledge of it had not attached to at all, or attached but in an outline not in detail, so it benefits by hearing and sight knowledge of what was not known to it. And this is impossible in the right of Him, may He be exalted; for hearing and sight do not disclose in His right, blessed and exalted, something that was not disclosed to His knowledge, may He be glorified and exalted, due to the necessity of the encompassment of His knowledge, blessed and exalted, of all known things, in their totality and their detail. Indeed, hearing and sight add to knowledge in His right, may He be glorified and exalted, only by their own reality and their specific attachment (3), and they add nothing to the reality of His knowledge, may He be exalted, at all.
His saying: 'And perception (al-idrāk), on the position holding it, is like them' — meaning like them in being necessary.
(1) This is an answer to an implied question: how can what the perceptions are attached to be exactly what knowledge is attached to when it is established that sight is stronger than knowledge?
(2) By this you know that the gist of the answer is: prohibition of analogizing the unseen from the witnessed.
(3) And by this you know that the disclosed object and the attached object in the attribute of knowledge and the attributes of perception are one, and the difference between the attributes of perception and the attribute of knowledge appears by the distinctness in the reality of attachment and disclosure. Thus hearing and sight are established because they are reported by revelation, and we confess inability to perceive their reality. Said the eminent scholar al-ʿAḍud in (al-Mawāqif) (p. 292): 'The sixth section: on that He, exalted, is hearing and seeing; hearing is indicated by revelation, and it is among what is known necessarily from the religion of Muhammad, peace be upon him, and the ḥadīth is filled with it; it cannot be denied nor interpreted.'
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection that sight (مشاهدة) is stronger than knowledge, implying that if perceptions attach to the same object as knowledge, then sight would add something. The author explains that this claim only holds for contingent beings (حادث) because their knowledge is deficient and not all-encompassing; they may gain through perception knowledge they lacked. For God, this is impossible because His knowledge necessarily encompasses all things in detail. Hearing and sight do not add anything to the reality of God's knowledge; they only add by their own specific attachment and reality. The footnotes clarify: (1) the passage answers an implicit question about how perceptions can attach to the same object as knowledge despite sight being stronger; (2) the answer is that we cannot analogize the unseen (God) to the witnessed (creatures); (3) the disclosed object is the same for both knowledge and perception, but the difference lies in the reality of attachment—hearing and sight are established by revelation and we cannot grasp their true nature. The author then quotes al-ʿAḍud affirming that hearing and sight are necessary attributes of God, known from revelation.

Key Terms
المشاهدة
الحادث
قياس الغائب على الشاهد
السمع
البصر
الإدراك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God has perception, then perception must add something to His knowledge, just as it does for humans.
Correction: God's knowledge is all-encompassing, so perception cannot add any new information. The attributes of hearing and sight are affirmed by revelation and differ from knowledge only in their specific mode of attachment.

Checkpoint
Why is the claim that 'sight is stronger than knowledge' invalid for God?
A) Because God does not have sight
B) Because God's knowledge encompasses all things in detail
C) Because sight is not an attribute of God
D) Because God's knowledge is limited

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is so perfect that perception cannot increase it; hearing and sight are affirmed by revelation without implying any deficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a situation where your understanding is only in outline (ijmāl), do you trust that God's knowledge of every detail is already complete, or do you anxiously demand that He show you the details before you submit? How would your day change if you truly believed that God's encompassing knowledge frees you from needing to grasp all details?
?
The contingent being gains from perception because his knowledge is deficient. Do you live as if you too lack knowledge you must acquire, or do you constantly act as though you already know? Reflect on a recent moment when you felt insecure about not knowing—did you feel compelled to 'see' in order to believe, or did you rest in God's knowledge?
?
Sanusi confesses inability to perceive the reality of God's hearing and sight. Is there a part of your faith that you are trying to rationally exhaust, rather than humbly accepting by revelation? What would it mean for you to say 'we confess inability' and still affirm those attributes without fully comprehending them?

Refuting the Claim that Sight is Stronger than Knowledge for God
Sanusi refutes the analogy between God and contingent beings regarding sight and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that sensory sight is stronger than knowledge cannot apply to God, and how the attributes of hearing and sight relate to His all-encompassing knowledge.

Core Idea
God's knowledge is all-encompassing, so nothing is newly disclosed by His hearing or sight.

This passage tackles a subtle objection: if sensory sight is considered stronger than knowledge for humans, does that hold for God? Sanusi refutes the analogy by highlighting the difference between contingent and divine knowledge. He shows that while our limited knowledge can be enhanced by sensory perception, God's knowledge is perfect and complete, leaving no room for addition. Understanding this distinction is crucial for preserving the uniqueness of divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The implicit question is that sight seems stronger than knowledge, so how can God's sight and hearing be the same as His knowledge?
This is an implied question addressed in the footnotes.
2
Understand the refutation's foundation
Sanusi refutes by preventing the analogy of the unseen upon the witnessed. For contingents, sight reveals matters not known in detail, but for God, knowledge encompasses all things in detail.
The key is God's complete encompassment (الإحاطة).
3
Grasp the positive assertion
Hearing and sight are distinct attributes with their own specific attachments, but they do not add to the reality of God's knowledge.
The disclosed object is the same; the difference is in the mode of attachment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك في حق
وما ثبت أنَّ المشاهدة أقوى مِنَ العلم إنَّما يصح الحادثِ (۱) ؛ لنقص عليه وعدم إحاطته(۲) فقد ينكشف له عندَ المشاهدة أمورٌ لم يتعلَّق بها علمُهُ أصلاً ، أو تعلَّق لكن على سبيل الإجمال لا على سبيل التفصيل ، فيستفيد بسبب السمع والبصر علماً بما لم يكن معلوماً عندَه
وهذا مستحيل في حقِّهِ تعالى ؛ فإنَّ السمع والبصر لا ينكشفُ بهما في حقه تبارك وتعالى شيء لم يكن منكشفاً لعلمه جلَّ وعلا ؛ لوجوبِ
إحاطة علمه تبارك وتعالى بجميع المعلوماتِ ؛ جُمْلتِها وتفصيلها وإِنَّما السمع والبصر يزيدان على العلم في حقه جلَّ وعلا بحقيقتهما وتعلقهما الخاص بهما (۳) ، ولا يزيدان في حقيقة علمهِ تعالى شيئاً
أصلاً .
(۱) هذا جواب عن سؤال مقدَّر ؛ تقديره : كيف يكون ما تعلقت به الإدراكات عين ما تعلق به العلم وقد ثبت أن المشاهدة أقوى من العلم ؟
(۲) بهذا تعلم أنَّ حاصل الجواب : منع قياس الغائب على الشاهد
(۳) وبهذا تعلم : أنَّ المنكشِف والمتعلَّق في صفة العلم وصفات الإدراك . . واحدٌ ، وإنما الفرق بين صفات الإدراك وصفة العلم يظهر بالتباين في حقيقة التعلُّق والانكشاف ، فثبت السمع والبصر لورودهما شرعاً ، ونقر بالعجز عن إدراك حقيقتهما
That is concerning the divine. And what is established that sensory sight is stronger than knowledge is only valid for the contingent (1) due to its deficiency and lack of encompassment (2). For it may be disclosed to him at the time of sight matters that his knowledge had not attached to at all, or had attached but in a general way not in detail, so he gains through hearing and sight knowledge of what was not known to him. And this is impossible with respect to the Exalted; for hearing and sight do not disclose with respect to Him, Blessed and Most High, anything that was not already disclosed to His knowledge, due to the necessity of His knowledge encompassing all known things, their universals and particulars. Rather, hearing and sight only add to knowledge in His right, Glorious and Most High, by their own reality and their specific attachment (3), and they do not add anything whatsoever to the reality of His knowledge. (1) This is an answer to an implied question: How can what is perceived be the same as what is known given that sight is stronger than knowledge? (2) By this you know that the sum of the answer is: preventing the analogy of the unseen upon the witnessed. (3) And by this you know that the disclosed and the attached in the attribute of knowledge and the attributes of perception... are one, and the difference between the attributes of perception and the attribute of knowledge appears through the divergence in the reality of attachment and disclosure. So hearing and sight are established because they are transmitted in revelation, and we confess inability to grasp their reality.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding the relationship between God's knowledge and His attributes of hearing and sight. The objection assumes that sensory sight (المشاهدة) is stronger than knowledge, so how can God's sight and hearing be the same as His knowledge? The answer distinguishes between contingent beings and God. For contingent beings, sight reveals things beyond their limited knowledge, but God's knowledge is all-encompassing in detail, so nothing is newly disclosed. Thus hearing and sight do not add to the reality of His knowledge; they are additional attributes with their own specific attachments. The footnotes clarify that the answer prevents the analogy of the unseen on the witnessed (الغائب على الشاهد), and that the disclosed object is the same for both, but the mode of attachment differs.

Key Terms
المشاهدة
العلم
الإحاطة
السمع
البصر
قياس الغائب على الشاهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's hearing and sight add to His knowledge in a way that changes its reality.
Correction: They are distinct attributes with their own specific attachments, but they do not add to the reality of His knowledge, which is already all-encompassing.

Checkpoint
What is the key difference that allows sight to be stronger than knowledge for contingent beings but not for God?
A) God's knowledge is limited.
B) God's knowledge encompasses all things in detail.
C) God does not have sight.
D) Contingent beings have no knowledge.

Key Takeaway
God's knowledge is all-encompassing in detail, so His hearing and sight do not disclose anything new, but are additional attributes with their own specific attachments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face uncertainty, do you panic as if your limited sight must guide you, or do you rest in the certainty that God's knowledge already holds the full picture? What practical step can you take today to shift from reliance on your own perception to trust in His omniscience?
?
In what areas of your life do you unconsciously project human limitations onto God, expecting Him to act or know as humans do? How would your faith change if you truly internalized that His attributes are beyond comparison?
?
If God's hearing and sight disclose nothing new to Him, what does that imply about the way you seek His guidance? Are you asking Him to show you something He doesn't already know, or are you humbly aligning your will with His all-encompassing decree?

The Eternal Speech of Allah: Definition and Proofs
Sanusi defines eternal speech and provides proofs from revelation and reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of Allah's eternal speech as a meaning subsisting in His essence, distinct from letters and sounds, and the proofs for it from revelation and reason.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute, not composed of letters and sounds.

In this passage, Imam Sanusi clarifies the nature of Allah's attribute of speech. He begins by defining it as an eternal meaning inherent in the divine essence, which is expressed through various scriptures. He then establishes its reality through both revealed texts and rational argument, emphasizing that what is fitting for Allah is necessary for Him.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of eternal speech
Understand the precise description: it is a meaning, not letters/sounds, free from temporal changes.
2
Notice the negations in the definition
The passage lists what eternal speech is not: not composed of parts, not subject to time, etc.
3
Identify the revelatory proof
See how the Book, Sunnah, and consensus affirm speech through commands, prohibitions, etc.
4
Understand the rational proof
Reason shows that since Allah knows all, He must have speech, and it is necessary for Him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والإدراك على القول بهِ مثلُهما ( يعني : مثلهما في وجوب تعلقِهِ بكلّ موجود ، وأنَّهُ لا يختص بما اختص به في الشاهد ، وقد تقدَّمَ فيهِ ثلاثةُ أقوال لأهل السنَّةِ (۱) ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق .
[ صفة الكلام ]
وَالْكَلامُ الأَزَلِيُّ : وَهُوَ الْمَعْنَى الْقَائِمُ بِالذَّاتِ ، الْمُعَبَّرُ عَنْهُ بِالْعِبَارَاتِ الْمُخْتَلِفَاتِ (۲) ، الْمُبَايِنُ لِجِنْسِ الْحُرُوفِ وَالأَصْوَاتِ ، الْمُنَزَّهُ عَنِ الْبَعْضِ وَالْكُلَّ ، وَالتَّقْدِيمِ وَالتَّأْخِيرِ ، وَالتَّجَدُّدِ وَالسُّكُوتِ ، وَاللَّحْنِ وَالْإِعْرَابِ وَسَائِرِ أَنْوَاعِ التَّغَيُّرَاتِ ، الْمُتَعَلِّقُ بِمَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ الْعِلْمُ مِنَ
الْمُتَعَلَّقَاتِ
لا شكّ أنَّ الكتاب والسنة والإجماع مصرحة بإثباتِ الكلام لمولانا تبارك وتعالى ؛ مِنْ أمرٍ ونهي ، ووعد ووعيد ، وتبشير وتحذير ،
وإخبار .
ودليل العقل أيضاً يدلُّ بالطريق القطعي : أن كل عالم بأمرٍ يصح أن يتكلم به ، ومولانا جل وعلا عالم بجميع المعلوماتِ ، فصح أنَّ لهُ كلاماً يتعلَّق بها ، وكلُّ ما صح أن يتّصفَ بِهِ جَلَّ وعلا وجبَ لهُ
(۱) وذاك عند قوله : ( واختلف في زيادة صفات ) ، وانظر ( ص ۲۳۷ )
(۲) فإذا عُبّر عنه بالعربية فالقرآن ، وبالسريانية فالإنجيل ، وبالعبرانية فالتوراة والمسمى واحد وإن اختلفت العبارات. « بناني » ( ص ٤٧ )
His saying: 'And perception, according to the view affirming it, is like them two' — meaning: like them two in the necessity of its attachment to every existent, and that it is not specific to what it is specific to in the witnessed. And three opinions of Ahl al-Sunnah have preceded concerning it (1). And with Allah is success.
[The Attribute of Speech]
And the eternal speech: it is the meaning subsisting in the Essence, expressed by diverse expressions (2), distinct from the genus of letters and sounds, transcendent of portion and whole, of precedence and postponement, of renewal and silence, of solecism and declension and all kinds of changes, attaching to what knowledge attaches to of the things to which attachment occurs. There is no doubt that the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus explicitly affirm the affirmation of speech for our Master, Blessed and Most High: of command and prohibition, promise and threat, glad tidings and warnings, and informing.
And the rational proof also indicates by a definitive way that every knower of a matter is fit to speak about it, and our Master, Glorious and Most High, is knower of all known things, so it is fit that He has speech that attaches to them. And everything that it is fit for Him, Glorious and Most High, to be described with is necessary for Him.
(1) That is concerning His saying: 'And they differed concerning the increase of attributes.' See p. 237.
(2) So if expressed in Arabic then it is the Qur'an, in Syriac then it is the Gospel, in Hebrew then it is the Torah, and the named is one even if the expressions differ. 'Banani' p. 47.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage defines the attribute of eternal speech (الكلام الأزلي) and provides its proofs. First, it clarifies a preceding statement about perception (الإدراك) being like hearing and sight in attachment to all existents, and notes three opinions of Ahl al-Sunnah on the matter. Then it moves to the definition of eternal speech: it is a meaning (معنى) subsisting in the divine Essence, expressed by different expressions (العبارات المختلفة) in different scriptures. It is distinct from letters and sounds, free from all temporal characteristics such as division, precedence, renewal, silence, and grammatical changes. It attaches to the same objects as knowledge. The proof from revelation (الكتاب, السنة, الإجماع) shows that God speaks through commands, prohibitions, promises, threats, etc. The rational proof (دليل العقل) is definitive: every knower of something can speak about it, and God knows all, so He has speech; and whatever is fitting for God (not impossible) is necessary for Him to have. The footnotes clarify that the three opinions refer to an earlier discussion on increase of attributes, and that the expressions differ but the speech is one.

Key Terms
الكلام الأزلي
المعنى القائم بالذات
العبارات المختلفة
الكتاب
السنة
الإجماع
دليل العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's speech is composed of letters and sounds like human speech.
Correction: God's speech is an eternal attribute, not composed of letters or sounds; these are only expressions of it.

Checkpoint
How does the rational proof establish that God has speech?
A) Because God commands and prohibits in revelation.
B) Because every knower of a thing can speak about it, and God knows all things.
C) Because the Qur'an is created.
D) Because God's speech is composed of words.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is an eternal attribute (meaning) inherent in His essence, proven by revelation and reason, and is not made of letters or sounds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's speech is a single eternal meaning, not multiple words, then every verse of the Quran is a direct expression of that one reality. Are you approaching the Quran as if each verse is a fresh address from that eternal meaning to you right now, or do you treat it as a static historical text?
?
The rational proof says that because Allah knows everything, He must speak about everything. Do you live as though God has spoken about every aspect of your life, or do you assume His silence on matters you'd rather not submit to His command?
?
Since Allah's speech is free from all change and imperfection, how do you reconcile your own fluctuating and imperfect speech with the call to reflect His attributes? What concrete step will you take today to make your words more truthful and aligned with His eternal speech?

The Hashwiyya Claim and Its Refutation
Sanusi presents the Hashwiyya claim and refutes it with a rational argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Hashwiyya view that God's speech consists of letters and sounds is rationally untenable.

Core Idea
Letters and sounds cannot be eternal because they are preceded and followed by non-existence.

The Hashwiyya, a sect known for anthropomorphism, claimed that God's speech is composed of letters and sounds like human speech, yet eternal. This directly contradicts the rational understanding of letters and sounds as temporal phenomena. Sanusi presents their view and refutes it with a simple but decisive argument about the nature of temporality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the author's argument.
Pay attention to how Sanusi introduces the sect before giving their view.
2
Identify the Hashwiyya claim
What do the Hashwiyya say about God's speech? They claim it is letters and sounds subsisting in God's essence, and they distinguish between the ink (created) and the written text (eternal).
Notice the apparent contradiction: they say the ink is created but the writing becomes identical to the eternal.
3
Find Sanusi's refutation
Sanusi argues that letters and sounds are only understood as created (hadith) because they come into existence after non-existence and cease. The eternal does not admit non-existence at any time.
This is a rational argument, not a scriptural one.
4
Reflect on the implication
If letters and sounds are temporal, then God's speech cannot be composed of them. The Hashwiyya view is self-contradictory.
This connects to the broader Ash'ari position that God's speech is an eternal attribute, not composed of temporal parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اختلف الناسُ بعد هذا على فِرَق :
فذهب الحشويَّةُ : إلى أنَّ هذا الكلام الذي يتّصفُ بهِ مولانا جلَّ وعز حروف وأصوات قائمة بذاتِهِ على حسب ما ثبت في الكلام اللساني في الشاهد ، وزعموا أنَّهُ معَ كونه حرفاً وصوتاً قديم ، بل زعموا أنَّ المدادَ حادث ، فإذا كُتِبَ بهِ القرآنُ صارَ بعينِهِ قديماً !
وهذا المذهب واضحُ الفسادِ ؛ إِذْ مِنَ المعلومِ أنَّ الحروف والأصوات لا تُعقَلُ إلا حادثةً ؛ لتجدُّدِها بعد عدم ، وعدمها بعد تجدد ، فالعدمُ يكتنفها سابقاً ولاحقاً ، والقديم لا يقبلُ العدمَ لا سابقاً ولا لاحقاً .
Then people differed after this into sects: al-Hashwiyya held that this speech which our Lord, mighty and majestic, is described with is letters and sounds subsisting in His essence, in accordance with what is established regarding linguistic speech in the witnessed realm. They claimed that while being letters and sound it is eternal, indeed they claimed that the ink is created (hadith), so if the Qur'an is written with it, it becomes identical to the eternal! This school is clearly corrupt, because it is known that letters and sounds are only understood as created, due to their coming into existence after non-existence, and their ceasing after coming into existence. Non-existence encompasses them before and after, and the eternal does not admit non-existence, neither before nor after.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage is a presentation and refutation of the Hashwiyya position on the nature of God's speech. The author introduces the sectarian division after establishing the necessity of speech for God. The Hashwiyya claim that God's speech consists of letters and sounds subsisting in His essence, similar to human speech. They further assert that this speech is eternal, and that the ink used to write the Qur'an is created, but the written text becomes identical to the eternal speech. This implication is that the physical book is eternal. The author declares this view clearly corrupt and provides a rational proof: letters and sounds are only conceivable as created because they come into existence after non-existence and cease after existence, so non-existence surrounds them. The eternal, by contrast, does not admit non-existence in any way. Therefore, letters and sounds cannot be eternal, refuting the Hashwiyya claim.

Key Terms
الحشويّة
الكلام
حروف وأصوات
القديم
الحدث
المداد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Hashwiyya view that the ink is created but the writing is eternal is logically coherent.
Correction: Sanusi shows it is contradictory because letters and sounds are inherently temporal. If the ink is created, the written letters and sounds are also created, not eternal.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi reject the Hashwiyya claim that God's speech is letters and sounds?
A) Because letters and sounds cannot be eternal since they are preceded by non-existence and followed by non-existence.
B) Because the Qur'an is created.
C) Because the Hashwiyya are innovators.
D) Because God's speech is not composed of parts.

Key Takeaway
The Hashwiyya view that God's speech consists of letters and sounds is refuted because letters and sounds are inherently temporal, and the eternal cannot be composed of temporal parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi says the eternal does not admit non-existence 'before or after.' Is there any aspect of your life—your health, your relationships, your possessions—that you treat as if it will never face non-existence? What would change if you truly internalized that everything except God will eventually cease?
?
The Hashwiyya confused the created ink with the eternal speech. In what ways do you confuse temporal means (like your own words, deeds, or status) with what is truly eternal? How might this confusion be 'clearly corrupt' in your own heart?
?
Sanusi's refutation is rational and decisive. Are there beliefs you hold about God that, when examined rationally, are contradictory? What keeps you from abandoning them, even when the proof is plain?

Mu'tazila view on God's speech and its refutation
Sanusi refutes the Mu'tazila view on God's speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila view that God's speech is created in a body and Sanusi's refutation showing that it leads to worshipping the bodies.

Core Idea
Speech cannot be delegated to creation without making creation divine.

The Mu'tazila attempted to preserve God's transcendence by locating His speech in created bodies. But Sanusi shows this backfires—if God has no speech in His essence, then the bodies become the commanding entities. This lesson unpacks the argument and its logical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila position
Read the passage carefully to understand the Mu'tazila view that God's speech is an act created in a body.
Note that they agree with Hashwiyya on letters and sounds but differ on location.
2
Identify the first objection
Sanusi claims the view is corrupt because it makes speech impossible for God as a knower.
This is a brief point; we'll move to the main argument.
3
Examine the worship problem
If no command exists in God's essence, the bodies that carry it become the object of worship.
This is the core of the refutation.
4
Consider the Mu'tazila response and Sanusi's counter
The Mu'tazila say the bodies indicate God's will. Sanusi replies that attribution requires the attribute to exist in the source first.
This uses the logic of conveying.
5
Understand the final refutation
Sanusi invokes God's general will to show the attempted escape fails.
God's will includes good and evil, so the bodies convey contradictory commands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذهبت المعتزلة : إلى أنَّ كلامه تعالى حروف وأصوات كما قالَتِ الحشويَّةُ ، إلا أنَّهم خالفوهم بأن قالوا : إِنَّ كلامَهُ تعالى فعلٌ مِنْ أفعالِهِ ؛ كرَزْقِهِ وعطائِهِ ، فلا يصح أن يقوم بذاتِهِ تعالى ؛ لاستحالة قيام الحوادثِ بهِ ، فإذا أراد الله تعالى أن يتكلم بأمرٍ أو نهي أو غيرهما مِنْ سائر أنواع الكلام .. خلقَ ذلكَ في جِرْمٍ مِنَ الأجرام ، وأسمع ذلكَ مَنْ شاءَ مِنْ ملائكته وأنبيائه ورُسُلِهِ .
وهذا المذهب أيضاً واضح الفسادِ ؛ لأنَّهُ يستلزم امتناع ما عُلِمَتْ صحتُهُ مِنَ الكلام في حق العالِمِ ، وأيضاً : إذا لم يكن في الذاتِ العليَّةِ أمر ولا نهي ، ولا وعد ولا وعيد، وإنَّما هي موجودةٌ في الأجرام الحادثة.. فالمكلفون إذا عابدون لتلك الأجرام ؛ إذ هي الآمرة الناهية (۱) .
فإنْ قالوا : إنَّ ما خُلِقَ فيها دال على ما عندَ اللهِ تعالى مِنَ الأمرِ والنهي ، والوعد والوعيد ، فهي كالمبلغةِ عنه تبارك وتعالى فالجواب : أنَّ الذات العليَّةَ عندَهم عارية عن الكلام أصلاً ؛ فلا أمرَ فيها ولا نهي ولا خبر ، ولا وعد ولا وعيدَ ، ومِنْ شرط تبليغ هذه الحقائقِ أن يتصف بها المبلغ عنه أولاً ، ثم تُبلغ عنه .
و
ومذهبهم : أنَّ هذهِ الحقائق إنَّما وُجِدَتِ ابتداء في تلك الأجرام ، ولم يكن لها وجود أصلاً في ذاتِهِ تبارك وتعالى ، فليس إذاً عندَهُ حُكم ولا خبرٌ يُبلغان عنهُ ، وإذا كان كذلك فالناس إذا عابدون لتلك الأجرام التي سُمِعَ منها الأمر والنهي ، والوعد والوعيد
ولا يُخلَّصهم ما زعموهُ : أَنَّ الله تعالى إرادة للخير ، فهي فهي التي تُمْتَثَلُ ، وهي التي بلغتها الأجرام عنه بصيغة الأمر والنهي ، والوعدِ والوعيد ، ونحو ذلكَ مِنَ الألفاظ الدالة على الأحكام ؛ لأنَّ هذا الذي تخيلوه باطل ؛ لما ثبتَ مِنَ البرهان القاطع أنَّ إرادته تعالى عامة للخيرِ والشر ، والطاعة والمعصية ، والكفر والإيمان ، فيلزم إذا أنْ
(۱) إذ الوصف إنما هو صفة لما قامت هي به؛ كالبياض خلقه تعالى في الثلج فصار الثلج هو الأبيض، لا خالق البياض تعالى وجل، ولكن هذا إلزام من أهل السنة لا يلتزمه المعتزلة، ولذا سيأتي بالفنقلة الآتية
The Mu'tazila held that His speech, exalted is He, is letters and sounds as the Hashwiyya said, except that they disagreed with them by saying: His speech, exalted is He, is an act among His acts, like His providing and giving. So it is not valid for it to subsist in His essence, because of the impossibility of accidents (hawadith) subsisting in Him. Therefore, when God, exalted is He, intends to speak with a command, prohibition, or other types of speech, He creates that in a body (jirm) among bodies, and makes it heard to whomever He wills of His angels, prophets, and messengers. This school also is clearly corrupt, because it necessitates the impossibility of what is known to be sound regarding speech in the case of the knower [God]. Also, if there is in the supreme essence no command, no prohibition, no promise, no threat, and they exist only in the created bodies, then responsible beings would be worshipping those bodies, since they are the commanding and prohibiting (1). If they say: that which is created in them indicates what is with God of command, prohibition, promise, and threat, so they are like conveyers (muballigha) from Him, blessed and exalted. The answer: the supreme essence according to them is devoid of speech entirely; there is no command, no prohibition, no report, no promise, no threat. And one of the conditions for conveying these realities is that the one conveyed about should first be described by them, then they are conveyed from him. Their position is that these realities only came into existence initially in those bodies, and they had no existence at all in His essence, blessed and exalted. Therefore, there is no judgment or report from Him to be conveyed. If that is so, then people are worshipping those bodies from which they heard command and prohibition, promise and threat. And what they claim does not save them: that God, exalted is He, wills good, so it is that will which is obeyed, and it is that which the bodies conveyed from Him in the form of command, prohibition, promise, threat, and similar expressions indicating judgments; because this which they imagined is false, due to the conclusive proof that His will, exalted is He, is general for good and evil, obedience and disobedience, disbelief and faith. Therefore, it would necessitate that (1) [Footnote: Indeed, the attribute is only a description of that in which it inheres; like whiteness which God created in snow, so the snow becomes the white thing, not the Creator of whiteness, exalted is He. But this is an argument (ilzam) by the Ahl al-Sunna that the Mu'tazila do not accept, and thus it will come with the following shift.]
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the Mu'tazila view on God's speech. The Mu'tazila agree with the Hashwiyya that speech is letters and sounds, but they differ by saying it is an act of God, not an attribute subsisting in His essence, because accidents cannot subsist in God. Instead, God creates speech in a body (e.g., a tree) and makes it heard. The author declares this view clearly corrupt for two reasons: first, it entails impossible consequences for speech in the case of a knower (God); second, if there is no command or prohibition in God's essence, only in bodies, then worshippers would be worshipping those bodies, since they are the ones commanding and prohibiting. An objection is then considered: the created speech indicates what is with God, so it functions as a message. The answer is that for a message to be conveyed, the sender must first possess the attribute; but the Mu'tazila hold that God's essence is devoid of speech, so nothing is conveyed. The refutation continues: since these realities exist only in bodies, and God's will is general for both good and evil (by conclusive proof), the attempted escape via God's will for good fails. The footnote explains that the argument about bodies commanding is an ilzam (necessary implication) by the Ahl al-Sunna that the Mu'tazila do not accept, but it will be addressed later.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الكلام
فعل
الأجرام
الحوادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Creating speech in bodies solves the problem of accidents in God.
Correction: It requires that God have speech in His essence for the bodies to be conveyers; otherwise, the bodies become the source of worship.

Checkpoint
What is the main problem Sanusi identifies with the Mu'tazila view that God's speech is created in a body?
A) It implies God does not speak at all.
B) It leads to worshipping the bodies that contain the speech.
C) It contradicts the Qur'an.
D) It denies God's power.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila view fails because it makes created bodies the source of command, undermining God's direct speech and leading to worshipping the bodies.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you truly believe you are hearing God's eternal speech, or do you sometimes treat it as if it were a created message from a created being? How can you deepen your reverence for the words as His direct address to you?
?
Sanusi warns that if speech is not in God's essence, then created things become the commanders, leading to worship of them. In your life, have you ever followed a person or a trend as if their commands were absolute, overshadowing God's direct commands? What would it take to realign your obedience to God's speech alone?
?
The Mu'tazila thought that denying an attribute in God protects His oneness, but actually it leads to attributing divinity to creation. Is there any area of your belief where you think you are protecting God's transcendence, but in reality you are reducing His attributes or making created things stand in His place? Examine your heart and commit to correcting it.

Refutation of Created Commands in Bodies
Sanusi refutes the claim that created objects convey God's commands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazilite view that commands are created in bodies leads logically to worship of those bodies and how Sanusi refutes their objections using necessary implications.

Core Idea
If commands are created in bodies, then people worship bodies, not God.

This passage is a key argument in the debate on God's speech. The Mu'tazila argue that God does not have eternal speech, so commands and prohibitions are created in bodies. Sanusi shows the absurd consequences: if commands come from bodies, those bodies become objects of worship. He then refutes their attempt to say the bodies merely convey God's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the initial phrase 'الحادثة' seems incomplete; it refers to the recently created bodies.
2
Identify the opponent's claim and Sanusi's first consequence
The opponent claims that commands created in bodies are indicators of God's will, making the bodies like conveyers. Sanusi counters that if so, people worship those bodies.
3
Analyze Sanusi's logical refutation
Sanusi points out that in the opponent's system, God has no speech, so there is nothing to convey. Thus the bodies must be the origin of commands, not mere conveyers.
This is a necessary implication (ilzām).
4
Understand the final refutation using God's universal will
The opponent tries to escape by saying God's will is only good. Sanusi shows that God's will encompasses good and evil, so the bodies would convey evil too, leading to no disobedience—an absurdity.
This seals the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحادثة.. فالمكلفون إذا عابدون لتلك الأجرام ؛ إذ هي الآمرة الناهية (1) . فإنْ قالوا : إنَّ ما خُلِقَ فيها دال على ما عندَ اللهِ تعالى مِنَ الأمر والنهي ، والوعد والوعيد ، فهي كالمبلغةِ عنه تبارك وتعالى فالجواب : أنَّ الذات العليَّةَ عندَهم عارية عن الكلام أصلاً ؛ فلا أمرَ فيها ولا نهي ولا خبر ، ولا وعد ولا وعيدَ ، ومِنْ شرط تبليغ هذه الحقائقِ أن يتصف بها المبلغ عنه أولاً ، ثم تُبلغ عنه . ومذهبهم : أنَّ هذهِ الحقائق إنَّما وُجِدَتِ ابتداء في تلك الأجرام ، ولم يكن لها وجود أصلاً في ذاتِهِ تبارك وتعالى ، فليس إذاً عندَهُ حُكم ولا خبرٌ يُبلغان عنهُ ، وإذا كان كذلك فالناس إذا عابدون لتلك الأجرام التي سُمِعَ منها الأمر والنهي ، والوعد والوعيد ولا يُخلَّصهم ما زعموهُ : أَنَّ الله تعالى إرادة للخير ، فهي التي تُمْتَثَلُ ، وهي التي بلغتها الأجرام عنه بصيغة الأمر والنهي ، والوعدِ والوعيد ، ونحو ذلكَ مِنَ الألفاظ الدالة على الأحكام ؛ لأنَّ هذا الذي تخيلوه باطل ؛ لما ثبتَ مِنَ البرهان القاطع أنَّ إرادته تعالى عامة للخيرِ والشر ، والطاعة والمعصية ، والكفر والإيمان ، فيلزم إذا أن لا معصية أصلاً؛ لأنَّ الخَلْقَ كلَّهم متصرفونَ على وَفْقِ إرادتِهِ تعالى (1) . (1) إذ الوصف إنما هو صفة لما قامت هي به ؛ كالبياض خلقه تعالى في الثلج فصار الثلج هو الأبيض ، لا خالق البياض تعالى وجلَّ ، ولكن هذا إلزام من أهل السنة لا يلتزمه المعتزلة ، ولذا سيأتي بالفنقلة الآتية
The [recently created things]... then the morally responsible ones are worshippers of those celestial bodies, since they are the commanding and forbidding (1). Then if they say: 'What is created in them indicates what is with God Almighty of command and prohibition, promise and threat, so they are like the conveyer from Him, Blessed and Most High,' then the answer: 'The Supreme Essence according to them is devoid of speech entirely; so there is no command in It, nor prohibition, nor report, nor promise, nor threat. And one condition of conveying these truths is that the one conveyed from must first be described with them, then they are conveyed from him.' And their doctrine is that these truths only came into existence initially in those celestial bodies, and they had no existence at all in His Essence, Blessed and Most High. So there is with Him neither a ruling nor a report to be conveyed from Him. And if this is so, then people are worshippers of those celestial bodies from which command and prohibition, promise and threat are heard. And that which they claimed does not save them: that God Almighty wills the good, so it is that which is obeyed, and it is that which the celestial bodies conveyed from Him in the form of command and prohibition, promise and threat, and similar expressions indicating rulings. Because this which they imagined is false; due to what has been established by decisive proof that His will, Most High, is general for good and evil, obedience and disobedience, unbelief and faith. So it follows then that there is no disobedience at all; because all of creation act in accordance with His will, Most High (1). (1) For the description is only an attribute of that in which it inheres; like whiteness which He, Most High, created in snow, so the snow becomes the white thing, not the Creator of whiteness, Most High and Glorified. But this is an argument from the Ahl al-Sunna which the Mu'tazila do not hold, and hence he will come with the following shift.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an opponent's objection regarding the conveyance of divine commands through created objects. The passage begins with a statement that if the opponents' view is accepted, then morally responsible people would be worshipping those celestial bodies (ajrām) because they are the ones that actually command and forbid. Then the author presents the opponent's claim: the commands, prohibitions, promises, and threats created in those bodies are indicators of what is with God, so the bodies are like conveyers from Him. The author answers that in the opponent's system, God is devoid of speech, so He has no command, prohibition, etc. in His essence. For something to be conveyed from someone, that person must first possess those attributes. The opponent's doctrine is that these truths only originate in the bodies and have no existence in God's essence, so there is nothing from God to convey. Consequently, people are worshipping the bodies that utter these words. The author refutes the opponent's attempted escape by appealing to God's will: they claim God wills only good, so the bodies convey that good. The author responds that it is established by decisive proof that God's will encompasses both good and evil, obedience and disobedience, faith and unbelief. Therefore, if the bodies convey the will, they convey evil as well, which contradicts their claim. In fact, if God's will is general, then all acts are in accordance with His will, so there is no disobedience at all, which is absurd. The footnote clarifies that the argument is a necessary implication (ilzām) from the Ahl al-Sunna, not an admission of the Mu'tazila's position.

طاعة (ṭā‘a)
معصية (ma‘ṣiya)
خير (khayr)
شر (sharr)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Commands created in bodies are merely conveyances from God, so worship is still for God.
Correction: Sanusi shows that if God has no speech, there is nothing to convey; thus the bodies become the source, leading to worship of bodies.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the consequence if the opponent's view (that commands are created in bodies) is accepted?
A) People would be worshipping God through those bodies.
B) People would be worshipping those bodies themselves.
C) People would be sinless because God's will is only for good.
D) People would be following God's commands through the bodies.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's refutation demonstrates that the Mu'tazilite view of created speech leads logically to shirk, an impossible consequence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself treating a human leader, a book, or even your own desires as the ultimate source of command in your life, effectively ascribing to them the authority that belongs only to God? How does Sanusi's warning about worshipping created objects challenge you to examine where you place ultimate authority?
?
If you truly believe that God's will encompasses everything—including your failures, your sins, and even the evil in the world—why do you still complain about your circumstances or rebel against His decree? What would change in your daily life if you internalized that there is no disobedience except within the scope of His will?
?
The Mu'tazila thought they were protecting God's transcendence, but Sanusi shows their view leads to shirk. Is there a belief you hold that you think honors God, but might actually be leading you away from Him? What would it cost you to examine that belief honestly today?

Refutation of Denial of Non-Letter Non-Sound Divine Speech
Sanusi refutes innovators who deny non-letter/non-sound divine speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni argument for God's speech as an attribute beyond letters and sounds, using internal speech as evidence.

Core Idea
God's speech is not like our speech—it is an eternal attribute without letters or sounds.

This passage addresses a core mistake of some innovators who deny that God's speech can exist without being composed of letters and sounds. Sanusi presents a powerful refutation by pointing to the internal speech we experience in our own souls, which is distinct from knowledge and will, yet meaningful. This establishes that speech can be non-letter/non-sound in the witnessed realm, thereby dismantling the innovators' position. The author then affirms the Sunni consensus on God's eternal speech attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation, to grasp the flow of Sanusi's argument. Note the refutation structure.
2
Identify the innovators' claim
Notice that Sanusi begins by stating the root cause: denial of non-letter/non-sound speech. Understand why this is foundational.
3
Follow the refutation using internal speech
Sanusi uses an analogy from our own experience: the internal speech (kalam nafsi) that conveys meaning without letters or sounds. Understand how this disproves the innovators' restriction.
4
Understand the affirmative Sunni position
Sanusi then states what Ahl al-Sunnah affirms: God's speech is an eternal attribute, free from temporal characteristics like priority, parts, silence, etc. Grasp the attributes of divine speech.
5
Reflect on the doctrine of incomparability
The passage concludes that the essence of God's speech is beyond human comprehension, just like His essence. This ensures tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا معصية أصلاً؛ لأنَّ الخَلْقَ كلَّهم متصرفونَ على وَفْقِ إرادتِهِ تعالى. والحامل لهؤلاء المبتدعة على هذه الأقوال الفاسدة : إنكارهم كلاماً غير حرفٍ ولا صوتٍ، وقد نقض عليهم علماء أهل السنة بما نجد في أنفسنا مِنَ الكلام الدال على المعاني؛ للقطع بأنَّه مغاير لما في النفس مِنَ العلوم والإراداتِ، والظنون والشكوك والأوهام. وإذا ثبت في الشاهدِ كلام ليسَ بحرفٍ ولا صوتٍ .. بطل ما عوّلوا عليهِ مِنْ حصر الكلام في الحروفِ والأصوات، واتَّضحَ أَنَّ الحق ما أجمعَ عليهِ أهلُ السَّنَّةِ مِنْ ثبوتِ كلام للمولى تبارك وتعالى؛ ليسَ مِنْ جنس الحروفِ والأصوات، منزّهاً عن التقدم والتأخُرِ، والجزء والكل، واللحن والإعراب والسكوت، ونحوها مِنْ خواص كلامنا الحادثِ، لسانيّاً كانَ أو نفسياً؛ لاستلزام ذلكَ كلّهِ النقص والبَكَمَ، والحدوث، وإِنَّما كلامه جلَّ وعلا صفةٌ واجبة القدم والبقاء، ما تعلَّقَ بهِ علمُهُ، وكُنْهُهُ محجوب عن العقلِ؛ إذْ لا مثلَ لهُ بجميع وجوهه، لا عقليّاً ولا وهميّاً ولا خياليّاً، ولا موجوداً ولا مقدراً، وذلك كذاتِهِ العليَّةِ وسائرِ صفاتِهِ.
There is no disobedience at all because all creatures are acting in accordance with His will, exalted is He. What drives these innovators to these corrupt statements is their denial of a speech that is not a letter nor a sound. And the scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah have refuted them by what we find within ourselves of speech that indicates meanings, because it is certain that it is different from what is in the soul of knowledges, volitions, opinions, doubts, and fancies. And if it is established in the witnessed realm a speech that is neither letter nor sound, then what they relied upon of restricting speech to letters and sounds is invalidated. And it becomes clear that the truth is what Ahl al-Sunnah have agreed upon: the affirmation of a speech for the Lord, blessed and exalted, not of the kind of letters and sounds, transcendent of priority and posteriority, part and whole, melody and inflection and silence, and similar attributes of our temporal speech, whether lingual or psychic, because all of that entails imperfection, muteness, and temporality. Rather His speech, may He be glorified and exalted, is an attribute necessarily pre-eternal and everlasting; it is whatever His knowledge is attached to, and its essence is veiled from the intellect, for there is nothing like it in all its aspects, neither intellectual, nor imaginal, nor estimative, nor existent, nor hypothetical, and that is like His exalted essence and the rest of His attributes.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and exposition. The author first explains that the innovators' denial of a speech that is not composed of letters or sounds is the root of their corrupt views. He then presents the Sunni refutation using internal speech (kalam nafsi) found within ourselves: we find in our souls a speech that conveys meanings and is distinct from knowledge, will, doubts, etc. This establishes that speech can exist without letters or sounds in the witnessed realm. Therefore, the innovators' restriction of speech to letters and sounds is false. The author then states the Sunni consensus: God's speech is an eternal attribute, not composed of letters or sounds, and is free from all temporal characteristics like priority, posteriority, part, whole, inflection, silence, etc., because these entail imperfection and temporality. God's speech is attached to His knowledge, and its true nature is beyond human comprehension, just like His essence and other attributes.

Key Terms
كلام
حرف
صوت
كلام نفسي
أهل السنة
قديم
صفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's speech attribute implies He speaks with letters and sounds like humans.
Correction: God's speech is an eternal attribute without letters, sounds, or temporality, as affirmed by Ahl al-Sunnah and proven by internal speech.

Checkpoint
What proof do Sunni scholars use to show that speech can exist without letters or sounds?
A) The existence of written text
B) The internal speech found within the soul
C) The testimony of prophets
D) The consensus of philosophers

Key Takeaway
God's speech is an eternal attribute, not composed of letters or sounds, and the existence of internal speech in humans refutes the denial of such speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you ever catch yourself imagining Allah's speech as a sound like a human voice? How does the truth that His speech is an eternal attribute, beyond letters and sounds, change the way you should approach the Quran? Will you make a conscious effort to think of His speech as a direct, timeless attribute rather than a physical event?
?
The passage says the essence of His speech is veiled from the intellect and nothing is like it. Does this humble you, or do you find yourself wanting to fully grasp it? How can you train yourself to accept the unknowable aspects of Allah's attributes without trying to reduce them to human terms? Write one practical step you will take this week to cultivate awe and submission before His transcendent speech.

Answer to Objection on Scope of Eternal Speech and Knowledge
Sanusi answers the objection that God's knowledge is more comprehensive than His speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi defends the comprehensive attachment of God's eternal speech to all objects of knowledge, and why the objection confuses a specific mode with the whole.

Core Idea
God's speech covers all objects of knowledge, but through multiple modes, not just command.

Sanusi addresses a subtle objection: if God commands something He knows will never happen, then knowledge seems to include something speech does not. His answer unveils a richer understanding of divine speech—it has multiple modes of relation to its objects, ensuring nothing falls outside its scope. Let's examine the objection and its precise rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the objector presents the problem: if God commands what He knows will not occur, then His command is attached to occurrence but knowledge to non-occurrence, making knowledge more comprehensive.
Notice the objector assumes 'speech' equals 'command'.
2
Identify the objector's reasoning
The objector concludes that knowledge has an object (non-occurrence) that speech does not. Spot the logical move: they equate speech with command alone.
3
Read Sanusi's reply
Sanusi responds that eternal speech has many attachments (command, prohibition, threat, information). Even if command is absent, other modes cover the same object. Detect the enumerated modes: prohibition, threat, informing.
The phrase 'بطريق النهي وبطريق الوعيد وبطريق الخبر' lists three additional modes.
4
Grasp the logical principle
The passage ends with a logical rule: negating the specific (command) does not negate the general (speech). Confirm that the objection fails because it only looked at one mode.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : قولُ أهل الحقِّ : إِنَّ الكلام الأزليَّ متعلق بجميع متعلقات العلم الأزلي قد يقدح فيهِ أنَّ أمر الله تعالى بعض المكلفين بما علم سبحانَهُ أنَّه لا يقعُ منهم .. يستلزمُ أَنَّ أَمرَهُ تعالى قد تعلَّق بوقوع ذلك المأمورِ ولم يتعلَّق بعدمِهِ، وعلمُهُ قد تعلَّق بعدم ذلك المأمور فقد تعلَّق علمُهُ سبحانَهُ بما لم يتعلَّق بهِ أمرُهُ الذي هو كلامه، فالعلم إذا أعم تعلُّقاً مِنَ الكلام. قلتُ : الكلامُ المذكورُ الأزلي لهُ تعلقات كثيرة لا نهاية لها وليس تعلقه منحصراً في التعلَّقِ الأمري، فإن كان لم يتعلق كلامه تبارك وتعالى بتزك المأمورِ في المثالِ بطريق الأمر .. فقد تعلَّق بهِ بطريق النهي وبطريق الوعيدِ وبطريقِ الخبر بعدم الوقوع، وهذه كلها الكلام الأزلي، فإذاً لا يمكن أن ينفرد العلم الأزلي بمتعلَّقِ تعلقات لا يكون متعلقاً للكلام الأزلي بوجه مِنْ وجوه التعلقاتِ فصح ما قالَهُ أئمَّةُ أهل السنَّةِ رضي الله تعالى عنهم : أنَّ الكلام الأزلي يتعلق بجميع ما تعلَّق بهِ العلم الأزلي، وبطل اعتراضُ مَنِ اعترض عليهم بالمثالِ السابق الذي انتفى بهِ بعضُ تعلقات الكلامِ الأزلي، ومِنَ المعلومِ : أَنَّهُ لا يلزمُ مِنْ نفي تعلَّقِ الأخص نفي تعلَّقِ الأعم.
If you say: The statement of the people of truth that eternal speech is attached to all objects of eternal knowledge may be flawed because God commanded some obligated persons what He knew would not occur from them... it implies that His command was attached to the occurrence of that commanded thing and not to its non-occurrence, while His knowledge was attached to its non-occurrence. So His knowledge is attached to something His command (which is His speech) was not attached to. Thus knowledge is more comprehensive in attachment than speech. I say: That eternal speech has many attachments without end, and its attachment is not restricted to the attachment of command. For if His speech, blessed and exalted, was not attached to that commanded thing in the example by way of command, it was attached to it by way of prohibition, by way of threat, and by way of informing of its non-occurrence. And all of these are eternal speech. So it is impossible for eternal knowledge to be alone with an attachment that is not attached to eternal speech in any way of attachments. Thus what the imams of Ahl al-Sunnah said is correct: that eternal speech is attached to all that eternal knowledge is attached to. And the objection of those who objected with the previous example, wherein some attachments of eternal speech were negated, is invalid. And it is known that the negation of the attachment of the more specific does not necessitate the negation of the attachment of the more general.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector argues: if God commands someone to do something that He knows will never happen, then His command is attached to the occurrence of that act, while His knowledge is attached to its non-occurrence. Thus knowledge covers something that command (speech) does not, making knowledge more comprehensive. The author responds: God's eternal speech has multiple modes of attachment—command, prohibition, threat, and information. For the same act, even if not commanded, it may be prohibited, threatened, or informed about. Therefore, the act is still an object of eternal speech in some mode. So knowledge cannot have an exclusive object. The conclusion is that the earlier claim stands: eternal speech attaches to all objects of eternal knowledge. The objection is invalid because negating one specific mode (command) does not negate the broader attachment (speech in general). This illustrates the logical principle that negating the specific does not negate the general.

علم أزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection confuses the command aspect of speech with the entirety of God's speech; God's speech includes multiple modalities covering all objects of knowledge.
Correction: Even when command does not apply, other modalities of speech (prohibition, threat, information) cover the same object, so knowledge has no exclusive object.

Checkpoint

A) Through the command itself, which is sufficient
B) Through other modes like prohibition, threat, or information
C) Such acts are not covered by speech at all
D) Through a special mode known only to God

Key Takeaway
God's eternal speech attaches to all objects of knowledge through multiple modalities, so no object is outside its scope.

?

Refuting the Objection: Knowledge Not More Comprehensive Than Speech
Sanusi presents and refutes an objection that knowledge relates to more things than eternal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi refutes the claim that divine knowledge is more comprehensive than divine speech by showing that eternal speech relates to all objects of knowledge through multiple modes.

Core Idea
Eternal speech has multiple modes—command, prohibition, threat, information—so it covers all objects of knowledge.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a common objection to the doctrine that eternal speech relates to all objects of eternal knowledge. The objector points to cases where Allah commands something He knows will not happen. Sanusi's response broadens our understanding of divine speech, showing it is not limited to commands alone.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection carefully: because command does not relate to non-occurrence, knowledge seems to cover more. Identify the example given.
The objector uses the case of a command that is not fulfilled to claim that knowledge has a relation where speech does not.
2
Explore Sanusi's response
Notice that Sanusi lists multiple modes of eternal speech: command, prohibition, threat, and information. See how each mode relates to the example.
Even if command does not cover non-occurrence, prohibition or information does.
3
Follow the conclusion
Understand how the refutation affirms the original position of Ahl al-Sunnah: eternal speech relates to all that eternal knowledge relates to.
The conclusion also points out that negating a specific mode does not negate the general relation.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this refutation is important for understanding divine attributes and the unity of God's speech.
It preserves the comprehensiveness of divine speech and prevents a false dichotomy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة كون العلم أعم تعلقاً من الكلام بجميع تعلقاته فإن قلت : قول أهل الحق : إن الكلام الأزلي متعلق بجميع متعلقات العلم الأزلي قد يقدح فيه أن أمر الله تعالى بعض المكلفين بما علم سبحانه أنه لا يقع منهم يستلزم أن أمره تعالى قد تعلق بوقوع ذلك المأمور ولم يتعلق بعدمه ، وعلمه قد تعلق بعدم ذلك المأمور فقد تعلق علمه سبحانه بما لم يتعلق به أمره الذي هو كلامه ، فالعلم إذا أعم تعلقاً من الكلام . قلت : الكلام المذكور الأزلي له تعلقات كثيرة لا نهاية لها وليس تعلقه منحصراً في التعلق الأمري ، فإن كان لم يتعلق كلامه تبارك وتعالى بترك المأمور في المثال بطريق الأمر فقد تعلق به بطريق النهي وبطريق الوعيد وبطريق الخبر بعدم الوقوع ، وهذه كلها الكلام الأزلي ، فإذاً لا يمكن أن ينفرد العلم الأزلي بمتعلق من تعلقات لا يكون متعلقاً للكلام الأزلي بوجه من وجوه التعلقات فصح ما قاله أئمة أهل السنة رضي الله تعالى عنهم : أن الكلام الأزلي يتعلق بجميع ما تعلق به العلم الأزلي ، وبطل اعتراض من اعترض عليهم بالمثال السابق الذي انتفى به بعض تعلقات الكلام الأزلي ، ومن المعلوم : أنه لا يلزم من نفي تعلق الأخص نفي تعلق الأعم.
The doubt that knowledge is more comprehensive in relation than speech with all its relations. If you say: The statement of the people of truth that eternal speech relates to all objects of eternal knowledge may be undermined by the fact that when Allah Almighty commands some morally responsible individuals to do something that He knows will not happen from them, this entails that His command related to the occurrence of that commanded thing and did not relate to its non-occurrence, while His knowledge related to the non-occurrence of that commanded thing. Thus His knowledge related to what His command—which is His speech—did not relate to. So knowledge is then more comprehensive in relation than speech. I say: The mentioned eternal speech has many relations without end, and its relation is not restricted to the mode of command. Even if His speech—blessed and exalted is He—did not relate to the abandonment of the commanded thing in the example by way of command, it related to it by way of prohibition, by way of threat, and by way of information of non-occurrence. All of these are eternal speech. Therefore it is impossible for eternal knowledge to be unique in having an object among objects of relations that is not an object of eternal speech in some mode of relation. So what the imams of the Ahl al-Sunnah—may Allah be pleased with them—said is correct: that eternal speech relates to all that eternal knowledge relates to. And the objection of whoever objected to them with the previous example, by which some relations of eternal speech were negated, is invalid. And it is known that negating the relation of the more specific does not entail negating the relation of the more general.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (shubha wa jawab) concerning the relationship between divine knowledge and divine speech. The objector argues that the statement of Ahl al-Haqq (that eternal speech relates to all objects of eternal knowledge) is undermined by the case where Allah commands something He knows will not occur. The command relates to occurrence, but knowledge relates to non-occurrence, so knowledge appears to have an object (the non-occurrence) that speech does not. The answer refutes this by noting that eternal speech has multiple modes: command, prohibition, threat, and information. In the example, although the command does not relate to the non-occurrence, eternal speech does relate to it through prohibition, threat, or information. Therefore, no object of knowledge escapes some relation of speech. The conclusion affirms the original position and points out that negating the specific relation (command) does not negate the more general relation (speech in all its modes).

Correction: Divine speech includes prohibition, threat, and information, so all objects of knowledge are covered by some mode of speech.

Key Takeaway
Eternal speech, through its multiple modes, encompasses all objects of eternal knowledge, so knowledge is not more comprehensive than speech.

The Quran's Four Modes of Existence and the Createdness of Recitation
Sanusi explains the four modes of existence and the distinction between created acts and eternal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran exists in four modes (external, mental, spoken, written) and why recitation is created while the recited is eternal.

Core Idea
The Quran is eternal speech, not contained in physical things, but indicated by them.

Sanusi explains that when the Salaf said the Quran is preserved in hearts, recited on tongues, and written in mushafs, they meant it literally, but not by indwelling. He clarifies the distinction through the four modes of existence, showing how the created acts indicate the eternal speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get a feel for Sanusi's argument.
2
Identify the four modes of existence
List the four modes: existence in external entities, in minds, on the tongue, and by writing. Note how Sanusi defines each.
3
Understand the distinction between created and eternal
Notice that Sanusi distinguishes tilawa (recitation) from matluw (the recited), etc. Understand why the first is created and the second eternal.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this distinction preserves Allah's transcendence while affirming the Quran's presence in worship through indication.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرفت مذهب أهل الحق في كلام الله تعالى عرفت أن إطلاق السلف رضي الله تعالى عنهم على كلام الله تعالى أنه محفوظ في الصدور ، مقروء بالألسنة ، مكتوب في المصاحف هو بطريق الحقيقة ، لا بطريق المجاز ، وليس يعنون بذلك حلول كلام الله تعالى القديم في هذه الأجرام تعالى الله عن ذلك ، وإنما يريدون أن كلامه عز وجل مذكور مدلول عليه : بتلاوة اللسان ، وكلام الجنان ، وكتابة البنان ، فهو موجود فيها فهماً وعلماً لا حلولاً ؛ لأن الشيء له وجودات أربع : وجود في الأعيان ، ووجود في الأذهان ، ووجود في اللسان ، ووجود بالبنان ؛ أي : بالكتابة بالأصابع . فالوجود الأول هو الوجود الذاتي الحقيقي ، وسائر الوجودات إنما هي باعتبار الدلالة والفهم ، وبهذا تعرف أن التلاوة غير المتلو ، والقراءة غير المقروء ، والكتابة غير المكتوب ؛ لأن الأول من كل قسم من هذه الأقسام حادث ، والثاني منها قديم لا نهاية له ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق.
And when you know the doctrine of the people of truth concerning the speech of Allah Almighty, you know that the Salaf—may Allah be pleased with them—applying the terms 'preserved in breasts, recited on tongues, written in mushafs' to the speech of Allah Almighty is by way of truth (haqiqa), not by way of metaphor (majaz). And they do not mean by that the indwelling (hulul) of the eternal speech of Allah Almighty in these bodies—Allah is exalted above that. Rather they mean that His speech—mighty and majestic is He—is remembered and indicated by the recitation of the tongue, the speech of the heart (i.e., mental recollection), and the writing of the fingers. So it exists in them by understanding and knowledge, not by indwelling. Because a thing has four modes of existence: existence in external entities (a'yan), existence in minds (adhhan), existence on the tongue (lisan), and existence by the fingers (banan)—i.e., by writing with fingers. So the first existence is the essential, real existence, and the rest of the existences are only by way of indication and understanding. And by this you know that recitation (tilawa) is other than the recited (matluw), reading (qira'a) other than the read (maqru'), and writing (kitaba) other than the written (maktub). Because the first of each of these categories is contingent (hadith), and the second of them is eternal (qadim) without end. And with Allah Almighty is success.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal clarification about the nature of the Quran and its relationship to the physical forms in which it is encountered. Sanusi first states that when one understands the Ahl al-Haqq position on divine speech, one realizes that the statements of the Salaf (the early Muslims) that the Quran is 'preserved in hearts, recited on tongues, written in mushafs' are literal (haqiqa) truth, not metaphorical. They do not mean that the eternal speech of Allah actually dwells in these created objects. Rather, they mean that the eternal speech is remembered and indicated by recitation, mental recall, and writing. Sanusi then introduces the concept of four modes of existence for any thing: external reality (a'yan), mental conception (adhhan), spoken expression (lisan), and written notation (banan). The first is the real, self-subsistent existence; the other three are merely indicative (dalala) and conceptual (fahm). Based on this, he concludes that recitation (tilawa) is distinct from the recited (matluw), reading (qira'a) distinct from the read (maqru'), and writing (kitaba) distinct from the written (maktub). The former are created (hadith) acts of humans; the latter are the eternal (qadim) divine speech itself. This preserves divine transcendence while affirming the genuine presence of the Quran in these forms by way of indication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that when the Salaf said the Quran is in hearts and mushafs, they meant the eternal speech literally dwells in those physical things.
Correction: Sanusi explains that the Salaf meant the Quran is indicated and understood through these forms, not that it dwells in them. The eternal speech does not inhabit created objects.

Checkpoint

B) Recitation is eternal, the recited is created
C) Recitation is created, the recited is eternal
D) Both are eternal

Key Takeaway
Recitation, reading, and writing are created acts that indicate the eternal Quran; they are not the divine speech itself.

Divine Limits and the Two Servants
Defines divine limits and contrasts faithful vs treacherous servants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of divine limits (hudud) and the contrasting outcomes of the faithful and treacherous servants based on divine grace and justice.

Core Idea
Allah sets clear limits; the trustworthy obey, the treacherous transgress.

Sanusi introduces the foundational idea that Allah has set boundaries for human actions. These boundaries are not arbitrary but define right and wrong. The passage then presents a stark contrast: those who uphold these limits are called trustworthy, while those who violate them are treacherous. This sets the stage for understanding moral responsibility in light of divine will.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once carefully. Notice the key terms for the five categories of action and the two contrasting descriptions of servants.
Pay attention to the parallel structure: 'fa man... kāna amīnan, wa man... kāna khā'inan'.
2
Understand the five categories
Identify the five categories of actions mentioned: wājib, mandūb, mubāḥ, ḥarām, makrūh. Understand that the first three are within the limits, the last two are transgressions.
These categories form the basis of Islamic legal theory.
3
Contrast the two servants
Focus on the contrast between the 'amīn' (trustworthy) and 'khā'in' (treacherous). Notice that trustworthiness is linked to divine success (tawfīq) and protection, while treachery is linked to divine justice (ʿadl) and being driven.
This highlights the interplay of divine grace and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا شكّ أنَّ مولانا جل وعزّ قد حد لعبيده المكلفين حدوداً ، وأمرهم وأوصاهم ألا يتعدوا حدودَهُ ؛ فحدَّ لنا سبحانه الواجب والمندوب والمباحَ ، ونهانا أنَّ نتعداها إلى فعل المحرَّم أوِ المكروه مِنَ الأفعالِ ، وأوصانا جلَّ وعلا بتقواه ، وبالفِرارِ مِنْ غضبه وعقابه إلى حَرَمِ طاعتِهِ وما جعلَه جلَّ وعلا بفضله أمارة على رضاه ونعيمِهِ وثوابه . فمَنْ وفَقَهُ الله للمحافظة على وصيَّتِهِ ، وحفظَهُ جَلَّ وعلا بفضلِهِ مِنْ مخالفتِهِ . . كانَ أميناً ، ومَنْ قهرَهُ تبارك وتعالى بعدلِهِ ، وطردَهُ إلى ولوج أبواب غضبِهِ ونِقَمِهِ ، وسدَّ عنه أبواب عصمتِهِ وفضله وكرمه . . كان خائناً
There is no doubt that our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, has set limits for His responsible servants, and commanded them and charged them not to transgress His limits. So He, glorified, defined for us the obligatory, the recommended, and the permissible, and forbade us from transgressing them to the doing of the prohibited or the disliked among actions. And He, exalted, charged us with His piety, and with fleeing from His anger and punishment to the sanctuary of His obedience and what He, exalted, made by His grace a sign of His pleasure, bliss, and reward. So whoever Allah grants success to preserve His charge and protects him by His grace from opposing Him, he is trustworthy. And whoever the Blessed and Exalted overcomes by His justice and drives him to enter the doors of His anger and punishments, and blocks from him the doors of His protection, grace, and generosity, he is treacherous.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of divine limits (hudud) and the consequences of observing or transgressing them. The author begins by affirming that Allah has set boundaries for morally responsible servants (mukallafun). These boundaries are not arbitrary; they are established through divine command and charge (wasiyya). The limits specifically delineate actions into categories: obligatory (wajib), recommended (mandub), and permissible (mubah). The prohibition is against exceeding these by performing prohibited (haram) or disliked (makruh) actions. The author then presents a contrast: the one whom Allah grants success (tawfiq) to adhere to His charge becomes 'trustworthy' (amin), while the one whom Allah overcomes by His justice and is driven to disobedience becomes 'treacherous' (kha'in). This distinction underscores the role of divine grace and justice in human moral outcomes.

Key Terms
حدود
المكلفون
الواجب
المندوب
المباح
المحرم
المكروه
أمين
خائن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Allah arbitrarily predestines some to be trustworthy and others treacherous without reason.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that trustworthiness comes through Allah's grace and success (tawfīq), while treachery results from Allah's justice (ʿadl) in response to human actions. Both are just and wise.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what type of person is called 'amīn' (trustworthy)?
A) One who never commits any sin
B) One whom Allah grants success to preserve His charge and protects from opposing Him
C) One who performs all obligatory acts perfectly
D) One who memorizes the divine limits

Key Takeaway
Divine limits define moral categories, and our response to them—by Allah's grace or justice—determines whether we are trustworthy or treacherous.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that Allah has defined limits for you: obligatory, recommended, permissible, prohibited, disliked. Where in your daily life are you most tempted to treat the disliked or prohibited as 'just a small thing'? What will you change starting today?
?
The passage says the trustworthy are those whom Allah grants success to preserve His charge. Do you truly believe that your obedience depends on Allah's grace, or do you secretly rely on your own strength? How does this affect your confidence in standing before Him?
?
Consider the two outcomes: trustworthiness or treachery. Which one describes your reaction when you sin—do you run back to the sanctuary of His obedience, or do you make excuses and justify the transgression? What would it mean for you to be 'trustworthy' today?
